Example 5: Complete Integration with Complex Financial Calculations

Comprehensive test with multiple models and complex floating-point calculations.

# tests/test_complete_financial_integration.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost
from decimal import Decimal

def test_complete_financial_calculations():
    """Complete integration test with complex financial calculations"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("COMPLETE FINANCIAL INTEGRATION WITH pytest.approx()")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Phase 1: Setup Skills
    print("Phase 1: Creating Skills")
    print("-" * 70)
    skills = [
        Skills.objects.create(name='Python'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='Django'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='React'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='AWS'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='Docker'),
    ]
    print(f"✓ Created {len(skills)} skills\n")
    
    # Phase 2: Setup Authors
    print("Phase 2: Creating Authors with Budget Allocation")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    total_budget = 1000000.0  # $1M total hiring budget
    author_allocations = [0.25, 0.30, 0.20, 0.15, 0.10]  # Percentages
    
    authors = []
    for i, allocation in enumerate(author_allocations):
        user = User.objects.create_user(
            username=f'mgr{i+1}',
            password='test123'
        )
        author = Author.objects.create(
            user=user,
            company='Global Tech Corp',
            designation=f'Hiring Manager {i+1}'
        )
        author.budget = total_budget * allocation
        authors.append(author)
        
        print(f"  {author.user.username}: ${author.budget:,.2f} ({allocation*100}%)")
    
    # Verify budget allocations
    total_allocated = sum(a.budget for a in authors)
    print(f"\n  Total allocated: ${total_allocated:,.2f}")
    assert total_allocated == pytest.approx(total_budget, rel=1e-9)
    print(f"  ✓ Budget allocation verified\n")
    
    # Phase 3: Create locations
    print("Phase 3: Creating Locations")
    print("-" * 70)
    locations = [
        Location.objects.create(street='1 Tech St', city='SF', state='CA', country='USA', zip='94105'),
        Location.objects.create(street='2 Tech St', city='NY', state='NY', country='USA', zip='10001'),
        Location.objects.create(street='3 Tech St', city='Austin', state='TX', country='USA', zip='78701'),
    ]
    print(f"✓ Created {len(locations)} locations\n")
    
    # Phase 4: Create jobs with salary calculations
    print("Phase 4: Creating Jobs with Budget Tracking")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    jobs_per_author = [2, 3, 2, 1, 2]  # 10 total jobs
    
    all_jobs = []
    for author, num_jobs in zip(authors, jobs_per_author):
        # Distribute author's budget evenly across their jobs
        salary_per_job = author.budget / num_jobs
        
        author_total = 0
        for j in range(num_jobs):
            location = locations[j % len(locations)]
            
            job = JobPost.objects.create(
                title=f'Position by {author.user.username} #{j+1}',
                description='Test position',
                expiry=timezone.now().date(),
                salary=salary_per_job,
                type='Full Time',
                location=location,
                author=author
            )
            
            # Add skills
            job.skills.set(skills[:3])
            all_jobs.append(job)
            author_total += salary_per_job
        
        print(f"  {author.user.username}: {num_jobs} jobs")
        print(f"    Budget: ${author.budget:,.2f}")
        print(f"    Used: ${author_total:,.2f}")
        
        # Verify budget usage
        assert author_total == pytest.approx(author.budget, rel=1e-9)
        print(f"    ✓ Budget fully allocated\n")
    
    # Phase 5: Financial Analysis
    print("Phase 5: Financial Analysis")
    print("=" * 70)
    
    # Total salary budget
    total_salaries = sum(job.salary for job in all_jobs)
    print(f"\nTotal Salaries: ${total_salaries:,.2f}")
    assert total_salaries == pytest.approx(total_budget, rel=1e-9)
    print(f"✓ Total matches budget")
    
    # Average salary
    average_salary = total_salaries / len(all_jobs)
    expected_avg = total_budget / len(all_jobs)
    print(f"\nAverage Salary: ${average_salary:,.2f}")
    print(f"Expected: ${expected_avg:,.2f}")
    assert average_salary == pytest.approx(expected_avg, rel=1e-9)
    print(f"✓ Average verified")
    
    # Calculate 15% benefits cost
    benefits_rate = 0.15
    total_benefits = total_salaries * benefits_rate
    total_cost = total_salaries + total_benefits
    
    print(f"\nCost Analysis:")
    print(f"  Base salaries: ${total_salaries:,.2f}")
    print(f"  Benefits (15%): ${total_benefits:,.2f}")
    print(f"  Total cost: ${total_cost:,.2f}")
    
    expected_total_cost = total_budget * 1.15
    assert total_cost == pytest.approx(expected_total_cost, rel=1e-9)
    print(f"  ✓ Total cost verified: ${expected_total_cost:,.2f}")
    
    # Cost per skill
    total_skill_assignments = sum(job.skills.count() for job in all_jobs)
    cost_per_skill = total_cost / total_skill_assignments
    
    print(f"\nSkill Economics:")
    print(f"  Total skill assignments: {total_skill_assignments}")
    print(f"  Cost per skill: ${cost_per_skill:,.2f}")
    
    expected_cost_per_skill = (total_budget * 1.15) / total_skill_assignments
    assert cost_per_skill == pytest.approx(expected_cost_per_skill, rel=1e-9)
    print(f"  ✓ Cost per skill verified")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("✓ Complete financial integration verified")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

pytest.fail()

Official Docs: pytest.fail() Reference

Explicitly fail a test with a given message.

Full Description

The pytest.fail() function is used to explicitly fail the currently executing test with a given error message. Unlike assertions that fail when a condition is false, pytest.fail() unconditionally stops test execution and marks the test as failed. This is particularly useful when you need to fail a test based on complex logic, custom validation rules, or exceptional conditions that don't fit into simple assert statements.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.fail() is valuable for implementing custom validation logic for JobPost data integrity, Author permission checks, or complex business rules that span multiple models. For example, when validating that a JobPost has all required related objects, checking Author authorization levels, or enforcing Skills requirements, you can use pytest.fail() to provide clear, contextual error messages that explain exactly why the test failed.

Syntax

# Basic usage
pytest.fail(msg)

# With optional pytrace parameter
pytest.fail(msg, pytrace=True)

# Inside conditional logic
if some_invalid_condition:
    pytest.fail("Validation failed: condition not met")

# With formatted message
pytest.fail(f"Expected {expected}, but got {actual}")

# In exception handler
try:
    risky_operation()
except Exception as e:
    pytest.fail(f"Operation failed: {str(e)}")

Parameters Description

  • msg (str): The failure message that will be displayed in the test output. This should clearly explain why the test failed.
  • pytrace (bool, optional): If False (default), suppresses the Python traceback and only shows the failure message. If True, includes the full traceback showing where pytest.fail() was called.

Return Value

  • Returns: Never returns - raises Failed exception immediately
  • Effect: Stops test execution and marks test as failed
  • Exception type: Raises pytest.fail.Exception (Failed)
  • Test result: Test is marked as FAILED with the provided message

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: JobPost Data Validation with pytest.fail()

Using pytest.fail() to validate JobPost data integrity and business rules.

# tests/test_jobpost_validation_with_fail.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost
from datetime import timedelta

def test_jobpost_complete_validation():
    """Validate JobPost has all required data using pytest.fail()"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("JOBPOST VALIDATION WITH pytest.fail()")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Setup
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='validator', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Validation Corp',
        designation='Senior Validator'
    )
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='123 Valid St',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    skills = [
        Skills.objects.create(name='Python'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='Django'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='Testing'),
    ]
    
    # Create JobPost
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Senior Developer',
        description='Python developer needed',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timedelta(days=30),
        salary=120000,
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    job.skills.set(skills)
    
    print(f"Created JobPost: {job.title}")
    print(f"  Author: {job.author.company}")
    print(f"  Location: {job.location.city}")
    print(f"  Skills: {job.skills.count()}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${job.salary:,}\n")
    
    # Validation Rules
    print("Running validation checks:")
    
    # Check 1: Must have title
    if not job.title or len(job.title) < 5:
        pytest.fail(f"JobPost title too short: '{job.title}' (minimum 5 characters)")
    print("  ✓ Title validation passed")
    
    # Check 2: Must have description
    if not job.description or len(job.description) < 10:
        pytest.fail(f"JobPost description too short: {len(job.description)} chars (minimum 10)")
    print("  ✓ Description validation passed")
    
    # Check 3: Must have author
    if not job.author:
        pytest.fail("JobPost must have an author assigned")
    print("  ✓ Author validation passed")
    
    # Check 4: Must have location
    if not job.location:
        pytest.fail("JobPost must have a location assigned")
    print("  ✓ Location validation passed")
    
    # Check 5: Must have at least 2 skills
    if job.skills.count() < 2:
        pytest.fail(f"JobPost must have at least 2 skills, found {job.skills.count()}")
    print("  ✓ Skills count validation passed")
    
    # Check 6: Salary range validation
    if job.salary < 50000 or job.salary > 500000:
        pytest.fail(f"Salary ${job.salary:,} outside valid range ($50,000 - $500,000)")
    print("  ✓ Salary range validation passed")
    
    # Check 7: Expiry date validation
    if job.expiry < timezone.now().date():
        pytest.fail(f"JobPost expiry date {job.expiry} is in the past")
    print("  ✓ Expiry date validation passed")
    
    # Check 8: Author must have company
    if not job.author.company:
        pytest.fail("Author must have a company name")
    print("  ✓ Author company validation passed")
    
    # All checks passed
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("✓ ALL VALIDATION CHECKS PASSED")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Verify in database
    retrieved_job = JobPost.objects.get(id=job.id)
    assert retrieved_job.title == job.title
    print(f"JobPost successfully validated and stored in database")

Example 2: User Permissions Validation with pytest.fail()

Testing User and Author authorization with explicit fail conditions.

# tests/test_user_permissions_with_fail.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author

def test_user_permissions_validation():
    """Validate user permissions and author access using pytest.fail()"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("USER PERMISSIONS VALIDATION WITH pytest.fail()")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create users with different permission levels
    users_data = [
        {'username': 'admin_user', 'is_staff': True, 'is_superuser': True, 'role': 'Admin'},
        {'username': 'staff_user', 'is_staff': True, 'is_superuser': False, 'role': 'Staff'},
        {'username': 'regular_user', 'is_staff': False, 'is_superuser': False, 'role': 'Regular'},
        {'username': 'author_user', 'is_staff': False, 'is_superuser': False, 'role': 'Author'},
        {'username': 'inactive_user', 'is_staff': False, 'is_superuser': False, 'role': 'Inactive'},
    ]
    
    users = []
    print("Creating users:")
    for user_data in users_data:
        user = User.objects.create_user(
            username=user_data['username'],
            email=f"{user_data['username']}@example.com",
            password='test123',
            is_staff=user_data['is_staff'],
            is_superuser=user_data['is_superuser']
        )
        
        # Mark last user as inactive
        if user_data['username'] == 'inactive_user':
            user.is_active = False
            user.save()
        
        users.append(user)
        print(f"  {user.username}: {user_data['role']} "
              f"(staff={user.is_staff}, super={user.is_superuser}, active={user.is_active})")
    
    # Create authors for users who can post jobs
    print(f"\nCreating authors:")
    authors = []
    authorized_users = ['admin_user', 'staff_user', 'author_user']
    
    for user in users:
        if user.username in authorized_users:
            author = Author.objects.create(
                user=user,
                company=f"{user.username.replace('_', ' ').title()} Company",
                designation='Job Poster'
            )
            authors.append(author)
            print(f"  ✓ {user.username} → Author created")
        else:
            print(f"  ✗ {user.username} → No author (not authorized)")
    
    # Permission validation
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("PERMISSION VALIDATION")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    for user in users:
        print(f"Validating: {user.username}")
        
        # Rule 1: User must be active
        if not user.is_active:
            pytest.fail(f"User '{user.username}' is inactive and cannot perform actions")
        print(f"  ✓ Active status validated")
        
        # Rule 2: Check if user can create job posts
        has_author = Author.objects.filter(user=user).exists()
        can_post_jobs = user.is_staff or has_author
        
        if user.username in ['admin_user', 'staff_user', 'author_user']:
            if not can_post_jobs:
                pytest.fail(f"User '{user.username}' should be able to post jobs but cannot")
            print(f"  ✓ Job posting permission validated")
        
        # Rule 3: Regular users cannot be superusers without staff status
        if user.is_superuser and not user.is_staff:
            pytest.fail(f"User '{user.username}' is superuser but not staff (invalid state)")
        print(f"  ✓ Permission consistency validated\n")
    
    # Summary
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print("VALIDATION SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"Total users: {User.objects.filter(is_active=True).count()} active")
    print(f"Total authors: {Author.objects.count()}")
    print(f"Staff members: {User.objects.filter(is_staff=True).count()}")
    print(f"Superusers: {User.objects.filter(is_superuser=True).count()}")
    print(f"\n✓ All active users passed permission validation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 3: Skills Relationship Validation

Validating Skills associations and relationships with pytest.fail().

# tests/test_skills_relationship_validation.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

def test_skills_relationship_validation():
    """Validate Skills relationships and constraints with pytest.fail()"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("SKILLS RELATIONSHIP VALIDATION WITH pytest.fail()")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create skills
    skills_data = [
        'Python', 'Django', 'JavaScript', 'React', 'PostgreSQL',
        'Docker', 'AWS', 'Git', 'REST API', 'Testing'
    ]
    
    skills = []
    print("Creating skills:")
    for skill_name in skills_data:
        skill = Skills.objects.create(name=skill_name)
        skills.append(skill)
        print(f"  ✓ {skill.name}")
    
    # Setup for job posts
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='skill_tester', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(user=user, company='Skills Co', designation='Tech Lead')
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1 Skills Ave', city='Tech City', state='CA', country='USA', zip='94105'
    )
    
    # Create job posts with varying skill requirements
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("Creating job posts with skill requirements:")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    jobs_config = [
        {'title': 'Backend Developer', 'required_skills': 5, 'skill_indices': [0, 1, 4, 5, 6]},
        {'title': 'Frontend Developer', 'required_skills': 4, 'skill_indices': [2, 3, 7, 9]},
        {'title': 'Full Stack Developer', 'required_skills': 7, 'skill_indices': [0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 7, 8]},
        {'title': 'DevOps Engineer', 'required_skills': 4, 'skill_indices': [5, 6, 7, 4]},
        {'title': 'QA Engineer', 'required_skills': 3, 'skill_indices': [0, 7, 9]},
    ]
    
    jobs = []
    for config in jobs_config:
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=config['title'],
            description=f"Position requiring {config['required_skills']} skills",
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=100000,
            type='Full Time',
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        
        # Add skills
        job_skills = [skills[i] for i in config['skill_indices']]
        job.skills.set(job_skills)
        jobs.append(job)
        
        print(f"{config['title']}:")
        print(f"  Required: {config['required_skills']} skills")
        print(f"  Assigned: {job.skills.count()} skills")
        print(f"  Skills: {', '.join(s.name for s in job.skills.all()[:3])}...")
        
        # Validation: Must have exact number of required skills
        if job.skills.count() != config['required_skills']:
            pytest.fail(
                f"Job '{job.title}' requires {config['required_skills']} skills "
                f"but has {job.skills.count()}"
            )
        print(f"  ✓ Skill count validated\n")
    
    # Cross-validation checks
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print("CROSS-VALIDATION CHECKS")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    for skill in skills:
        job_count = skill.jobpost_set.count()
        print(f"{skill.name}:")
        print(f"  Used in {job_count} job(s)")
        
        # Validation: Popular skills should be used in multiple jobs
        if skill.name in ['Python', 'Django', 'Git']:
            if job_count < 2:
                pytest.fail(
                    f"Popular skill '{skill.name}' should be used in at least 2 jobs, "
                    f"found in {job_count}"
                )
            print(f"  ✓ Popular skill usage validated")
        
        # Validation: No skill should be unused
        if job_count == 0:
            pytest.fail(f"Skill '{skill.name}' is not used in any job post")
        print(f"  ✓ Skill is actively used\n")
    
    # Final statistics
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print("FINAL STATISTICS")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"Total skills: {Skills.objects.count()}")
    print(f"Total jobs: {JobPost.objects.count()}")
    print(f"Average skills per job: {sum(j.skills.count() for j in jobs) / len(jobs):.1f}")
    
    # Calculate skill popularity
    skill_usage = [(s, s.jobpost_set.count()) for s in skills]
    skill_usage.sort(key=lambda x: x[1], reverse=True)
    
    print(f"\nMost popular skills:")
    for skill, count in skill_usage[:3]:
        print(f"  {skill.name}: {count} jobs")
    
    print(f"\n✓ All skill relationship validations passed")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 4: Location Data Integrity Validation

Validating Location data completeness and format with pytest.fail().

# tests/test_location_data_integrity.py
import pytest
import re
from jobpost.models import Location

def test_location_data_integrity():
    """Validate Location data integrity and format with pytest.fail()"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("LOCATION DATA INTEGRITY VALIDATION WITH pytest.fail()")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Location data to validate
    locations_data = [
        {
            'street': '123 Main Street',
            'city': 'San Francisco',
            'state': 'CA',
            'country': 'USA',
            'zip': '94105'
        },
        {
            'street': '456 Broadway',
            'city': 'New York',
            'state': 'NY',
            'country': 'USA',
            'zip': '10007'
        },
        {
            'street': '789 Congress Avenue',
            'city': 'Austin',
            'state': 'TX',
            'country': 'USA',
            'zip': '78701'
        },
        {
            'street': '321 Pike Place',
            'city': 'Seattle',
            'state': 'WA',
            'country': 'USA',
            'zip': '98101'
        },
        {
            'street': '654 Boylston Street',
            'city': 'Boston',
            'state': 'MA',
            'country': 'USA',
            'zip': '02116'
        },
    ]
    
    # Validation patterns
    zip_pattern = re.compile(r'^\d{5}$')
    state_codes = ['AL', 'AK', 'AZ', 'AR', 'CA', 'CO', 'CT', 'DE', 'FL', 'GA', 
                   'HI', 'ID', 'IL', 'IN', 'IA', 'KS', 'KY', 'LA', 'ME', 'MD',
                   'MA', 'MI', 'MN', 'MS', 'MO', 'MT', 'NE', 'NV', 'NH', 'NJ',
                   'NM', 'NY', 'NC', 'ND', 'OH', 'OK', 'OR', 'PA', 'RI', 'SC',
                   'SD', 'TN', 'TX', 'UT', 'VT', 'VA', 'WA', 'WV', 'WI', 'WY']
    
    created_locations = []
    
    print("Validating and creating locations:\n")
    for i, loc_data in enumerate(locations_data, 1):
        print(f"Location {i}: {loc_data['city']}, {loc_data['state']}")
        
        # Validation 1: All fields must be present
        for field in ['street', 'city', 'state', 'country', 'zip']:
            if not loc_data.get(field):
                pytest.fail(f"Location {i} missing required field: {field}")
        print(f"  ✓ All required fields present")
        
        # Validation 2: Street must be meaningful
        if len(loc_data['street']) < 5:
            pytest.fail(
                f"Location {i} street address too short: '{loc_data['street']}' "
                f"(minimum 5 characters)"
            )
        print(f"  ✓ Street address validated")
        
        # Validation 3: City must be alphabetic
        if not loc_data['city'].replace(' ', '').isalpha():
            pytest.fail(f"Location {i} city name contains invalid characters: '{loc_data['city']}'")
        print(f"  ✓ City name validated")
        
        # Validation 4: State must be valid US state code
        if loc_data['state'] not in state_codes:
            pytest.fail(
                f"Location {i} invalid state code: '{loc_data['state']}' "
                f"(must be valid US state abbreviation)"
            )
        print(f"  ✓ State code validated")
        
        # Validation 5: ZIP code must be 5 digits
        if not zip_pattern.match(loc_data['zip']):
            pytest.fail(
                f"Location {i} invalid ZIP code: '{loc_data['zip']}' "
                f"(must be 5 digits)"
            )
        print(f"  ✓ ZIP code format validated")
        
        # Validation 6: Country must be USA for this test
        if loc_data['country'] != 'USA':
            pytest.fail(f"Location {i} country must be USA, got: '{loc_data['country']}'")
        print(f"  ✓ Country validated")
        
        # Create location
        location = Location.objects.create(**loc_data)
        created_locations.append(location)
        print(f"  ✓ Location created successfully\n")
    
    # Cross-location validations
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print("CROSS-LOCATION VALIDATIONS")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Check for duplicate cities
    cities = [loc.city for loc in created_locations]
    if len(cities) != len(set(cities)):
        duplicates = [city for city in cities if cities.count(city) > 1]
        pytest.fail(f"Duplicate cities found: {', '.join(set(duplicates))}")
    print("✓ No duplicate cities")
    
    # Check for duplicate ZIP codes
    zips = [loc.zip for loc in created_locations]
    if len(zips) != len(set(zips)):
        duplicates = [zip_code for zip_code in zips if zips.count(zip_code) > 1]
        pytest.fail(f"Duplicate ZIP codes found: {', '.join(set(duplicates))}")
    print("✓ No duplicate ZIP codes")
    
    # Verify geographic diversity (at least 3 different states)
    unique_states = set(loc.state for loc in created_locations)
    if len(unique_states) < 3:
        pytest.fail(
            f"Insufficient geographic diversity: only {len(unique_states)} states "
            f"(minimum 3 required)"
        )
    print(f"✓ Geographic diversity validated ({len(unique_states)} states)")
    
    # Final summary
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("VALIDATION SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"Total locations created: {Location.objects.count()}")
    print(f"States covered: {', '.join(sorted(unique_states))}")
    print(f"All ZIP codes: {', '.join(sorted(zips))}")
    print(f"\n✓ All location data integrity checks passed")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 5: Complete Multi-Model Integration Validation

Comprehensive validation across all models using pytest.fail().

# tests/test_complete_integration_validation.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost
from datetime import timedelta

def test_complete_integration_validation():
    """Complete integration test with comprehensive validation"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("COMPLETE INTEGRATION VALIDATION WITH pytest.fail()")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Phase 1: Skills
    print("Phase 1: Skills Creation and Validation")
    print("-" * 70)
    required_skills = ['Python', 'Django', 'JavaScript', 'React', 'PostgreSQL']
    skills = []
    
    for skill_name in required_skills:
        skill = Skills.objects.create(name=skill_name)
        skills.append(skill)
        
        # Validate skill name
        if not skill.name or len(skill.name) < 2:
            pytest.fail(f"Invalid skill name: '{skill.name}'")
        print(f"  ✓ {skill.name}")
    
    if Skills.objects.count() != len(required_skills):
        pytest.fail(f"Expected {len(required_skills)} skills, found {Skills.objects.count()}")
    print(f"✓ Created {Skills.objects.count()} skills\n")
    
    # Phase 2: Users and Authors
    print("Phase 2: Users and Authors Creation and Validation")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    users_data = [
        ('john_doe', 'john@company.com', 'Acme Corp', 'Senior Recruiter'),
        ('jane_smith', 'jane@tech.com', 'Tech Solutions', 'HR Manager'),
        ('bob_jones', 'bob@startup.com', 'Startup Inc', 'Talent Acquisition'),
    ]
    
    authors = []
    for username, email, company, designation in users_data:
        # Create user
        user = User.objects.create_user(
            username=username,
            email=email,
            password='secure_password_123'
        )
        
        # Validate user
        if not user.username or not user.email:
            pytest.fail(f"User validation failed: missing username or email")
        if not user.is_active:
            pytest.fail(f"User '{username}' should be active by default")
        
        # Create author
        author = Author.objects.create(
            user=user,
            company=company,
            designation=designation
        )
        
        # Validate author
        if not author.company or len(author.company) < 3:
            pytest.fail(f"Author company name too short: '{author.company}'")
        if not author.designation:
            pytest.fail(f"Author '{username}' missing designation")
        
        authors.append(author)
        print(f"  ✓ {username} → {company} ({designation})")
    
    if Author.objects.count() != len(users_data):
        pytest.fail(f"Expected {len(users_data)} authors, found {Author.objects.count()}")
    print(f"✓ Created {Author.objects.count()} authors\n")
    
    # Phase 3: Locations
    print("Phase 3: Locations Creation and Validation")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    locations_data = [
        ('100 Tech Plaza', 'San Francisco', 'CA', 'USA', '94105'),
        ('200 Innovation Way', 'New York', 'NY', 'USA', '10001'),
        ('300 Startup Lane', 'Austin', 'TX', 'USA', '78701'),
    ]
    
    locations = []
    for street, city, state, country, zip_code in locations_data:
        location = Location.objects.create(
            street=street,
            city=city,
            state=state,
            country=country,
            zip=zip_code
        )
        
        # Validate location
        if not all([location.street, location.city, location.state, location.country, location.zip]):
            pytest.fail(f"Location validation failed: missing required fields")
        if len(location.zip) != 5 or not location.zip.isdigit():
            pytest.fail(f"Invalid ZIP code: '{location.zip}'")
        
        locations.append(location)
        print(f"  ✓ {city}, {state} ({zip_code})")
    
    if Location.objects.count() != len(locations_data):
        pytest.fail(f"Expected {len(locations_data)} locations, found {Location.objects.count()}")
    print(f"✓ Created {Location.objects.count()} locations\n")
    
    # Phase 4: Job Posts with Comprehensive Validation
    print("Phase 4: Job Posts Creation and Validation")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    jobs_data = [
        ('Senior Python Developer', 'Expert Python developer', 150000, 'Full Time', 0, 0, [0, 1, 4]),
        ('Full Stack Engineer', 'Full stack development', 130000, 'Full Time', 1, 1, [0, 1, 2, 3]),
        ('Backend Developer', 'Backend development', 120000, 'Part Time', 2, 2, [0, 1, 4]),
    ]
    
    jobs = []
    for title, desc, salary, job_type, loc_idx, auth_idx, skill_indices in jobs_data:
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=title,
            description=desc,
            expiry=timezone.now().date() + timedelta(days=30),
            salary=salary,
            type=job_type,
            location=locations[loc_idx],
            author=authors[auth_idx]
        )
        
        # Add skills
        job_skills = [skills[i] for i in skill_indices]
        job.skills.set(job_skills)
        
        # Comprehensive validation
        if not job.title or len(job.title) < 5:
            pytest.fail(f"Job title too short: '{job.title}'")
        if job.salary < 50000:
            pytest.fail(f"Salary too low: ${job.salary}")
        if job.skills.count() < 2:
            pytest.fail(f"Job '{title}' needs at least 2 skills, has {job.skills.count()}")
        if not job.location:
            pytest.fail(f"Job '{title}' missing location")
        if not job.author:
            pytest.fail(f"Job '{title}' missing author")
        if job.expiry < timezone.now().date():
            pytest.fail(f"Job '{title}' expiry date is in the past")
        
        jobs.append(job)
        print(f"  ✓ {title}")
        print(f"    Salary: ${salary:,}, Skills: {job.skills.count()}, Location: {job.location.city}")
    
    if JobPost.objects.count() != len(jobs_data):
        pytest.fail(f"Expected {len(jobs_data)} jobs, found {JobPost.objects.count()}")
    print(f"✓ Created {JobPost.objects.count()} job posts\n")
    
    # Phase 5: Integration Validation
    print("Phase 5: Integration Validation")
    print("=" * 70)
    
    # Validate relationships
    for job in jobs:
        # Each job must have valid relationships
        if not job.author or not Author.objects.filter(id=job.author.id).exists():
            pytest.fail(f"Job '{job.title}' has invalid author reference")
        if not job.location or not Location.objects.filter(id=job.location.id).exists():
            pytest.fail(f"Job '{job.title}' has invalid location reference")
        if job.skills.count() == 0:
            pytest.fail(f"Job '{job.title}' has no skills")
    
    print("✓ All job relationships validated")
    
    # Validate data consistency
    total_jobs = JobPost.objects.count()
    jobs_with_skills = JobPost.objects.filter(skills__isnull=False).distinct().count()
    
    if jobs_with_skills != total_jobs:
        pytest.fail(f"Some jobs missing skills: {total_jobs - jobs_with_skills}")
    print("✓ All jobs have skills assigned")
    
    # Final summary
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("FINAL SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"Skills: {Skills.objects.count()}")
    print(f"Users: {User.objects.count()}")
    print(f"Authors: {Author.objects.count()}")
    print(f"Locations: {Location.objects.count()}")
    print(f"Job Posts: {JobPost.objects.count()}")
    print(f"\n✓ COMPLETE INTEGRATION VALIDATION PASSED")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

pytest.skip()

Official Docs: pytest.skip() Reference

Skip the execution of a test with an optional reason.

Full Description

The pytest.skip() function immediately skips the currently executing test, marking it as skipped rather than passed or failed. Unlike test failures, skipped tests indicate that the test was intentionally not run due to specific conditions - such as missing dependencies, unsupported platforms, or incomplete features. When pytest.skip() is called, test execution stops immediately and the test is marked with an 'S' in the test report.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.skip() is valuable for conditionally skipping tests based on Django version, database backend, available third-party packages, or feature flags. For example, you might skip JobPost tests that require specific PostgreSQL features if running on SQLite, skip Author tests that need certain authentication backends, or skip Skills matching tests if machine learning libraries aren't installed.

Syntax

# Basic skip
pytest.skip("Reason for skipping")

# Skip with allow_module_level
pytest.skip("Missing dependency", allow_module_level=True)

# Conditional skip
if not some_condition:
    pytest.skip("Condition not met")

# Skip in fixture
@pytest.fixture
def my_fixture():
    if not check_requirement():
        pytest.skip("Requirement not available")
    return setup_data()

# Skip based on import
try:
    import some_module
except ImportError:
    pytest.skip("some_module not installed", allow_module_level=True)

Parameters Description

  • msg (str): The reason why the test is being skipped. This message will be displayed in the test report to explain why the test was not executed.
  • allow_module_level (bool, optional): If True, allows skipping at module level (outside of test functions). Default is False. Use this when you want to skip all tests in a module based on a condition.

Return Value

  • Returns: Never returns - raises Skipped exception immediately
  • Effect: Stops test execution and marks test as skipped
  • Exception type: Raises pytest.skip.Exception (Skipped)
  • Test result: Test is marked as SKIPPED with the provided reason

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: Skip JobPost Tests Based on Database Backend

Conditionally skip tests that require specific database features.

# tests/test_jobpost_database_specific.py
import pytest
from django.conf import settings
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from django.db import connection
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

def test_jobpost_with_database_specific_features():
    """Test JobPost with database-specific features"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("JOBPOST DATABASE-SPECIFIC FEATURES TEST")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Check database backend
    db_engine = settings.DATABASES['default']['ENGINE']
    print(f"Current database: {db_engine}")
    
    # Skip if not PostgreSQL (some features require PostgreSQL)
    if 'postgresql' not in db_engine.lower():
        pytest.skip(f"This test requires PostgreSQL, current database: {db_engine}")
    
    print("✓ PostgreSQL detected, proceeding with test\n")
    
    # Setup
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='pg_tester', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='PostgreSQL Corp',
        designation='Database Admin'
    )
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1 Database Lane',
        city='SF',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    # Create skills with PostgreSQL-specific features
    skills = [
        Skills.objects.create(name='PostgreSQL'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='Database Design'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='Query Optimization'),
    ]
    
    # Create job posts
    jobs = []
    for i in range(5):
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=f'Database Engineer {i+1}',
            description=f'PostgreSQL-focused position {i+1}',
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=100000 + (i * 10000),
            type='Full Time',
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        job.skills.set(skills)
        jobs.append(job)
    
    print("Created job posts:")
    for job in jobs:
        print(f"  {job.title}: ${job.salary:,}")
    
    # Use PostgreSQL-specific query features (e.g., full-text search)
    print(f"\nUsing PostgreSQL-specific features:")
    print(f"  Total jobs: {JobPost.objects.count()}")
    print(f"  Jobs with 'Database' in title: {JobPost.objects.filter(title__icontains='Database').count()}")
    
    # Advanced PostgreSQL query (would fail on SQLite)
    from django.contrib.postgres.search import SearchVector
    
    # Add search vector (PostgreSQL-specific)
    print(f"  ✓ PostgreSQL full-text search available")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("✓ PostgreSQL-specific test completed successfully")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 2: Skip Skills Tests Based on Missing Dependencies

Skip tests when optional packages aren't installed.

# tests/test_skills_ml_matching.py
import pytest
from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost
from django.utils import timezone

# Check for optional ML libraries
try:
    import numpy as np
    import sklearn
    HAS_ML_LIBS = True
except ImportError:
    HAS_ML_LIBS = False

def test_skills_ml_matching():
    """Test skills matching using machine learning (requires numpy, sklearn)"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("SKILLS ML MATCHING TEST")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Skip if ML libraries not available
    if not HAS_ML_LIBS:
        pytest.skip("This test requires numpy and sklearn for ML-based matching")
    
    print("✓ ML libraries available (numpy, sklearn)")
    print("Proceeding with ML-based skills matching\n")
    
    # Create skills
    all_skills = [
        'Python', 'Django', 'JavaScript', 'React', 'Vue.js',
        'Node.js', 'PostgreSQL', 'MongoDB', 'Docker', 'Kubernetes',
        'AWS', 'Azure', 'Machine Learning', 'Data Science', 'Testing'
    ]
    
    skills = []
    for skill_name in all_skills:
        skill = Skills.objects.create(name=skill_name)
        skills.append(skill)
    
    print(f"Created {len(skills)} skills for ML matching")
    
    # Setup job post
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='ml_recruiter', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='ML Tech Corp',
        designation='AI Recruiter'
    )
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1 ML Street',
        city='San Francisco',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    # Create jobs with different skill sets
    jobs_config = [
        ('Backend Developer', [0, 1, 6, 8, 10]),  # Python, Django, PostgreSQL, Docker, AWS
        ('Frontend Developer', [2, 3, 4, 14]),     # JavaScript, React, Vue.js, Testing
        ('Full Stack Developer', [0, 1, 2, 3, 6]), # Python, Django, JS, React, PostgreSQL
        ('DevOps Engineer', [8, 9, 10, 11]),       # Docker, K8s, AWS, Azure
        ('Data Scientist', [0, 6, 7, 12, 13]),     # Python, PostgreSQL, MongoDB, ML, DS
    ]
    
    jobs = []
    print(f"\nCreating jobs with skill requirements:")
    for title, skill_indices in jobs_config:
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=title,
            description=f'{title} position',
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=120000,
            type='Full Time',
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        job_skills = [skills[i] for i in skill_indices]
        job.skills.set(job_skills)
        jobs.append(job)
        print(f"  {title}: {len(job_skills)} skills")
    
    # Simulate ML-based skill matching
    print(f"\nPerforming ML-based skill similarity analysis:")
    
    # Create skill vectors (simplified for demonstration)
    skill_vectors = np.random.rand(len(all_skills), 10)
    
    print(f"  Skill vector dimensions: {skill_vectors.shape}")
    print(f"  Using cosine similarity for matching")
    
    # Calculate similarities between jobs
    print(f"\nJob similarity scores:")
    for i, job1 in enumerate(jobs):
        for job2 in jobs[i+1:]:
            # Simplified similarity calculation
            overlap = len(set(job1.skills.all()) & set(job2.skills.all()))
            total = len(set(job1.skills.all()) | set(job2.skills.all()))
            similarity = overlap / total if total > 0 else 0
            
            print(f"  {job1.title[:20]:20} vs {job2.title[:20]:20}: {similarity:.2f}")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("✓ ML-based skills matching completed successfully")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 3: Skip Author Tests Based on Django Version

Skip tests that use features from newer Django versions.

# tests/test_author_django_version_specific.py
import pytest
import django
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author, Location, JobPost
from django.utils import timezone

def test_author_with_new_django_features():
    """Test Author model with Django 4.2+ features"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("AUTHOR DJANGO VERSION-SPECIFIC TEST")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Check Django version
    django_version = django.VERSION
    print(f"Current Django version: {django.get_version()}")
    print(f"Version tuple: {django_version}")
    
    # Skip if Django < 4.2
    if django_version < (4, 2):
        pytest.skip(f"This test requires Django 4.2+, current version: {django.get_version()}")
    
    print("✓ Django 4.2+ detected, proceeding with test\n")
    
    # Create users and authors
    users_data = [
        ('alice', 'alice@tech.com', 'Tech Alpha', 'Senior Manager'),
        ('bob', 'bob@tech.com', 'Tech Beta', 'Lead Recruiter'),
        ('carol', 'carol@tech.com', 'Tech Gamma', 'HR Director'),
        ('dave', 'dave@tech.com', 'Tech Delta', 'Talent Specialist'),
        ('eve', 'eve@tech.com', 'Tech Epsilon', 'Hiring Coordinator'),
    ]
    
    authors = []
    print("Creating authors:")
    for username, email, company, designation in users_data:
        user = User.objects.create_user(
            username=username,
            email=email,
            password='secure_pass'
        )
        author = Author.objects.create(
            user=user,
            company=company,
            designation=designation
        )
        authors.append(author)
        print(f"  {username}: {company} - {designation}")
    
    # Use Django 4.2+ queryset features
    print(f"\nUsing Django 4.2+ queryset features:")
    
    # Example: agg_or_default() or other 4.2+ features
    from django.db.models import Count, Q
    
    # Complex query with modern Django features
    author_stats = Author.objects.annotate(
        job_count=Count('jobpost', distinct=True)
    ).values('company', 'job_count')
    
    print(f"  Author statistics query executed successfully")
    print(f"  Total authors: {Author.objects.count()}")
    
    # Create some job posts for authors
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1 Modern St',
        city='SF',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    print(f"\nCreating job posts:")
    for i, author in enumerate(authors):
        num_jobs = i + 1  # 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 jobs per author
        for j in range(num_jobs):
            JobPost.objects.create(
                title=f'Position {j+1} by {author.user.username}',
                description='Test position',
                expiry=timezone.now().date(),
                salary=100000,
                type='Full Time',
                location=location,
                author=author
            )
        print(f"  {author.user.username}: {num_jobs} jobs")
    
    # Verify with modern Django queries
    from django.db.models import Sum, Avg
    
    total_jobs = JobPost.objects.count()
    avg_jobs_per_author = total_jobs / Author.objects.count()
    
    print(f"\nStatistics:")
    print(f"  Total jobs: {total_jobs}")
    print(f"  Average jobs per author: {avg_jobs_per_author:.1f}")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("✓ Django 4.2+ features test completed successfully")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 4: Skip Location Tests on Specific Platforms

# tests/test_location_platform_specific.py
import pytest
import sys
import platform
from jobpost.models import Location, User, Author, JobPost
from django.utils import timezone

def test_location_with_platform_specific_features():
    """Test Location with platform-specific features"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("LOCATION PLATFORM-SPECIFIC TEST")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Check platform
    current_platform = platform.system()
    python_version = sys.version_info
    
    print(f"Platform: {current_platform}")
    print(f"Python version: {python_version.major}.{python_version.minor}.{python_version.micro}")
    
    # Skip on Windows (example: Unix-specific file operations)
    if current_platform == 'Windows':
        pytest.skip("This test requires Unix/Linux for file system operations")
    
    print("✓ Unix/Linux platform detected, proceeding with test\n")
    
    # Create locations with geographic data
    locations_data = [
        ('Seattle', 'WA', '47.6062', '-122.3321'),

        ('San Diego', 'CA', '32.7157', '-117.1611'),
    ]
    
    locations = []
    print("Creating locations with coordinates:")
    for city, state, lat, lon in locations_data:
        location = Location.objects.create(
            street=f'100 {city} Street',
            city=city,
            state=state,
            country='USA',
            zip='00000'
        )

        location.latitude = float(lat)
        location.longitude = float(lon)
        locations.append(location)

    # Perform Unix-specific operations
    print(f"\nPerforming platform-specific operations:")
    print(f"  ✓ File permissions check (Unix)")
    print(f"  ✓ Path operations (Unix)")
    print(f"  ✓ Geographic calculations")
    
    # Setup for job posts
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='geo_user', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Geographic Inc',
        designation='Location Manager'
    )
    
    # Create jobs for each location
    print(f"\nCreating jobs for each location:")
    for i, location in enumerate(locations):
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=f'Regional Manager - {location.city}',
            description=f'Position in {location.city}',
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=100000 + (i * 5000),
            type='Full Time',
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        print(f"  {job.title}: ${job.salary:,}")

    print(f"\nLocation statistics:")
    print(f"  Total locations: {Location.objects.count()}")
    print(f"  Total jobs: {JobPost.objects.count()}")
    print(f"  West Coast coverage: {Location.objects.filter(state__in=['WA', 'OR', 'CA']).count()} locations")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("✓ Platform-specific test completed successfully")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 5: Conditional Skip Based on Environment Variables

Skip tests based on environment configuration and feature flags.

# tests/test_integration_with_feature_flags.py
import pytest
import os
from django.conf import settings
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

def test_integration_with_feature_flags():
    """Integration test that checks feature flags and environment"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("INTEGRATION TEST WITH FEATURE FLAGS")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Check environment variables
    print("Checking environment configuration:")
    
    is_ci = os.getenv('CI', 'false').lower() == 'true'
    is_production = os.getenv('ENVIRONMENT', 'development') == 'production'
    enable_advanced_features = os.getenv('ENABLE_ADVANCED_FEATURES', 'false').lower() == 'true'
    
    print(f"  CI Environment: {is_ci}")
    print(f"  Production: {is_production}")
    print(f"  Advanced Features: {enable_advanced_features}")
    
    # Skip if running in production
    if is_production:
        pytest.skip("This test modifies data and should not run in production")
    
    print("✓ Not in production, safe to proceed\n")
    
    # Skip if advanced features not enabled
    if not enable_advanced_features:
        pytest.skip("Advanced features not enabled (set ENABLE_ADVANCED_FEATURES=true)")
    
    print("✓ Advanced features enabled\n")
    
    # Proceed with test
    print("Setting up complete test environment:")
    
    # Phase 1: Skills
    print("\nPhase 1: Skills")
    skills = []
    for skill_name in ['Python', 'Django', 'React', 'PostgreSQL', 'Docker']:
        skill = Skills.objects.create(name=skill_name)
        skills.append(skill)
    print(f"  ✓ Created {len(skills)} skills")
    
    # Phase 2: Users and Authors
    print("\nPhase 2: Users and Authors")
    users_data = [
        ('admin', 'admin@company.com', 'Enterprise Corp', 'CEO'),
        ('hr_manager', 'hr@company.com', 'Enterprise Corp', 'HR Manager'),
        ('recruiter1', 'r1@company.com', 'Enterprise Corp', 'Senior Recruiter'),
        ('recruiter2', 'r2@company.com', 'Enterprise Corp', 'Recruiter'),
        ('coordinator', 'coord@company.com', 'Enterprise Corp', 'HR Coordinator'),
    ]
    
    authors = []
    for username, email, company, designation in users_data:
        user = User.objects.create_user(
            username=username,
            email=email,
            password='secure_password'
        )
        author = Author.objects.create(
            user=user,
            company=company,
            designation=designation
        )
        authors.append(author)
    print(f"  ✓ Created {len(authors)} authors")
    
    # Phase 3: Locations
    print("\nPhase 3: Locations")
    locations = [
        Location.objects.create(
            street=f'{i}00 Corporate Blvd',
            city='Tech City',
            state='CA',
            country='USA',
            zip=f'9410{i}'
        ) for i in range(1, 6)
    ]
    print(f"  ✓ Created {len(locations)} locations")
    
    # Phase 4: Job Posts
    print("\nPhase 4: Job Posts")
    jobs = []
    for i in range(10):
        author = authors[i % len(authors)]
        location = locations[i % len(locations)]
        
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=f'Advanced Position {i+1}',
            description=f'Advanced features test position {i+1}',
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=100000 + (i * 10000),
            type=['Full Time', 'Part Time'][i % 2],
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        job.skills.set(skills[:3])
        jobs.append(job)
    print(f"  ✓ Created {len(jobs)} job posts")
    
    # Advanced feature testing
    print(f"\nTesting advanced features:")
    print(f"  Complex queries")
    print(f"  Batch operations")
    print(f"  Relationship traversal")
    
    # Statistics
    from django.db.models import Count, Avg
    
    stats = JobPost.objects.aggregate(
        total=Count('id'),
        avg_salary=Avg('salary')
    )
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("FINAL STATISTICS")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"Skills: {Skills.objects.count()}")
    print(f"Users: {User.objects.count()}")
    print(f"Authors: {Author.objects.count()}")
    print(f"Locations: {Location.objects.count()}")
    print(f"Job Posts: {stats['total']}")
    print(f"Average Salary: ${stats['avg_salary']:,.2f}")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Advanced features integration test completed")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

pytest.importorskip()

Official Docs: pytest.importorskip() Reference

Import and return a module, or skip the test if the import fails.

Full Description

The pytest.importorskip() function attempts to import a module and returns it if successful. If the import fails (module not installed), it automatically skips the test with an appropriate message. This is more elegant than using try/except with pytest.skip() because it combines both the import attempt and the skip decision in a single call. You can also specify a minimum version requirement to skip tests when an older version of a module is installed.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.importorskip() is essential for tests that depend on optional packages like celery for async JobPost processing, elasticsearch for Skills searching, redis for caching Author data, or pillow for Location image processing. It ensures tests run only when required dependencies are available and meet version requirements, making your test suite more robust across different development environments.

Syntax

# Basic import or skip
module = pytest.importorskip("module_name")

# With minimum version requirement
module = pytest.importorskip("module_name", minversion="2.0.0")

# Using imported module
requests = pytest.importorskip("requests")
response = requests.get("https://api.example.com")

# With reason
celery = pytest.importorskip("celery", reason="Async tasks require celery")

# At module level
pytestmark = pytest.mark.skipif(
    not pytest.importorskip("pandas", minversion="1.0"),
    reason="pandas 1.0+ required"
)

Parameters Description

  • modname (str): The name of the module to import. Can be a package name or a module path like "package.module".
  • minversion (str, optional): Minimum version required. If the installed version is older, the test will be skipped. Version string should match the module's __version__ format.
  • reason (str, optional): Custom reason for skipping. If not provided, pytest generates a default message indicating the module is not available.

Return Value

  • Returns: The imported module object if import succeeds and version requirement is met
  • Raises: pytest.skip.Exception (Skipped) if import fails or version requirement not met
  • Module availability: Returned module can be used immediately in the test
  • Version checking: Automatically compares installed version with minversion if specified

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: JobPost Export with Optional pandas Dependency

Export JobPost data to CSV/Excel using pandas if available.

# tests/test_jobpost_export_with_pandas.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

def test_jobpost_export_to_dataframe():
    """Test JobPost export using pandas (requires pandas)"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("JOBPOST EXPORT WITH PANDAS")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Import pandas or skip test
    pd = pytest.importorskip("pandas", minversion="1.0.0")
    print(f"✓ pandas {pd.__version__} imported successfully\n")
    
    # Setup data
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='data_analyst', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Data Analytics Corp',
        designation='Senior Data Analyst'
    )
    
    locations = [
        Location.objects.create(
            street=f'{i}00 Data Street',
            city=['SF', 'NY', 'Austin', 'Seattle', 'Boston'][i],
            state=['CA', 'NY', 'TX', 'WA', 'MA'][i],
            country='USA',
            zip=f'9410{i}'
        ) for i in range(5)
    ]
    
    skills = [
        Skills.objects.create(name='Python'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='Data Analysis'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='pandas'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='SQL'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='Visualization'),
    ]
    
    # Create job posts
    print("Creating job posts:")
    jobs_data = [
        ('Data Analyst', 'Analyze business data', 90000, 'Full Time', 0),
        ('Senior Data Analyst', 'Lead data analysis team', 120000, 'Full Time', 1),
        ('Data Scientist', 'ML and statistics', 140000, 'Full Time', 2),
        ('BI Developer', 'Business intelligence', 110000, 'Part Time', 3),
        ('Data Engineer', 'Data pipeline development', 130000, 'Full Time', 4),
    ]
    
    jobs = []
    for title, desc, salary, job_type, loc_idx in jobs_data:
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=title,
            description=desc,
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=salary,
            type=job_type,
            location=locations[loc_idx],
            author=author
        )
        job.skills.set(skills[:3])
        jobs.append(job)
        print(f"  {title}: ${salary:,}")
    
    # Export to pandas DataFrame
    print(f"\nExporting to pandas DataFrame:")
    
    # Query data
    jobs_queryset = JobPost.objects.select_related('author', 'location').all()
    
    # Convert to DataFrame
    data = []
    for job in jobs_queryset:
        data.append({
            'Title': job.title,
            'Description': job.description,
            'Salary': job.salary,
            'Type': job.type,
            'City': job.location.city,
            'State': job.location.state,
            'Company': job.author.company,
            'Skills': job.skills.count()
        })
    
    df = pd.DataFrame(data)
    
    print(f"\nDataFrame created:")
    print(f"  Shape: {df.shape}")
    print(f"  Columns: {list(df.columns)}")
    print(f"\nDataFrame preview:")
    print(df.to_string(index=False))
    
    # Statistical analysis
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("STATISTICAL ANALYSIS")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    
    stats = df['Salary'].describe()
    print(f"\nSalary statistics:")
    print(f"  Mean: ${stats['mean']:,.2f}")
    print(f"  Median: ${df['Salary'].median():,.2f}")
    print(f"  Min: ${stats['min']:,.2f}")
    print(f"  Max: ${stats['max']:,.2f}")
    print(f"  Std Dev: ${stats['std']:,.2f}")
    
    # Group by analysis
    print(f"\nSalary by job type:")
    grouped = df.groupby('Type')['Salary'].agg(['mean', 'count'])
    print(grouped.to_string())
    
    # Export capabilities
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("EXPORT CAPABILITIES VERIFIED")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"✓ DataFrame creation")
    print(f"✓ Statistical analysis")
    print(f"✓ Grouping and aggregation")
    print(f"✓ Ready for CSV/Excel export")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 2: Skills Matching with Machine Learning Libraries

Advanced skills matching using scikit-learn if available.

# tests/test_skills_ml_matching_advanced.py
import pytest
from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost
from django.utils import timezone

def test_skills_ml_matching_with_sklearn():
    """Test advanced skills matching with scikit-learn"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("SKILLS ML MATCHING WITH SCIKIT-LEARN")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Import required libraries or skip
    np = pytest.importorskip("numpy", minversion="1.20.0")
    sklearn = pytest.importorskip("sklearn", minversion="1.0.0")
    
    print(f"✓ numpy {np.__version__} imported")
    print(f"✓ scikit-learn {sklearn.__version__} imported\n")
    
    from sklearn.feature_extraction.text import TfidfVectorizer
    from sklearn.metrics.pairwise import cosine_similarity
    
    # Create comprehensive skills
    skills_list = [
        'Python', 'Django', 'Flask', 'FastAPI',
        'JavaScript', 'React', 'Vue.js', 'Angular',
        'PostgreSQL', 'MongoDB', 'Redis', 'MySQL',
        'Docker', 'Kubernetes', 'AWS', 'Azure',
        'Machine Learning', 'Deep Learning', 'NLP', 'Computer Vision'
    ]
    
    skills = []
    print("Creating skills:")
    for skill_name in skills_list:
        skill = Skills.objects.create(name=skill_name)
        skills.append(skill)
    print(f"  ✓ Created {len(skills)} skills\n")
    
    # Setup
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='ml_recruiter', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='ML Tech Corp',
        designation='AI Recruiter'
    )
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1 ML Ave',
        city='SF',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    # Create diverse job posts
    jobs_config = [
        ('Backend Developer', [0, 1, 8, 12]),
        ('Frontend Developer', [4, 5, 6, 7]),
        ('Full Stack Developer', [0, 1, 4, 5, 8]),
        ('DevOps Engineer', [12, 13, 14, 15]),
        ('ML Engineer', [0, 16, 17, 18, 19]),
    ]
    
    jobs = []
    skill_descriptions = []
    
    print("Creating jobs with skill requirements:")
    for title, skill_indices in jobs_config:
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=title,
            description=f'{title} position',
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=120000,
            type='Full Time',
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        job_skills = [skills[i] for i in skill_indices]
        job.skills.set(job_skills)
        jobs.append(job)
        
        # Create skill description for ML
        skill_text = ' '.join([s.name for s in job_skills])
        skill_descriptions.append(skill_text)
        
        print(f"  {title}")
        print(f"    Skills: {', '.join([s.name for s in job_skills])}")
    
    # ML-based skill matching
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("ML-BASED SKILL SIMILARITY ANALYSIS")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create TF-IDF vectors
    vectorizer = TfidfVectorizer()
    tfidf_matrix = vectorizer.fit_transform(skill_descriptions)
    
    print(f"TF-IDF Matrix:")
    print(f"  Shape: {tfidf_matrix.shape}")
    print(f"  Features: {len(vectorizer.get_feature_names_out())}")
    
    # Calculate similarity matrix
    similarity_matrix = cosine_similarity(tfidf_matrix)
    
    print(f"\nJob Similarity Matrix:")
    print(f"{'':25}", end='')
    for job in jobs:
        print(f"{job.title[:15]:>17}", end='')
    print()
    
    for i, job1 in enumerate(jobs):
        print(f"{job1.title[:24]:25}", end='')
        for j, job2 in enumerate(jobs):
            sim_score = similarity_matrix[i][j]
            print(f"{sim_score:17.3f}", end='')
        print()
    
    # Find most similar job pairs
    print(f"\nTop 3 similar job pairs:")
    similarities = []
    for i in range(len(jobs)):
        for j in range(i+1, len(jobs)):
            similarities.append((jobs[i], jobs[j], similarity_matrix[i][j]))
    
    similarities.sort(key=lambda x: x[2], reverse=True)
    
    for job1, job2, score in similarities[:3]:
        print(f"  {job1.title} ↔ {job2.title}")
        print(f"    Similarity: {score:.3f}")
        
        # Show overlapping skills
        skills1 = set(job1.skills.all())
        skills2 = set(job2.skills.all())
        overlap = skills1 & skills2
        
        if overlap:
            print(f"    Common skills: {', '.join([s.name for s in overlap])}")
        print()
    
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print("✓ ML-based skills matching completed")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 3: Author Notifications with Celery

Async task processing for Author notifications using Celery.

# tests/test_author_celery_tasks.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author, Location, JobPost, Skills
from django.utils import timezone

def test_author_async_notifications():
    """Test Author notification system with Celery"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("AUTHOR ASYNC NOTIFICATIONS WITH CELERY")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Import Celery or skip
    celery = pytest.importorskip("celery", minversion="5.0.0")
    print(f"✓ Celery {celery.__version__} imported\n")
    
    # Create authors
    authors_data = [
        ('john_hr', 'john@company.com', 'Tech Alpha', 'HR Manager'),
        ('jane_recruiter', 'jane@company.com', 'Tech Beta', 'Senior Recruiter'),
        ('bob_coordinator', 'bob@company.com', 'Tech Gamma', 'Coordinator'),
        ('alice_lead', 'alice@company.com', 'Tech Delta', 'Recruiting Lead'),
        ('charlie_specialist', 'charlie@company.com', 'Tech Epsilon', 'Talent Specialist'),
    ]
    
    authors = []
    print("Creating authors:")
    for username, email, company, designation in authors_data:
        user = User.objects.create_user(
            username=username,
            email=email,
            password='test123'
        )
        author = Author.objects.create(
            user=user,
            company=company,
            designation=designation
        )
        authors.append(author)
        print(f"  {username}: {email}")
    
    # Create location and skills
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1 Async Lane',
        city='SF',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    skills = [
        Skills.objects.create(name='Python'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='Celery'),
        Skills.objects.create(name='Redis'),
    ]
    
    # Create jobs for each author
    print(f"\nCreating job posts:")
    jobs_per_author = [2, 3, 1, 4, 2]
    
    all_jobs = []
    for i, (author, job_count) in enumerate(zip(authors, jobs_per_author)):
        for j in range(job_count):
            job = JobPost.objects.create(
                title=f'Position {j+1} by {author.user.username}',
                description='Test job posting',
                expiry=timezone.now().date(),
                salary=100000 + (i * 10000),
                type='Full Time',
                location=location,
                author=author
            )
            job.skills.set(skills)
            all_jobs.append(job)
        print(f"  {author.user.username}: {job_count} jobs")
    
    # Simulate async task processing
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("SIMULATING ASYNC NOTIFICATION TASKS")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Task: Send notification to each author about their jobs
    notification_tasks = []
    
    for author in authors:
        author_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(author=author)
        job_count = author_jobs.count()
        
        # Simulate task creation
        task_info = {
            'author': author.user.username,
            'email': author.user.email,
            'job_count': job_count,
            'company': author.company,
            'task_id': f'task-{author.id}',
            'status': 'queued'
        }
        notification_tasks.append(task_info)
        
        print(f"Task {task_info['task_id']}:")
        print(f"  Author: {task_info['author']}")
        print(f"  Email: {task_info['email']}")
        print(f"  Jobs to notify: {task_info['job_count']}")
        print(f"  Status: {task_info['status']}\n")
    
    # Simulate task execution
    print("Executing tasks (simulated):")
    for task in notification_tasks:
        task['status'] = 'success'
        print(f"  ✓ {task['task_id']}: Notification sent to {task['email']}")
    
    # Summary
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TASK EXECUTION SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"Total tasks: {len(notification_tasks)}")
    print(f"Successful: {sum(1 for t in notification_tasks if t['status'] == 'success')}")
    print(f"Total notifications sent: {sum(t['job_count'] for t in notification_tasks)}")
    print(f"\n✓ Celery task system verified")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 4: Location Image Processing with Pillow

Process and validate location images using Pillow library.

# tests/test_location_image_processing.py
import pytest
from jobpost.models import Location, User, Author, JobPost
from django.utils import timezone
from io import BytesIO

def test_location_image_processing():
    """Test Location image processing with Pillow"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("LOCATION IMAGE PROCESSING WITH PILLOW")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Import Pillow or skip
    PIL = pytest.importorskip("PIL", minversion="9.0.0")
    print(f"✓ Pillow {PIL.__version__} imported\n")
    
    from PIL import Image, ImageDraw, ImageFont
    
    # Create locations
    locations_data = [
        ('San Francisco', 'CA', '123 Market St', '94105'),
        ('New York', 'NY', '456 Broadway', '10007'),
        ('Austin', 'TX', '789 Congress Ave', '78701'),
        ('Seattle', 'WA', '321 Pike Place', '98101'),
        ('Boston', 'MA', '654 Boylston St', '02116'),
    ]
    
    locations = []
    print("Creating locations:")
    for city, state, street, zip_code in locations_data:
        location = Location.objects.create(
            street=street,
            city=city,
            state=state,
            country='USA',
            zip=zip_code
        )
        locations.append(location)
        print(f"  {city}, {state}")
    
    # Generate location preview images
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("GENERATING LOCATION PREVIEW IMAGES")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    image_data = []
    
    for location in locations:
        # Create image
        img = Image.new('RGB', (400, 200), color='#14b8a6')
        draw = ImageDraw.Draw(img)
        
        # Add text
        text = f"{location.city}, {location.state}"
        
        # Calculate text position (centered)
        bbox = draw.textbbox((0, 0), text)
        text_width = bbox[2] - bbox[0]
        text_height = bbox[3] - bbox[1]
        position = ((400 - text_width) // 2, (200 - text_height) // 2)
        
        draw.text(position, text, fill='white')
        
        # Add border
        draw.rectangle([(0, 0), (399, 199)], outline='white', width=3)
        
        # Get image info
        img_format = img.format if img.format else 'PNG'
        img_size = img.size
        img_mode = img.mode
        
        image_info = {
            'location': location,
            'image': img,
            'format': img_format,
            'size': img_size,
            'mode': img_mode,
            'file_size': len(img.tobytes())
        }
        image_data.append(image_info)
        
        print(f"{location.city}, {location.state}:")
        print(f"  Format: {img_format}")
        print(f"  Size: {img_size}")
        print(f"  Mode: {img_mode}")
        print(f"  Bytes: {image_info['file_size']:,}\n")
    
    # Image validation
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print("IMAGE VALIDATION")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    total_size = 0
    for info in image_data:
        # Validate image
        img = info['image']
        
        # Check dimensions
        width, height = img.size
        assert width == 400 and height == 200, f"Invalid dimensions: {img.size}"
        
        # Check mode
        assert img.mode == 'RGB', f"Invalid mode: {img.mode}"
        
        total_size += info['file_size']
        print(f"✓ {info['location'].city}: Validated")
    
    # Summary
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("IMAGE PROCESSING SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"Total images: {len(image_data)}")
    print(f"Total size: {total_size:,} bytes ({total_size / 1024:.2f} KB)")
    print(f"Average size: {total_size / len(image_data):,.0f} bytes")
    print(f"\n✓ All location images processed successfully")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create jobs for locations with images
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='image_admin', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Visual Corp',
        designation='Image Manager'
    )
    
    print("Creating jobs for image-enabled locations:")
    for location in locations:
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=f'Position in {location.city}',
            description='Job with location image',
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=120000,
            type='Full Time',
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        print(f"  ✓ {job.title}")

Example 5: Complete Integration with Multiple Optional Dependencies

Comprehensive test using multiple optional libraries across all models.

# tests/test_complete_optional_dependencies.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

def test_complete_integration_optional_deps():
    """Complete integration test with multiple optional dependencies"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("COMPLETE INTEGRATION WITH OPTIONAL DEPENDENCIES")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Check and import optional dependencies
    print("Checking optional dependencies:")
    
    dependencies = {}
    
    # pandas for data export
    try:
        pd = pytest.importorskip("pandas", minversion="1.0.0")
        dependencies['pandas'] = pd.__version__
        print(f"  ✓ pandas {pd.__version__}")
    except Exception:
        pd = None
        print(f"  ✗ pandas not available")
    
    # requests for API calls
    try:
        requests = pytest.importorskip("requests", minversion="2.20.0")
        dependencies['requests'] = requests.__version__
        print(f"  ✓ requests {requests.__version__}")
    except Exception:
        requests = None
        print(f"  ✗ requests not available")
    
    # At least one optional dependency required
    if not any([pd, requests]):
        pytest.skip("At least one optional dependency (pandas or requests) required")
    
    print(f"\nProceeding with available dependencies\n")
    
    # Phase 1: Create Skills
    print("Phase 1: Creating Skills")
    print("-" * 70)
    skills_list = [
        'Python', 'Django', 'REST API', 'PostgreSQL', 'Redis',
        'Docker', 'Kubernetes', 'AWS', 'React', 'TypeScript'
    ]
    
    skills = []
    for skill_name in skills_list:
        skill = Skills.objects.create(name=skill_name)
        skills.append(skill)
    print(f"✓ Created {len(skills)} skills\n")
    
    # Phase 2: Create Users and Authors
    print("Phase 2: Creating Users and Authors")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    users_data = [
        ('tech_lead', 'lead@tech.com', 'Innovation Inc', 'Technical Lead'),
        ('senior_hr', 'hr@tech.com', 'Innovation Inc', 'Senior HR'),
        ('recruiter', 'recruit@tech.com', 'Innovation Inc', 'Recruiter'),
        ('manager', 'manager@tech.com', 'Innovation Inc', 'Hiring Manager'),
        ('coordinator', 'coord@tech.com', 'Innovation Inc', 'Coordinator'),
    ]
    
    authors = []
    for username, email, company, designation in users_data:
        user = User.objects.create_user(
            username=username,
            email=email,
            password='secure_pass'
        )
        author = Author.objects.create(
            user=user,
            company=company,
            designation=designation
        )
        authors.append(author)
    print(f"✓ Created {len(authors)} authors\n")
    
    # Phase 3: Create Locations
    print("Phase 3: Creating Locations")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    locations_data = [
        ('SF', 'CA'), ('NY', 'NY'), ('Austin', 'TX'),
        ('Seattle', 'WA'), ('Boston', 'MA')
    ]
    
    locations = []
    for i, (city, state) in enumerate(locations_data):
        location = Location.objects.create(
            street=f'{i+1}00 Tech Street',
            city=city,
            state=state,
            country='USA',
            zip=f'9410{i}'
        )
        locations.append(location)
    print(f"✓ Created {len(locations)} locations\n")
    
    # Phase 4: Create Job Posts
    print("Phase 4: Creating Job Posts")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    jobs = []
    for i in range(15):
        author = authors[i % len(authors)]
        location = locations[i % len(locations)]
        
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=f'Engineer Position {i+1}',
            description=f'Technical position {i+1}',
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=90000 + (i * 5000),
            type=['Full Time', 'Part Time'][i % 2],
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        
        # Assign 3-5 random skills
        num_skills = 3 + (i % 3)
        job.skills.set(skills[:num_skills])
        jobs.append(job)
    
    print(f"✓ Created {len(jobs)} job posts\n")

                'Type': job.type,
                'City': job.location.city,
                'Author': job.author.user.username,
                'Skills': job.skills.count()
            })
        
        df = pd.DataFrame(data)
        
        print("DataFrame Statistics:")
        print(f"  Shape: {df.shape}")
        print(f"  Salary Mean: ${df['Salary'].mean():,.2f}")
        print(f"  Salary Median: ${df['Salary'].median():,.2f}")

        print(df['City'].value_counts().to_string())
        print()

            'active_jobs': JobPost.objects.filter(type='Full Time').count()

    print(f"\n✓ Complete integration test passed")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
