pytest.xfail()

Official Docs: pytest.xfail() Reference

Imperatively mark a test as expected to fail.

Full Description

The pytest.xfail() function marks a test as "expected to fail" (xfail). Unlike pytest.skip() which prevents test execution entirely, xfail runs the test but expects it to fail. If the test fails as expected, it's marked as XFAIL. If it unexpectedly passes, it's marked as XPASS (unexpected pass). This is useful for documenting known bugs, incomplete features, or platform-specific issues while keeping them in your test suite.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.xfail() is valuable for tracking known issues like JobPost validation bugs awaiting fixes, Author permission features under development, Skills matching algorithms being refined, or Location geocoding issues with certain addresses. It keeps these tests visible in your suite while preventing CI failures, and alerts you when issues are unexpectedly resolved.

Syntax

# Basic xfail
pytest.xfail("Known bug in validation")

# With reason
pytest.xfail(reason="Feature not yet implemented")

# Conditional xfail
if some_condition:
    pytest.xfail("Fails under certain conditions")

# With raises parameter (expected exception)
pytest.xfail(reason="Expected to raise ValueError", raises=ValueError)

# With run parameter (control execution)
pytest.xfail(reason="Don't even run this", run=False)

# With strict mode
pytest.xfail(reason="Must fail", strict=True)

Parameters Description

  • reason (str, optional): Explanation for why the test is expected to fail. Displayed in test reports to document the known issue.
  • raises (Exception or tuple of Exceptions, optional): Specific exception type(s) expected to be raised. If specified, only those exceptions will be considered as expected failures.
  • run (bool, optional): If False, the test won't run at all (similar to skip). If True (default), the test runs and is expected to fail.
  • strict (bool, optional): If True, an unexpected pass (XPASS) will fail the test. If False (default), XPASS is just reported but doesn't fail the build.

Return Value

  • Returns: Never returns - raises pytest.xfail.Exception immediately
  • Effect: Marks test as XFAIL (expected failure) or XPASS (unexpected pass)
  • Test execution: Test runs unless run=False is specified
  • CI impact: XFAIL doesn't cause build failures (unless strict=True and test passes)

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: JobPost Validation Known Bug

Mark test as xfail for a known JobPost validation bug.

# tests/test_jobpost_known_bug.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from django.core.exceptions import ValidationError
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

def test_jobpost_negative_salary_validation():
    """Test JobPost validation with negative salary (known bug)"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("JOBPOST NEGATIVE SALARY VALIDATION (KNOWN BUG)")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Setup
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='bug_tester', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Bug Testing Corp',
        designation='QA Engineer'
    )
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1 Bug Street',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    # This is a known bug: negative salaries should be rejected but aren't
    print("Testing known bug: negative salary acceptance")
    print("Expected behavior: Should raise ValidationError")
    print("Actual behavior: Accepts negative salary\n")
    
    # Mark as expected failure
    pytest.xfail(reason="Known bug: JobPost accepts negative salary (issue #123)")
    
    # Create job with negative salary
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Test Position',
        description='Testing negative salary bug',
        expiry=timezone.now().date(),
        salary=-50000,  # Negative salary - should fail but doesn't
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    
    print(f"Job created: {job.title}")
    print(f"Salary: ${job.salary:,}")
    print(f"Bug confirmed: Negative salary accepted\n")
    
    # This assertion will fail, which is expected
    assert job.salary > 0, "Salary should be positive"
    
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print("This test is marked as XFAIL due to known bug")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

        ('lead', 'lead@company.com', 'TechCorp', 'Team Lead', 3),
        ('senior', 'senior@company.com', 'TechCorp', 'Senior Recruiter', 2),
        ('junior', 'junior@company.com', 'TechCorp', 'Junior Recruiter', 1),
    ]
    
    authors = []

Example 4: Location Geocoding Platform-Specific Issue

Test that fails on certain platforms due to geocoding issues.

# tests/test_location_geocoding.py
import pytest
import sys
from jobpost.models import Location

def test_location_geocoding_coordinates():
    """Test Location coordinate generation (platform-specific issue)"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("LOCATION GEOCODING TEST (PLATFORM-SPECIFIC ISSUE)")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    platform = sys.platform
    print(f"Platform: {platform}")
    
    # Create locations
    locations_data = [
        ('San Francisco', 'CA', '37.7749', '-122.4194'),
        ('New York', 'NY', '40.7128', '-74.0060'),
        ('Austin', 'TX', '30.2672', '-97.7431'),
        ('Seattle', 'WA', '47.6062', '-122.3321'),
        ('Boston', 'MA', '42.3601', '-71.0589'),
    ]
    
    locations = []
    print(f"\nCreating locations:")
    for city, state, lat, lon in locations_data:
        location = Location.objects.create(
            street=f'100 {city} St',
            city=city,
            state=state,
            country='USA',
            zip='00000'
        )
        # Simulate coordinate storage
        location._latitude = float(lat)
        location._longitude = float(lon)
        locations.append(location)
        print(f"  {city}, {state}: ({lat}, {lon})")
    
    # Known issue on Windows: coordinate precision differs
    if platform == 'win32':
        print(f"\nKnown issue detected: Windows coordinate precision")
        pytest.xfail(reason="Geocoding precision issue on Windows (issue #901)")
    
    print(f"\nValidating coordinates:")
    
    # Test coordinate precision
    for location in locations:
        lat = location._latitude
        lon = location._longitude
        
        # Check precision (fails on Windows due to floating point handling)
        lat_precision = len(str(lat).split('.')[-1])
        lon_precision = len(str(lon).split('.')[-1])
        
        print(f"  {location.city}:")
        print(f"    Latitude precision: {lat_precision} decimals")
        print(f"    Longitude precision: {lon_precision} decimals")
        
        # This assertion fails on Windows
        assert lat_precision >= 4, f"Latitude precision insufficient: {lat_precision}"
        assert lon_precision >= 4, f"Longitude precision insufficient: {lon_precision}"
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("All coordinate validations passed")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 5: Complete Integration with Multiple Known Issues

Comprehensive test tracking multiple xfail conditions.

# tests/test_integration_known_issues.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

def test_complete_workflow_with_known_issues():
    """Complete workflow test with multiple known issues"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("COMPLETE WORKFLOW WITH KNOWN ISSUES")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Track known issues
    known_issues = []
    
    # Phase 1: Skills with duplicate detection issue
    print("Phase 1: Skills Creation")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    skills = []
    skills_names = ['Python', 'python', 'PYTHON', 'Django', 'React']
    
    for skill_name in skills_names:
        skill = Skills.objects.create(name=skill_name)
        skills.append(skill)
        print(f"  Created: {skill.name}")
    
    # Known issue: case-insensitive duplicates allowed
    unique_skills = set(s.name.lower() for s in skills)
    if len(unique_skills) < len(skills):
        issue = "Duplicate skills with different cases allowed"
        known_issues.append(issue)
        print(f"  ⚠ Issue: {issue}")
    
    print()
    
    # Phase 2: Authors
    print("Phase 2: Authors Creation")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    users_data = [
        ('user1', 'user1@test.com', 'Company A', 'Manager'),
        ('user2', 'user2@test.com', 'Company B', 'Recruiter'),
        ('user3', 'user3@test.com', '', 'Lead'),  # Empty company
    ]
    
    authors = []
    for username, email, company, designation in users_data:
        user = User.objects.create_user(
            username=username,
            email=email,
            password='test123'
        )
        author = Author.objects.create(
            user=user,
            company=company,
            designation=designation
        )
        authors.append(author)
        print(f"  {username}: {company or '[EMPTY]'} - {designation}")
        
        # Known issue: empty company allowed
        if not company:
            issue = "Empty company name allowed for authors"
            if issue not in known_issues:
                known_issues.append(issue)
            print(f"    ⚠ Issue: {issue}")
    
    print()
    
    # Phase 3: Locations
    print("Phase 3: Locations Creation")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    locations = []
    for i in range(3):
        location = Location.objects.create(
            street=f'{i}00 Test St',
            city='TestCity',
            state='XX',  # Invalid state code
            country='USA',
            zip='12345'
        )
        locations.append(location)
        print(f"  Location {i+1}: State={location.state}")
        
        # Known issue: invalid state codes accepted
        if location.state not in ['CA', 'NY', 'TX', 'WA', 'MA']:
            issue = "Invalid state codes accepted"
            if issue not in known_issues:
                known_issues.append(issue)
            print(f"    ⚠ Issue: {issue}")
    
    print()
    
    # Phase 4: Job Posts
    print("Phase 4: Job Posts Creation")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    jobs = []
    for i, author in enumerate(authors):
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=f'Job {i+1}',
            description='Test job',
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=50000 if i < 2 else 0,  # Zero salary for last job
            type='Full Time',
            location=locations[i],
            author=author
        )
        job.skills.set(skills[:2])
        jobs.append(job)
        print(f"  {job.title}: Salary=${job.salary}")
        
        # Known issue: zero salary allowed
        if job.salary == 0:
            issue = "Zero salary accepted for job posts"
            if issue not in known_issues:
                known_issues.append(issue)
            print(f"    ⚠ Issue: {issue}")
    
    # Summary of known issues
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("KNOWN ISSUES SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"Total known issues found: {len(known_issues)}\n")
    
    for i, issue in enumerate(known_issues, 1):
        print(f"{i}. {issue}")
    
    # Mark test as xfail due to multiple known issues
    if known_issues:
        issues_text = '; '.join(known_issues[:2])  # First 2 issues
        pytest.xfail(reason=f"Multiple known issues: {issues_text}")
    
    # Validation that will fail due to known issues
    print(f"\nRunning validations:")
    
    # This will fail: duplicate skills
    unique_count = len(set(s.name.lower() for s in skills))
    print(f"  Unique skills check: {unique_count} vs {len(skills)}")
    assert unique_count == len(skills), "Duplicate skills detected"
    
    # This will fail: empty companies
    empty_companies = sum(1 for a in authors if not a.company)
    print(f"  Empty companies: {empty_companies}")
    assert empty_companies == 0, "Authors with empty companies found"
    
    # This will fail: invalid states
    invalid_states = sum(1 for loc in locations if loc.state == 'XX')
    print(f"  Invalid states: {invalid_states}")
    assert invalid_states == 0, "Invalid state codes found"
    
    # This will fail: zero salaries
    zero_salaries = sum(1 for job in jobs if job.salary == 0)
    print(f"  Zero salaries: {zero_salaries}")
    assert zero_salaries == 0, "Jobs with zero salary found"
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("All validations passed (unexpected)")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

pytest.exit()

Official Docs: pytest.exit() Reference

Exit the test session with a return code.

Full Description

The pytest.exit() function immediately terminates the entire test session with a specified message and return code. Unlike skip() or xfail() which affect individual tests, exit() halts all remaining test execution. This is useful for critical failures where continuing testing is meaningless—such as database connection failures, missing critical configuration, or detecting fundamental environment issues.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.exit() is valuable for pre-flight checks: verifying database connectivity before running JobPost tests, ensuring required environment variables are set for Author authentication, validating critical configuration like MEDIA_ROOT for Location images, or checking that essential services like Redis are available. It prevents wasting time running hundreds of tests when a fundamental requirement isn't met.

Syntax

# Basic exit
pytest.exit("Critical failure")

# With return code
pytest.exit("Database unavailable", returncode=2)

# Conditional exit
if not critical_service_available():
    pytest.exit("Service down", returncode=1)

# In conftest.py for session-level checks
def pytest_sessionstart(session):
    if not database_available():
        pytest.exit("Database not available")

Parameters Description

  • msg (str): Message explaining why the test session is being terminated. Displayed to the user before exit.
  • returncode (int, optional): Exit code to return to the operating system. Defaults to 0 (success). Use non-zero codes (1-255) to indicate errors. Common convention: 1 for general errors, 2 for configuration issues, 3 for service unavailability.

Return Value

  • Returns: Never returns - raises pytest.exit.Exception immediately
  • Effect: Terminates entire test session immediately
  • Exit code: Returns specified returncode to OS
  • Remaining tests: All uncompleted tests are not executed

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: Database Connection Pre-Flight Check

Exit if database is unavailable before running any JobPost tests.

# conftest.py
import pytest
from django.db import connection
from django.db.utils import OperationalError

def pytest_sessionstart(session):
    """Check database connectivity before running any tests"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("PRE-FLIGHT CHECK: Database Connectivity")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    try:
        # Attempt database connection
        with connection.cursor() as cursor:
            cursor.execute("SELECT 1")
            result = cursor.fetchone()
            
        print("✓ Database connection: SUCCESS")
        print(f"  Database: {connection.settings_dict['NAME']}")
        print(f"  Engine: {connection.settings_dict['ENGINE']}")
        print(f"  Host: {connection.settings_dict.get('HOST', 'localhost')}")
        
        # Check if our tables exist
        tables = connection.introspection.table_names()
        required_tables = ['jobpost_skills', 'jobpost_author', 'jobpost_location', 'jobpost_jobpost']
        
        print(f"\n✓ Checking required tables:")
        missing_tables = []
        for table in required_tables:
            if table in tables:
                print(f"  ✓ {table}")
            else:
                print(f"  ✗ {table} (MISSING)")
                missing_tables.append(table)
        
        if missing_tables:
            print(f"\n{'='*70}")
            print(f"CRITICAL: Missing {len(missing_tables)} required tables")
            print(f"{'='*70}")
            pytest.exit(
                f"Missing required tables: {', '.join(missing_tables)}. "
                f"Run 'python manage.py migrate' first.",
                returncode=2
            )
        
        print(f"\n{'='*70}")
        print("All pre-flight checks passed - proceeding with tests")
        print(f"{'='*70}\n")
        
    except OperationalError as e:
        print(f"\n✗ Database connection: FAILED")
        print(f"  Error: {e}")
        print(f"\n{'='*70}")
        print("CRITICAL: Cannot connect to database")
        print(f"{'='*70}")
        pytest.exit(
            f"Database connection failed: {e}. "
            f"Check your database settings and ensure the database is running.",
            returncode=1
        )

Example 2: Environment Variables Validation

Exit if required environment variables are missing.

# conftest.py
import pytest
import os

def pytest_configure(config):
    """Validate required environment variables before testing"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("ENVIRONMENT VALIDATION")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Define required environment variables for testing
    required_vars = {
        'DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE': 'Django settings module',
        'DATABASE_URL': 'Database connection string',
        'SECRET_KEY': 'Django secret key',
        'MEDIA_ROOT': 'Media files directory',
        'EMAIL_HOST': 'Email server host',
    }
    
    missing_vars = []
    present_vars = []
    
    print("Checking required environment variables:")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    for var_name, description in required_vars.items():
        value = os.environ.get(var_name)
        
        if value:
            # Mask sensitive values
            if 'SECRET' in var_name or 'PASSWORD' in var_name:
                display_value = '*' * 8
            else:
                display_value = value[:50] + '...' if len(value) > 50 else value
            
            present_vars.append(var_name)
            print(f"  ✓ {var_name}")
            print(f"    Description: {description}")
            print(f"    Value: {display_value}")
        else:
            missing_vars.append(var_name)
            print(f"  ✗ {var_name}")
            print(f"    Description: {description}")
            print(f"    Status: MISSING")
    
    print()
    
    # Summary
    print(f"Summary:")
    print(f"  Present: {len(present_vars)}/{len(required_vars)}")
    print(f"  Missing: {len(missing_vars)}/{len(required_vars)}")
    
    if missing_vars:
        print(f"\n{'='*70}")
        print(f"CRITICAL: Missing required environment variables")
        print(f"{'='*70}")
        print("\nMissing variables:")
        for var in missing_vars:
            print(f"  - {var}: {required_vars[var]}")
        
        print("\nTo fix this, set the environment variables:")
        print("  export DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE='anihpj.settings'")
        print("  export DATABASE_URL='postgresql://user:pass@localhost/db'")
        print("  # ... etc")
        
        pytest.exit(
            f"Missing {len(missing_vars)} required environment variable(s): "
            f"{', '.join(missing_vars)}. Cannot proceed with tests.",
            returncode=2
        )
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("Environment validation passed")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 3: Critical Service Availability Check

Exit if required services (Redis, Celery) are unavailable.

# conftest.py
import pytest
import socket

def check_service_availability(host, port, service_name):
    """Check if a service is available by attempting to connect"""
    try:
        sock = socket.socket(socket.AF_INET, socket.SOCK_STREAM)
        sock.settimeout(2)
        result = sock.connect_ex((host, port))
        sock.close()
        return result == 0
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"    Error checking {service_name}: {e}")
        return False

def pytest_sessionstart(session):
    """Verify critical services are available"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("CRITICAL SERVICES CHECK")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Define critical services
    services = [
        ('localhost', 5432, 'PostgreSQL', True),   # Required
        ('localhost', 6379, 'Redis', True),         # Required
        ('localhost', 5672, 'RabbitMQ', False),     # Optional
        ('localhost', 9200, 'Elasticsearch', False),# Optional
    ]
    
    unavailable_required = []
    unavailable_optional = []
    available = []
    
    print("Checking service availability:")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    for host, port, name, required in services:
        print(f"\n  {name} ({host}:{port})")
        print(f"    Required: {'Yes' if required else 'No'}")
        
        is_available = check_service_availability(host, port, name)
        
        if is_available:
            print(f"    Status: ✓ AVAILABLE")
            available.append(name)
        else:
            print(f"    Status: ✗ UNAVAILABLE")
            if required:
                unavailable_required.append(name)
            else:
                unavailable_optional.append(name)
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"Available: {len(available)}")
    print(f"Unavailable (Required): {len(unavailable_required)}")
    print(f"Unavailable (Optional): {len(unavailable_optional)}")
    
    # Exit if required services are unavailable
    if unavailable_required:
        print(f"\n{'='*70}")
        print("CRITICAL: Required services unavailable")
        print(f"{'='*70}")
        print("\nUnavailable required services:")
        for service in unavailable_required:
            print(f"  - {service}")
        
        print("\nTests cannot run without these services.")
        print("Please start the required services and try again.")
        
        pytest.exit(
            f"Required services unavailable: {', '.join(unavailable_required)}. "
            f"Start these services before running tests.",
            returncode=3
        )
    
    if unavailable_optional:
        print(f"\nWARNING: Optional services unavailable:")
        for service in unavailable_optional:
            print(f"  - {service}")
        print("Some tests may be skipped.")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("Service check passed - proceeding with tests")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 4: Django Version Compatibility Check

Exit if Django version is incompatible with tests.

# conftest.py
import pytest
import django
from packaging import version

def pytest_configure(config):
    """Check Django version compatibility"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("DJANGO VERSION COMPATIBILITY CHECK")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    current_version = django.get_version()
    current_parsed = version.parse(current_version)
    
    print(f"Current Django version: {current_version}")
    
    # Define version requirements
    min_version = version.parse("4.2.0")
    max_version = version.parse("6.0.0")
    recommended_version = version.parse("5.0.0")
    
    print(f"Minimum required: {min_version}")
    print(f"Maximum supported: {max_version}")
    print(f"Recommended: {recommended_version}")
    print()
    
    # Check version compatibility
    print("Compatibility check:")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    is_compatible = True
    warnings = []
    
    if current_parsed < min_version:
        print(f"  ✗ Version too old: {current_version} < {min_version}")
        is_compatible = False
    else:
        print(f"  ✓ Meets minimum version requirement")
    
    if current_parsed >= max_version:
        print(f"  ✗ Version too new: {current_version} >= {max_version}")
        is_compatible = False
    else:
        print(f"  ✓ Below maximum version")
    
    # Check for deprecated features
    if current_parsed.major < 5:
        warnings.append("Using Django < 5.0: Some modern features unavailable")
        print(f"  ⚠ {warnings[-1]}")
    
    # Check for known issues with specific versions
    known_issues = {
        "4.2.7": "Known bug with QuerySet annotations",
        "4.2.8": "Performance regression in migrations",
    }
    
    if current_version in known_issues:
        issue = known_issues[current_version]
        warnings.append(f"Known issue in {current_version}: {issue}")
        print(f"  ⚠ {warnings[-1]}")
    
    print()
    
    # Exit if incompatible
    if not is_compatible:
        print(f"{'='*70}")
        print("CRITICAL: Django version incompatible")
        print(f"{'='*70}")
        print(f"\nYour Django version ({current_version}) is not compatible.")
        print(f"Required: {min_version} <= version < {max_version}")
        print(f"\nTo fix this:")
        print(f"  pip install 'Django>={min_version},<{max_version}'")
        
        pytest.exit(
            f"Django version {current_version} is incompatible. "
            f"Required: {min_version} <= version < {max_version}",
            returncode=2
        )
    
    # Display warnings
    if warnings:
        print(f"Warnings ({len(warnings)}):")
        for warn in warnings:
            print(f"  - {warn}")
        print()
    
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print(f"Django version {current_version} is compatible")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 5: Complete System Readiness Check

Comprehensive pre-flight validation before test execution.

# conftest.py
import pytest
import os
import sys
from django.db import connection
from django.conf import settings
import django

def pytest_sessionstart(session):
    """Comprehensive system readiness check"""
    print(f"\n{'='*80}")
    print("SYSTEM READINESS CHECK")
    print(f"{'='*80}\n")
    
    checks_passed = []
    checks_failed = []
    checks_warnings = []
    
    # Check 1: Python version
    print("1. Python Version")
    print("-" * 80)
    python_version = sys.version_info
    print(f"   Version: {python_version.major}.{python_version.minor}.{python_version.micro}")
    
    if python_version < (3, 9):
        checks_failed.append(("Python Version", f"Python {python_version.major}.{python_version.minor} too old (need 3.9+)"))
        print("   Status: ✗ FAILED - Too old")
    else:
        checks_passed.append("Python Version")
        print("   Status: ✓ PASSED")
    print()
    
    # Check 2: Django version
    print("2. Django Version")
    print("-" * 80)
    django_version = django.get_version()
    print(f"   Version: {django_version}")
    
    if django.VERSION < (4, 2):
        checks_failed.append(("Django Version", f"Django {django_version} too old (need 4.2+)"))
        print("   Status: ✗ FAILED - Too old")
    else:
        checks_passed.append("Django Version")
        print("   Status: ✓ PASSED")
    print()
    
    # Check 3: Database connectivity
    print("3. Database Connectivity")
    print("-" * 80)
    try:
        with connection.cursor() as cursor:
            cursor.execute("SELECT 1")
        print(f"   Database: {connection.settings_dict['NAME']}")
        print(f"   Engine: {connection.settings_dict['ENGINE'].split('.')[-1]}")
        checks_passed.append("Database Connectivity")
        print("   Status: ✓ PASSED")
    except Exception as e:
        checks_failed.append(("Database Connectivity", str(e)))
        print(f"   Error: {e}")
        print("   Status: ✗ FAILED")
    print()
    
    # Check 4: Required Django apps
    print("4. Required Django Apps")
    print("-" * 80)
    required_apps = ['jobpost', 'django.contrib.auth', 'django.contrib.contenttypes']
    missing_apps = [app for app in required_apps if app not in settings.INSTALLED_APPS]
    
    if missing_apps:
        checks_failed.append(("Required Apps", f"Missing: {', '.join(missing_apps)}"))
        print(f"   Missing: {', '.join(missing_apps)}")
        print("   Status: ✗ FAILED")
    else:
        checks_passed.append("Required Django Apps")
        print(f"   All {len(required_apps)} required apps installed")
        print("   Status: ✓ PASSED")
    print()
    
    # Check 5: Database migrations
    print("5. Database Migrations")
    print("-" * 80)
    try:
        from django.db.migrations.executor import MigrationExecutor
        executor = MigrationExecutor(connection)
        plan = executor.migration_plan(executor.loader.graph.leaf_nodes())
        
        if plan:
            checks_warnings.append(("Migrations", f"{len(plan)} unapplied migrations"))
            print(f"   Unapplied migrations: {len(plan)}")
            print("   Status: ⚠ WARNING - Migrations pending")
        else:
            checks_passed.append("Database Migrations")
            print("   All migrations applied")
            print("   Status: ✓ PASSED")
    except Exception as e:
        checks_warnings.append(("Migrations", f"Cannot check: {e}"))
        print(f"   Error: {e}")
        print("   Status: ⚠ WARNING")
    print()
    
    # Check 6: File permissions
    print("6. File Permissions")
    print("-" * 80)
    test_paths = [
        (settings.MEDIA_ROOT, "MEDIA_ROOT"),
        (settings.BASE_DIR, "BASE_DIR"),
    ]
    
    permission_issues = []
    for path, name in test_paths:
        if os.path.exists(path):
            if os.access(path, os.W_OK):
                print(f"   ✓ {name}: writable")
            else:
                permission_issues.append(f"{name} not writable")
                print(f"   ✗ {name}: NOT writable")
        else:
            permission_issues.append(f"{name} doesn't exist")
            print(f"   ✗ {name}: doesn't exist")
    
    if permission_issues:
        checks_failed.append(("File Permissions", ', '.join(permission_issues)))
        print("   Status: ✗ FAILED")
    else:
        checks_passed.append("File Permissions")
        print("   Status: ✓ PASSED")
    print()
    
    # Summary
    print(f"{'='*80}")
    print("READINESS CHECK SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*80}")
    print(f"Passed:   {len(checks_passed)}")
    print(f"Failed:   {len(checks_failed)}")
    print(f"Warnings: {len(checks_warnings)}")
    print()
    
    if checks_failed:
        print("FAILED CHECKS:")
        for check_name, error in checks_failed:
            print(f"  ✗ {check_name}: {error}")
        print()
    
    if checks_warnings:
        print("WARNINGS:")
        for check_name, warning in checks_warnings:
            print(f"  ⚠ {check_name}: {warning}")
        print()
    
    # Exit if critical checks failed
    if checks_failed:
        print(f"{'='*80}")
        print("CRITICAL: System not ready for testing")
        print(f"{'='*80}")
        print(f"\n{len(checks_failed)} critical check(s) failed.")
        print("Fix these issues before running tests.")
        
        pytest.exit(
            f"System readiness check failed: {len(checks_failed)} critical issues. "
            f"First issue: {checks_failed[0][1]}",
            returncode=1
        )
    
    print(f"{'='*80}")
    print("System ready - proceeding with test execution")
    print(f"{'='*80}\n")

pytest.main()

Official Docs: pytest.main() Reference

Perform an in-process test run programmatically.

Full Description

The pytest.main() function allows you to invoke pytest programmatically from Python code, rather than from the command line. It returns an exit code (0 for success, non-zero for failures) and accepts the same arguments as the command-line interface. This is useful for integrating pytest into custom scripts, building test automation tools, creating test runners for IDEs, or embedding tests in applications.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.main() enables advanced testing workflows: creating custom test runners that execute JobPost tests with specific configurations, building CI/CD scripts that run different test suites (unit tests for Skills, integration tests for Author workflows), creating management commands that run tests programmatically, or developing testing dashboards that execute and monitor tests for Location and JobPost models.

Syntax

# Basic usage
pytest.main()

# With command-line arguments
pytest.main(['-v', 'tests/'])

# With specific options
pytest.main(['--tb=short', '-x', 'tests/test_jobpost.py'])

# With plugins
pytest.main(['-v'], plugins=[MyPlugin()])

# Capture return code
exit_code = pytest.main(['-v'])
if exit_code == 0:
    print("All tests passed!")

# Common patterns
pytest.main(['-v', '--tb=short', '-k', 'test_skills'])
pytest.main(['--collect-only'])  # Just collect, don't run
pytest.main(['-x', '--pdb'])     # Stop on first failure, enter debugger

Parameters Description

  • args (list of str, optional): Command-line arguments as a list of strings. Same as you would pass to pytest on the command line. If None, uses sys.argv. Examples: ['-v'], ['--tb=short'], ['tests/'], ['-k', 'test_name']
  • plugins (list, optional): List of plugin objects to register for this test run. Allows extending pytest with custom functionality without installing packages.

Return Value

  • Returns: int - Exit code from the test run
  • Exit codes:
    • 0: All tests passed
    • 1: Tests were collected and run but some failed
    • 2: Test execution was interrupted by the user
    • 3: Internal error occurred
    • 4: pytest command line usage error
    • 5: No tests were collected

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: Custom Test Runner Script

Create a custom script to run JobPost tests with specific configurations.

# run_jobpost_tests.py
import pytest
import sys
from pathlib import Path

def run_jobpost_tests():
    """Custom test runner for JobPost tests"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("JOBPOST TEST RUNNER")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Define test configuration
    test_dir = Path(__file__).parent / 'tests'
    
    print("Configuration:")
    print(f"  Test directory: {test_dir}")
    print(f"  Python version: {sys.version_info.major}.{sys.version_info.minor}")
    print()
    
    # Run different test suites
    test_suites = [
        {
            'name': 'JobPost Model Tests',
            'args': [
                str(test_dir / 'test_jobpost_models.py'),
                '-v',
                '--tb=short',
                '-k', 'test_jobpost',
            ]
        },
        {
            'name': 'JobPost API Tests',
            'args': [
                str(test_dir / 'test_jobpost_api.py'),
                '-v',
                '--tb=line',
            ]
        },
        {
            'name': 'JobPost Integration Tests',
            'args': [
                str(test_dir / 'test_jobpost_integration.py'),
                '-v',
                '-x',  # Stop on first failure
            ]
        },
    ]
    
    results = []
    
    for suite in test_suites:
        print(f"\nRunning: {suite['name']}")
        print("-" * 70)
        print(f"Arguments: {' '.join(suite['args'])}")
        print()
        
        # Run tests
        exit_code = pytest.main(suite['args'])
        
        results.append({
            'name': suite['name'],
            'exit_code': exit_code,
            'status': 'PASSED' if exit_code == 0 else 'FAILED'
        })
        
        print(f"\nResult: {results[-1]['status']} (exit code: {exit_code})")
        print()
    
    # Summary
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print("TEST SUITE SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    passed = sum(1 for r in results if r['exit_code'] == 0)
    failed = len(results) - passed
    
    print(f"Total suites: {len(results)}")
    print(f"Passed: {passed}")
    print(f"Failed: {failed}")
    print()
    
    print("Details:")
    for result in results:
        status_symbol = '✓' if result['exit_code'] == 0 else '✗'
        print(f"  {status_symbol} {result['name']}: {result['status']}")
    
    print()
    
    # Overall result
    overall_exit_code = 0 if failed == 0 else 1
    print(f"Overall result: {'SUCCESS' if overall_exit_code == 0 else 'FAILURE'}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    return overall_exit_code

if __name__ == '__main__':
    exit_code = run_jobpost_tests()
    sys.exit(exit_code)

Example 2: Django Management Command for Testing

Create a Django management command that runs tests programmatically.

# anihpj/management/commands/runtests.py
import pytest
from django.core.management.base import BaseCommand
from django.conf import settings

class Command(BaseCommand):
    help = 'Run pytest tests programmatically with custom options'

    def add_arguments(self, parser):
        parser.add_argument(
            '--model',
            type=str,
            help='Test specific model (jobpost, skills, author, location)',
        )
        parser.add_argument(
            '--verbose',
            action='store_true',
            help='Verbose output',
        )
        parser.add_argument(
            '--coverage',
            action='store_true',
            help='Run with coverage report',
        )
        parser.add_argument(
            '--fast',
            action='store_true',
            help='Skip slow tests',
        )

    def handle(self, *args, **options):
        self.stdout.write(f"\n{'='*70}")
        self.stdout.write("ANIHPJ PROJECT TEST RUNNER")
        self.stdout.write(f"{'='*70}\n")
        
        # Build pytest arguments
        pytest_args = []
        
        # Model-specific tests
        if options['model']:
            model = options['model'].lower()
            test_file = f'tests/test_{model}.py'
            pytest_args.append(test_file)
            self.stdout.write(f"Testing model: {model}")
        else:
            pytest_args.append('tests/')
            self.stdout.write("Testing all models")
        
        # Verbosity
        if options['verbose']:
            pytest_args.extend(['-v', '-s'])
            self.stdout.write("Verbose mode: ON")
        else:
            pytest_args.append('-q')
            self.stdout.write("Verbose mode: OFF")
        
        # Coverage
        if options['coverage']:
            pytest_args.extend([
                '--cov=jobpost',
                '--cov-report=html',
                '--cov-report=term'
            ])
            self.stdout.write("Coverage: ON")
        
        # Fast mode (skip slow tests)
        if options['fast']:
            pytest_args.extend(['-m', 'not slow'])
            self.stdout.write("Fast mode: ON (skipping slow tests)")
        
        self.stdout.write(f"\nPytest arguments: {' '.join(pytest_args)}\n")
        
        # Run tests
        self.stdout.write("-" * 70)
        exit_code = pytest.main(pytest_args)
        self.stdout.write("-" * 70)
        
        # Report results
        self.stdout.write(f"\n{'='*70}")
        if exit_code == 0:
            self.stdout.write(self.style.SUCCESS('✓ All tests passed!'))
        elif exit_code == 1:
            self.stdout.write(self.style.ERROR('✗ Some tests failed'))
        elif exit_code == 5:
            self.stdout.write(self.style.WARNING('⚠ No tests collected'))
        else:
            self.stdout.write(self.style.ERROR(f'✗ Error (exit code: {exit_code})'))
        
        self.stdout.write(f"{'='*70}\n")
        
        return exit_code

Example 3: Continuous Integration Script

Build a CI/CD script that runs different test stages.

# ci_test_runner.py
import pytest
import sys
from datetime import datetime

def run_ci_tests():
    """Run tests in CI/CD pipeline with multiple stages"""
    print(f"\n{'='*80}")
    print("CI/CD TEST PIPELINE")
    print(f"Started: {datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S')}")
    print(f"{'='*80}\n")
    
    stages = [
        {
            'name': 'Stage 1: Unit Tests (Fast)',
            'args': [
                'tests/',
                '-m', 'unit',
                '-v',
                '--tb=line',
                '--durations=5',
            ],
            'critical': True,
        },
        {
            'name': 'Stage 2: Integration Tests',
            'args': [
                'tests/',
                '-m', 'integration',
                '-v',
                '--tb=short',
            ],
            'critical': True,
        },
        {
            'name': 'Stage 3: End-to-End Tests',
            'args': [
                'tests/',
                '-m', 'e2e',
                '-v',
                '--tb=long',
            ],
            'critical': False,  # Non-blocking
        },
        {
            'name': 'Stage 4: Performance Tests',
            'args': [
                'tests/',
                '-m', 'performance',
                '-v',
                '--durations=0',
            ],
            'critical': False,  # Non-blocking
        },
        {
            'name': 'Stage 5: Coverage Report',
            'args': [
                'tests/',
                '--cov=jobpost',
                '--cov=anihpj',
                '--cov-report=html',
                '--cov-report=term',
                '--cov-fail-under=80',
            ],
            'critical': True,
        },
    ]
    
    results = []
    failed_stages = []
    
    for i, stage in enumerate(stages, 1):
        print(f"\n{'='*80}")
        print(f"{stage['name']}")
        print(f"Critical: {'Yes' if stage['critical'] else 'No'}")
        print(f"{'='*80}")
        print(f"Arguments: {' '.join(stage['args'])}")
        print()
        
        start_time = datetime.now()
        
        # Run stage
        exit_code = pytest.main(stage['args'])
        
        end_time = datetime.now()
        duration = (end_time - start_time).total_seconds()
        
        result = {
            'stage': i,
            'name': stage['name'],
            'exit_code': exit_code,
            'duration': duration,
            'critical': stage['critical'],
            'status': 'PASSED' if exit_code == 0 else 'FAILED',
        }
        results.append(result)
        
        print(f"\nStage {i} result: {result['status']}")
        print(f"Duration: {duration:.2f}s")
        print(f"Exit code: {exit_code}")
        
        # Track failures
        if exit_code != 0:
            failed_stages.append(result)
            
            # Stop on critical failure
            if stage['critical']:
                print(f"\n{'='*80}")
                print(f"CRITICAL FAILURE IN STAGE {i}")
                print(f"Stopping pipeline")
                print(f"{'='*80}")
                break
            else:
                print(f"\nNon-critical failure - continuing...")
    
    # Final summary
    print(f"\n{'='*80}")
    print("CI/CD PIPELINE SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*80}\n")
    
    total_duration = sum(r['duration'] for r in results)
    passed = sum(1 for r in results if r['exit_code'] == 0)
    failed = len(results) - passed
    
    print(f"Completed: {datetime.now().strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S')}")
    print(f"Total duration: {total_duration:.2f}s")
    print(f"Stages run: {len(results)}/{len(stages)}")
    print(f"Passed: {passed}")
    print(f"Failed: {failed}")
    print()
    
    print("Stage Results:")
    for result in results:
        symbol = '✓' if result['exit_code'] == 0 else '✗'
        critical_flag = ' [CRITICAL]' if result['critical'] else ''
        print(f"  {symbol} Stage {result['stage']}: {result['name']}{critical_flag}")
        print(f"     Status: {result['status']}, Duration: {result['duration']:.2f}s")
    
    if failed_stages:
        print(f"\nFailed Stages ({len(failed_stages)}):")
        for result in failed_stages:
            critical_flag = ' [CRITICAL]' if result['critical'] else ''
            print(f"  ✗ Stage {result['stage']}: {result['name']}{critical_flag}")
    
    print()
    
    # Overall result
    critical_failures = sum(1 for r in failed_stages if r['critical'])
    
    if critical_failures > 0:
        print(f"Pipeline result: ✗ FAILED ({critical_failures} critical failure(s))")
        overall_exit_code = 1
    elif failed:
        print(f"Pipeline result: ⚠ PASSED WITH WARNINGS ({failed} non-critical failure(s))")
        overall_exit_code = 0
    else:
        print(f"Pipeline result: ✓ SUCCESS")
        overall_exit_code = 0
    
    print(f"{'='*80}\n")
    
    return overall_exit_code

if __name__ == '__main__':
    exit_code = run_ci_tests()
    sys.exit(exit_code)

Example 4: Interactive Test Dashboard

Create an interactive script to run specific test categories.

# test_dashboard.py
import pytest
import sys

def display_menu():
    """Display test categories menu"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("ANIHPJ TEST DASHBOARD")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print("Select test category to run:\n")
    print("  1. Skills Tests")
    print("  2. Author Tests")
    print("  3. Location Tests")
    print("  4. JobPost Tests")
    print("  5. Complete Integration Tests")
    print("  6. Quick Smoke Tests")
    print("  7. Full Test Suite")
    print("  8. Custom Test Pattern")
    print("  0. Exit")
    print()

def run_skills_tests():
    """Run Skills model tests"""
    print("\nRunning Skills Tests...")
    args = [
        'tests/test_skills.py',
        '-v',
        '--tb=short',
    ]
    return pytest.main(args)

def run_author_tests():
    """Run Author model tests"""
    print("\nRunning Author Tests...")
    args = [
        'tests/test_author.py',
        '-v',
        '--tb=short',
    ]
    return pytest.main(args)

def run_location_tests():
    """Run Location model tests"""
    print("\nRunning Location Tests...")
    args = [
        'tests/test_location.py',
        '-v',
        '--tb=short',
    ]
    return pytest.main(args)

def run_jobpost_tests():
    """Run JobPost model tests"""
    print("\nRunning JobPost Tests...")
    args = [
        'tests/test_jobpost.py',
        '-v',
        '--tb=short',
    ]
    return pytest.main(args)

def run_integration_tests():
    """Run complete integration tests"""
    print("\nRunning Complete Integration Tests...")
    args = [
        'tests/',
        '-m', 'integration',
        '-v',
        '--tb=long',
    ]
    return pytest.main(args)

def run_smoke_tests():
    """Run quick smoke tests"""
    print("\nRunning Quick Smoke Tests...")
    args = [
        'tests/',
        '-m', 'smoke',
        '-v',
        '-x',  # Stop on first failure
    ]
    return pytest.main(args)

def run_full_suite():
    """Run complete test suite"""
    print("\nRunning Full Test Suite...")
    args = [
        'tests/',
        '-v',
        '--cov=jobpost',
        '--cov-report=term',
    ]
    return pytest.main(args)

def run_custom_pattern():
    """Run tests matching custom pattern"""
    pattern = input("\nEnter test pattern (e.g., 'test_create'): ")
    print(f"\nRunning tests matching: {pattern}")
    args = [
        'tests/',
        '-k', pattern,
        '-v',
    ]
    return pytest.main(args)

def main():
    """Main dashboard loop"""
    test_functions = {
        '1': run_skills_tests,
        '2': run_author_tests,
        '3': run_location_tests,
        '4': run_jobpost_tests,
        '5': run_integration_tests,
        '6': run_smoke_tests,
        '7': run_full_suite,
        '8': run_custom_pattern,
    }
    
    while True:
        display_menu()
        
        choice = input("Enter your choice (0-8): ").strip()
        
        if choice == '0':
            print("\nExiting test dashboard. Goodbye!")
            sys.exit(0)
        
        if choice in test_functions:
            print(f"\n{'-'*70}")
            exit_code = test_functions[choice]()
            print(f"{'-'*70}")
            
            if exit_code == 0:
                print("\n✓ Tests PASSED")
            else:
                print(f"\n✗ Tests FAILED (exit code: {exit_code})")
            
            input("\nPress Enter to continue...")
        else:
            print("\n✗ Invalid choice. Please select 0-8.")
            input("\nPress Enter to continue...")

if __name__ == '__main__':
    try:
        main()
    except KeyboardInterrupt:
        print("\n\nInterrupted by user. Exiting...")
        sys.exit(0)

Example 5: Automated Test Report Generator

Generate detailed test reports with pytest.main() programmatically.

# generate_test_report.py
import pytest
import json
from datetime import datetime
from pathlib import Path

def generate_test_report():
    """Generate comprehensive test report"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST REPORT GENERATOR")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    timestamp = datetime.now().strftime('%Y%m%d_%H%M%S')
    report_dir = Path('test_reports') / timestamp
    report_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    
    print(f"Report directory: {report_dir}")
    print()
    
    # Test configurations
    test_runs = [
        {
            'name': 'Unit Tests',
            'args': [
                'tests/',
                '-m', 'unit',
                f'--html={report_dir}/unit_report.html',
                '--self-contained-html',
                f'--junit-xml={report_dir}/unit_results.xml',
            ]
        },
        {
            'name': 'Integration Tests',
            'args': [
                'tests/',
                '-m', 'integration',
                f'--html={report_dir}/integration_report.html',
                '--self-contained-html',
                f'--junit-xml={report_dir}/integration_results.xml',
            ]
        },
        {
            'name': 'All Tests with Coverage',
            'args': [
                'tests/',
                '--cov=jobpost',
                '--cov=anihpj',
                f'--cov-report=html:{report_dir}/coverage',
                '--cov-report=json:{}/coverage.json'.format(report_dir),
                f'--html={report_dir}/full_report.html',
                '--self-contained-html',
                f'--junit-xml={report_dir}/full_results.xml',
            ]
        },
    ]
    
    results = []
    
    for run_config in test_runs:
        print(f"\n{'='*70}")
        print(f"Running: {run_config['name']}")
        print(f"{'='*70}")
        
        start_time = datetime.now()
        exit_code = pytest.main(run_config['args'])
        end_time = datetime.now()
        
        duration = (end_time - start_time).total_seconds()
        
        result = {
            'name': run_config['name'],
            'exit_code': exit_code,
            'status': 'PASSED' if exit_code == 0 else 'FAILED',
            'start_time': start_time.isoformat(),
            'end_time': end_time.isoformat(),
            'duration_seconds': duration,
        }
        results.append(result)
        
        print(f"\nResult: {result['status']}")
        print(f"Duration: {duration:.2f}s")
    
    # Generate summary JSON
    summary = {
        'generated_at': datetime.now().isoformat(),
        'report_directory': str(report_dir),
        'total_runs': len(results),
        'passed': sum(1 for r in results if r['exit_code'] == 0),
        'failed': sum(1 for r in results if r['exit_code'] != 0),
        'total_duration': sum(r['duration_seconds'] for r in results),
        'results': results,
    }
    
    summary_file = report_dir / 'summary.json'
    with open(summary_file, 'w') as f:
        json.dump(summary, f, indent=2)
    
    # Generate text summary
    summary_text = report_dir / 'summary.txt'
    with open(summary_text, 'w') as f:
        f.write("="*70 + "\n")
        f.write("TEST EXECUTION SUMMARY\n")
        f.write("="*70 + "\n\n")
        f.write(f"Generated: {summary['generated_at']}\n")
        f.write(f"Report Directory: {summary['report_directory']}\n\n")
        f.write(f"Total Test Runs: {summary['total_runs']}\n")
        f.write(f"Passed: {summary['passed']}\n")
        f.write(f"Failed: {summary['failed']}\n")
        f.write(f"Total Duration: {summary['total_duration']:.2f}s\n\n")
        f.write("="*70 + "\n")
        f.write("DETAILED RESULTS\n")
        f.write("="*70 + "\n\n")
        
        for result in results:
            f.write(f"Test Run: {result['name']}\n")
            f.write(f"  Status: {result['status']}\n")
            f.write(f"  Exit Code: {result['exit_code']}\n")
            f.write(f"  Duration: {result['duration_seconds']:.2f}s\n")
            f.write(f"  Start: {result['start_time']}\n")
            f.write(f"  End: {result['end_time']}\n")
            f.write("\n")
    
    # Print final summary
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("REPORT GENERATION COMPLETE")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print(f"Generated reports:")
    print(f"  Location: {report_dir}")
    print(f"  HTML Reports: {len(test_runs)}")
    print(f"  XML Reports: {len(test_runs)}")
    print(f"  Coverage Report: Yes")
    print(f"  Summary JSON: {summary_file}")
    print(f"  Summary Text: {summary_text}")
    print()
    
    print(f"Test Results:")
    print(f"  Total runs: {summary['total_runs']}")
    print(f"  Passed: {summary['passed']}")
    print(f"  Failed: {summary['failed']}")
    print(f"  Total duration: {summary['total_duration']:.2f}s")
    print()
    
    overall_success = summary['failed'] == 0
    if overall_success:
        print("✓ All test runs PASSED")
        return 0
    else:
        print(f"✗ {summary['failed']} test run(s) FAILED")
        return 1

if __name__ == '__main__':
    exit_code = generate_test_report()
    sys.exit(exit_code)

pytest.param()

Official Docs: pytest.param() Reference

Specify parameter sets for parametrized tests with marks and ids.

Full Description

The pytest.param() function creates parameter sets for use with @pytest.mark.parametrize. It allows you to attach marks (like skip, xfail) to specific parameter combinations and provide custom IDs for better test identification. This gives fine-grained control over parametrized tests—you can skip certain parameter combinations, mark some as expected to fail, or provide descriptive names that make test output more readable.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.param() enhances parametrized testing: testing JobPost creation with multiple salary ranges while marking known edge cases as xfail, testing Author permissions with different user types while skipping admin scenarios in certain environments, validating Location data with various address formats while providing clear test IDs, or testing Skills matching with different algorithms while marking experimental ones as expected to fail.

Syntax

# Basic usage with values
pytest.param(value1, value2, value3)

# With ID for better test identification
pytest.param(value1, value2, id="descriptive-name")

# With marks (skip, xfail, etc.)
pytest.param(value1, value2, marks=pytest.mark.skip)
pytest.param(value1, value2, marks=pytest.mark.xfail)

# Multiple marks
pytest.param(value1, value2, marks=[pytest.mark.slow, pytest.mark.xfail])

# Combined ID and marks
pytest.param(value1, value2, id="edge-case", marks=pytest.mark.xfail)

# In parametrize decorator
@pytest.mark.parametrize("arg1,arg2", [
    pytest.param(1, 2, id="case-1"),
    pytest.param(3, 4, id="case-2"),
    pytest.param(5, 6, id="known-bug", marks=pytest.mark.xfail),
])

Parameters Description

  • *values: The actual parameter values to pass to the test function. Number of values must match the number of parameters in @pytest.mark.parametrize.
  • marks (mark or list of marks, optional): Pytest marks to apply to this specific parameter set. Can be a single mark (pytest.mark.skip) or a list of marks. Common marks: skip, skipif, xfail, slow, custom marks.
  • id (str, optional): Custom identifier for this parameter set, displayed in test output. Makes test results more readable than default parameter representation.

Return Value

  • Returns: ParameterSet object suitable for use with @pytest.mark.parametrize
  • Contains: Parameter values, marks, and optional ID
  • Usage: Pass to parametrize decorator's argvalues list

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: JobPost Salary Ranges with Edge Cases

Test JobPost creation with various salary ranges, marking edge cases.

# tests/test_jobpost_salary_param.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Author, Location, JobPost, Skills

@pytest.mark.parametrize("title,salary,expected_category,test_type", [
    pytest.param(
        "Intern Position",
        30000,
        "entry",
        "standard",
        id="entry-level-intern"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Junior Developer",
        65000,
        "junior",
        "standard",
        id="junior-developer"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Senior Engineer",
        135000,
        "senior",
        "standard",
        id="senior-engineer"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Staff Engineer",
        200000,
        "staff",
        "standard",
        id="staff-engineer"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Principal Engineer",
        350000,
        "principal",
        "standard",
        id="principal-engineer"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Edge Case: Zero",
        0,
        "invalid",
        "edge",
        id="zero-salary-known-bug",
        marks=pytest.mark.xfail(reason="Zero salary validation not implemented")
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Edge Case: Negative",
        -50000,
        "invalid",
        "edge",
        id="negative-salary-known-bug",
        marks=pytest.mark.xfail(reason="Negative salary validation not implemented")
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Edge Case: Extreme High",
        10000000,
        "executive",
        "edge",
        id="extreme-high-salary",
        marks=pytest.mark.slow
    ),
])
def test_jobpost_salary_categories(title, salary, expected_category, test_type):
    """Test JobPost creation with various salary ranges"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print(f"TEST: {title}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Setup
    user = User.objects.create_user(username=f'user_sal_{salary}', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Test Corp',
        designation='Recruiter'
    )
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1 Test St',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    skill = Skills.objects.create(name=f'Skill_{salary}')
    
    print(f"Test Type: {test_type.upper()}")
    print(f"Expected Category: {expected_category}")
    print(f"Salary: ${salary:,}")
    print()
    
    # Create JobPost
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title=title,
        description=f'Position with ${salary:,} salary',
        expiry=timezone.now().date(),
        salary=salary,
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    job.skills.add(skill)
    
    print(f"JobPost created:")
    print(f"  ID: {job.id}")
    print(f"  Title: {job.title}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${job.salary:,}")
    print(f"  Author: {job.author.user.username}")
    print(f"  Location: {job.location.city}, {job.location.state}")
    print(f"  Skills: {', '.join(s.name for s in job.skills.all())}")
    print()
    
    # Categorize salary
    if salary < 0:
        actual_category = "invalid"
    elif salary == 0:
        actual_category = "invalid"
    elif salary < 50000:
        actual_category = "entry"
    elif salary < 100000:
        actual_category = "junior"
    elif salary < 150000:
        actual_category = "senior"
    elif salary < 250000:
        actual_category = "staff"
    else:
        actual_category = "principal"
    
    print(f"Salary categorization:")
    print(f"  Expected: {expected_category}")
    print(f"  Actual: {actual_category}")
    print()
    
    # Validation
    if test_type == "edge" and salary <= 0:
        # For edge cases with invalid salary, should raise error
        # But due to known bug, it doesn't
        assert job.salary <= 0, "Invalid salary accepted (known bug)"
    else:
        assert actual_category == expected_category, f"Category mismatch: {actual_category} != {expected_category}"
    
    print(f"✓ Test passed for category: {expected_category}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 2: Author Permission Levels with Platform-Specific Skips

Test Author permissions, skipping certain scenarios based on environment.

# tests/test_author_permissions_param.py
import pytest
import sys
import os
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author

@pytest.mark.parametrize("username,company,designation,permission_level,can_post_high_salary", [
    pytest.param(
        "intern_recruiter",
        "TechCorp",
        "Intern Recruiter",
        1,
        False,
        id="level-1-intern"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "junior_recruiter",
        "TechCorp",
        "Junior Recruiter",
        2,
        False,
        id="level-2-junior"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "senior_recruiter",
        "TechCorp",
        "Senior Recruiter",
        3,
        True,
        id="level-3-senior"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "lead_recruiter",
        "TechCorp",
        "Lead Recruiter",
        4,
        True,
        id="level-4-lead"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "manager",
        "TechCorp",
        "Hiring Manager",
        5,
        True,
        id="level-5-manager"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "admin_user",
        "TechCorp",
        "Administrator",
        10,
        True,
        id="level-10-admin",
        marks=pytest.mark.skipif(
            sys.platform == 'win32',
            reason="Admin tests not supported on Windows"
        )
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "super_admin",
        "TechCorp",
        "Super Administrator",
        99,
        True,
        id="level-99-superadmin",
        marks=[
            pytest.mark.skipif(
                os.environ.get('CI') == 'true',
                reason="Super admin not available in CI"
            ),
            pytest.mark.slow
        ]
    ),
])
def test_author_permission_levels(username, company, designation, permission_level, can_post_high_salary):
    """Test Author creation with different permission levels"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print(f"TEST: {designation} (Level {permission_level})")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create user and author
    user = User.objects.create_user(
        username=username,
        email=f'{username}@techcorp.com',
        password='test123'
    )
    
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company=company,
        designation=designation
    )
    
    # Simulate permission level (not in actual model)
    author._permission_level = permission_level
    author._can_post_high_salary = can_post_high_salary
    
    print(f"Author created:")
    print(f"  Username: {user.username}")
    print(f"  Company: {company}")
    print(f"  Designation: {designation}")
    print(f"  Permission Level: {permission_level}")
    print(f"  Email: {user.email}")
    print()
    
    print(f"Permissions:")
    print(f"  Can post high salary jobs: {can_post_high_salary}")
    print(f"  Can edit own posts: {permission_level >= 1}")
    print(f"  Can edit team posts: {permission_level >= 3}")
    print(f"  Can edit all posts: {permission_level >= 5}")
    print(f"  Has admin access: {permission_level >= 10}")
    print()
    
    # Validate author
    assert author.user.username == username
    assert author.company == company
    assert author.designation == designation
    assert author._permission_level == permission_level
    assert author._can_post_high_salary == can_post_high_salary
    
    # Check permission-based access
    if permission_level >= 3:
        print(f"✓ Senior level access granted")
    if permission_level >= 10:
        print(f"✓ Admin level access granted")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Test passed for {designation}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 3: Location Address Formats with Descriptive IDs

Test Location creation with various address formats using clear IDs.

# tests/test_location_formats_param.py
import pytest
from jobpost.models import Location

@pytest.mark.parametrize("street,city,state,country,zip_code,format_type", [
    pytest.param(
        "123 Main Street",
        "New York",
        "NY",
        "USA",
        "10001",
        "standard-us",
        id="US-standard-format"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Apt 4B, 456 Oak Avenue",
        "Los Angeles",
        "CA",
        "USA",
        "90001",
        "apartment",
        id="US-apartment-format"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Suite 200, 789 Corporate Blvd",
        "Chicago",
        "IL",
        "USA",
        "60601",
        "commercial",
        id="US-commercial-suite"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Building 5, Floor 10, 321 Tech Park",
        "Austin",
        "TX",
        "USA",
        "78701",
        "tech-campus",
        id="US-tech-campus-complex"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "PO Box 1234",
        "Seattle",
        "WA",
        "USA",
        "98101",
        "po-box",
        id="US-po-box-format"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "1 Hacker Way",
        "Menlo Park",
        "CA",
        "USA",
        "94025",
        "famous",
        id="Famous-Facebook-HQ"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "1600 Amphitheatre Parkway",
        "Mountain View",
        "CA",
        "USA",
        "94043",
        "famous",
        id="Famous-Google-HQ"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "",  # Empty street
        "Boston",
        "MA",
        "USA",
        "02101",
        "invalid",
        id="Empty-street-validation-bug",
        marks=pytest.mark.xfail(reason="Empty street validation not implemented")
    ),
])
def test_location_address_formats(street, city, state, country, zip_code, format_type):
    """Test Location creation with various address formats"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print(f"TEST: {format_type.upper()} FORMAT")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create location
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street=street,
        city=city,
        state=state,
        country=country,
        zip=zip_code
    )
    
    print(f"Location created:")
    print(f"  ID: {location.id}")
    print(f"  Street: {street or '[EMPTY]'}")
    print(f"  City: {city}")
    print(f"  State: {state}")
    print(f"  Country: {country}")
    print(f"  ZIP: {zip_code}")
    print(f"  Format Type: {format_type}")
    print()
    
    # Format full address
    full_address = f"{street}, {city}, {state} {zip_code}, {country}"
    print(f"Full Address: {full_address}")
    print()
    
    # Validate based on format type
    if format_type == "standard-us":
        assert len(street) > 0, "Street should not be empty"
        assert len(city) > 0, "City should not be empty"
        assert len(state) == 2, "State should be 2 characters"
        assert len(zip_code) == 5, "ZIP should be 5 digits"
        print(f"✓ Standard US format validated")
    
    elif format_type == "apartment":
        assert "Apt" in street or "Unit" in street, "Should contain apartment indicator"
        print(f"✓ Apartment format validated")
    
    elif format_type == "commercial":
        assert "Suite" in street or "Floor" in street or "Office" in street, "Should contain commercial indicator"
        print(f"✓ Commercial format validated")
    
    elif format_type == "tech-campus":
        assert "Building" in street or "Campus" in street or "Park" in street, "Should contain campus indicator"
        print(f"✓ Tech campus format validated")
    
    elif format_type == "po-box":
        assert "PO Box" in street or "P.O. Box" in street, "Should be PO Box format"
        print(f"✓ PO Box format validated")
    
    elif format_type == "famous":
        print(f"✓ Famous location format")
    
    elif format_type == "invalid":
        # Should fail validation but doesn't (known bug)
        assert len(street) == 0, "Empty street accepted (known bug)"
        print(f"✓ Invalid format accepted (known bug)")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Test completed for {format_type} format")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 4: Skills Matching Algorithms with Experimental Marks

Test different Skills matching algorithms, marking experimental ones as xfail.

# tests/test_skills_algorithms_param.py
import pytest
from jobpost.models import Skills

@pytest.mark.parametrize("skill_name,algorithm,match_threshold,is_experimental", [
    pytest.param(
        "Python",
        "exact",
        1.0,
        False,
        id="Algorithm-ExactMatch-Stable"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "JavaScript",
        "case-insensitive",
        0.9,
        False,
        id="Algorithm-CaseInsensitive-Stable"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Machine Learning",
        "fuzzy",
        0.8,
        False,
        id="Algorithm-Fuzzy-Stable"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "React.js",
        "semantic",
        0.7,
        True,
        id="Algorithm-Semantic-Experimental",
        marks=pytest.mark.xfail(reason="Semantic matching under development")
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "AI/ML",
        "nlp-based",
        0.75,
        True,
        id="Algorithm-NLP-Experimental",
        marks=[
            pytest.mark.xfail(reason="NLP matching experimental"),
            pytest.mark.slow
        ]
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Full Stack",
        "context-aware",
        0.85,
        True,
        id="Algorithm-ContextAware-Experimental",
        marks=pytest.mark.xfail(reason="Context-aware matching in beta")
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "DevOps",
        "graph-based",
        0.6,
        True,
        id="Algorithm-GraphBased-Experimental",
        marks=[
            pytest.mark.xfail(reason="Graph-based matching prototype"),
            pytest.mark.slow
        ]
    ),
])
def test_skills_matching_algorithms(skill_name, algorithm, match_threshold, is_experimental):
    """Test different skills matching algorithms"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print(f"TEST: {skill_name} - {algorithm.upper()} ALGORITHM")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create skill
    skill = Skills.objects.create(name=skill_name)
    
    print(f"Skill created:")
    print(f"  ID: {skill.id}")
    print(f"  Name: {skill_name}")
    print()
    
    print(f"Algorithm configuration:")
    print(f"  Algorithm: {algorithm}")
    print(f"  Match Threshold: {match_threshold}")
    print(f"  Status: {'EXPERIMENTAL' if is_experimental else 'STABLE'}")
    print()
    
    # Test data for matching
    test_inputs = [
        skill_name,  # Exact match
        skill_name.lower(),  # Lowercase
        skill_name.upper(),  # Uppercase
        skill_name.replace(' ', ''),  # No spaces
    ]
    
    print(f"Testing {algorithm} matching:")
    print("-" * 70)
    
    matches = []
    for test_input in test_inputs:
        # Simulate matching based on algorithm
        if algorithm == "exact":
            score = 1.0 if test_input == skill_name else 0.0
        elif algorithm == "case-insensitive":
            score = 1.0 if test_input.lower() == skill_name.lower() else 0.0
        elif algorithm == "fuzzy":
            # Simplified fuzzy matching
            score = len(set(test_input.lower()) & set(skill_name.lower())) / max(len(test_input), len(skill_name))
        elif algorithm in ["semantic", "nlp-based", "context-aware", "graph-based"]:
            # Experimental algorithms - not fully implemented
            score = 0.5  # Placeholder
        else:
            score = 0.0
        
        is_match = score >= match_threshold
        matches.append((test_input, score, is_match))
        
        match_symbol = '✓' if is_match else '✗'
        print(f"  {match_symbol} Input: '{test_input}'")
        print(f"     Score: {score:.2f} (threshold: {match_threshold})")
        print(f"     Match: {is_match}")
    
    print()
    
    # Validation
    total_matches = sum(1 for _, _, is_match in matches if is_match)
    print(f"Results:")
    print(f"  Total tests: {len(test_inputs)}")
    print(f"  Matches: {total_matches}")
    print(f"  Match rate: {total_matches/len(test_inputs)*100:.1f}%")
    print()
    
    if is_experimental:
        # Experimental algorithms - expect at least some functionality
        print(f"⚠ Experimental algorithm - results may vary")
        assert total_matches >= 0, "Experimental algorithm should run without crashing"
    else:
        # Stable algorithms - should match appropriately
        if algorithm == "exact":
            assert total_matches >= 1, "Should match exact input"
        elif algorithm in ["case-insensitive", "fuzzy"]:
            assert total_matches >= 2, "Should match multiple variants"
    
    print(f"✓ Test completed for {algorithm} algorithm")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 5: Complete Integration with Multiple pytest.param Features

Comprehensive test using all pytest.param features together.

# tests/test_complete_param_integration.py
import pytest
import sys
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

@pytest.mark.parametrize("scenario,user_data,job_data,expected_status,special_handling", [
    pytest.param(
        "Standard job posting",
        {"username": "user1", "email": "user1@test.com"},
        {"title": "Python Developer", "salary": 100000, "skills": ["Python", "Django"]},
        "active",
        None,
        id="Scenario-1-Standard-Success"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "High salary position",
        {"username": "user2", "email": "user2@test.com"},
        {"title": "Senior Architect", "salary": 250000, "skills": ["Architecture", "Leadership"]},
        "active",
        None,
        id="Scenario-2-HighSalary-Success"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Multiple skills required",
        {"username": "user3", "email": "user3@test.com"},
        {"title": "Full Stack Engineer", "salary": 130000, "skills": ["Python", "JavaScript", "React", "Django", "PostgreSQL"]},
        "active",
        None,
        id="Scenario-3-MultiSkill-Success"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Entry level position",
        {"username": "user4", "email": "user4@test.com"},
        {"title": "Junior Developer", "salary": 60000, "skills": ["Python"]},
        "active",
        None,
        id="Scenario-4-EntryLevel-Success"
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Zero salary bug",
        {"username": "user5", "email": "user5@test.com"},
        {"title": "Volunteer Position", "salary": 0, "skills": ["Any"]},
        "invalid",
        "known_bug",
        id="Scenario-5-ZeroSalary-KnownBug",
        marks=pytest.mark.xfail(reason="Zero salary validation not implemented")
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Negative salary bug",
        {"username": "user6", "email": "user6@test.com"},
        {"title": "Invalid Job", "salary": -50000, "skills": ["Test"]},
        "invalid",
        "known_bug",
        id="Scenario-6-NegativeSalary-KnownBug",
        marks=pytest.mark.xfail(reason="Negative salary validation not implemented")
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Admin-only high-value job",
        {"username": "admin", "email": "admin@test.com"},
        {"title": "C-Level Position", "salary": 500000, "skills": ["Executive", "Strategy"]},
        "active",
        "admin_required",
        id="Scenario-7-AdminOnly-Skip",
        marks=pytest.mark.skipif(
            sys.platform == 'win32',
            reason="Admin features not available on Windows"
        )
    ),
    pytest.param(
        "Performance test with many skills",
        {"username": "perf_user", "email": "perf@test.com"},
        {"title": "Unicorn Developer", "salary": 200000, "skills": [f"Skill{i}" for i in range(50)]},
        "active",
        "performance",
        id="Scenario-8-Performance-ManySkills",
        marks=[pytest.mark.slow, pytest.mark.performance]
    ),
])
def test_complete_job_posting_scenarios(scenario, user_data, job_data, expected_status, special_handling):
    """Comprehensive job posting test with multiple scenarios"""
    print(f"\n{'='*80}")
    print(f"SCENARIO: {scenario}")
    print(f"{'='*80}\n")
    
    # Display configuration
    print(f"Configuration:")
    print(f"  Expected Status: {expected_status}")
    if special_handling:
        print(f"  Special Handling: {special_handling}")
    print()
    
    # Create user
    user = User.objects.create_user(
        username=user_data["username"],
        email=user_data["email"],
        password='test123'
    )
    print(f"User created: {user.username} ({user.email})")
    
    # Create author
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Test Corp',
        designation='Recruiter'
    )
    print(f"Author created: {author.company} - {author.designation}")
    
    # Create location
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1 Test St',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    print(f"Location created: {location.city}, {location.state}")
    
    # Create skills
    skills = []
    for skill_name in job_data["skills"]:
        skill, created = Skills.objects.get_or_create(name=skill_name)
        skills.append(skill)
    print(f"Skills created: {len(skills)} skill(s)")
    
    print()
    
    # Create job post
    print(f"Creating JobPost:")
    print(f"  Title: {job_data['title']}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${job_data['salary']:,}")
    print(f"  Skills: {len(skills)}")
    
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title=job_data["title"],
        description=f"Test job for {scenario}",
        expiry=timezone.now().date(),
        salary=job_data["salary"],
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    job.skills.set(skills)
    
    print(f"\nJobPost created successfully:")
    print(f"  ID: {job.id}")
    print(f"  Title: {job.title}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${job.salary:,}")
    print(f"  Skills count: {job.skills.count()}")
    print(f"  Author: {job.author.user.username}")
    print(f"  Location: {job.location.city}")
    print()
    
    # Validate based on expected status
    if expected_status == "active":
        assert job.salary > 0, "Active job should have positive salary"
        assert job.skills.count() > 0, "Active job should have skills"
        print(f"✓ Job validation passed: ACTIVE status")
    elif expected_status == "invalid":
        # For known bugs - should be invalid but isn't
        if special_handling == "known_bug":
            assert job.salary <= 0, "Invalid salary accepted (known bug)"
            print(f"⚠ Invalid job accepted due to known bug")
    
    print()
    
    # Special handling
    if special_handling == "performance":
        print(f"Performance metrics:")
        print(f"  Skills attached: {job.skills.count()}")
        print(f"  Query time: ")
    elif special_handling == "admin_required":
        print(f"Admin-level job created")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Scenario completed: {scenario}")
    print(f"{'='*80}\n")
