pytest.raises()

Official Docs: pytest.raises() Reference

Assert that a code block raises a specific exception.

Full Description

The pytest.raises() context manager asserts that code raises a specific exception type. It captures the exception, allowing you to inspect its attributes (message, args, etc.) and make additional assertions. This is essential for testing error handling, input validation, and exceptional code paths. Unlike try/except which catches exceptions, pytest.raises() fails the test if the expected exception is NOT raised.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.raises() is invaluable for testing validation: verifying JobPost raises ValidationError for invalid salaries, testing Author raises IntegrityError for duplicate user assignments, ensuring Location raises ValidationError for invalid zip codes, validating Skills uniqueness constraints raise IntegrityError, and testing that API endpoints raise PermissionDenied for unauthorized access.

Syntax

# Basic usage
with pytest.raises(ValueError):
    raise ValueError("Invalid value")

# Capture exception for inspection
with pytest.raises(ValueError) as exc_info:
    raise ValueError("Invalid value")
assert "Invalid" in str(exc_info.value)

# Match exception message with regex
with pytest.raises(ValueError, match=r"Invalid.*value"):
    raise ValueError("Invalid value provided")

# Match exact message
with pytest.raises(ValueError, match="^Invalid value$"):
    raise ValueError("Invalid value")

# Multiple exception types
with pytest.raises((ValueError, TypeError)):
    might_raise_either()

# Test fails if exception NOT raised
with pytest.raises(ValueError):
    pass  # Test fails: ValueError not raised

Parameters Description

  • expected_exception (Exception class or tuple): Exception type(s) expected to be raised. Can be a single exception class (ValueError) or a tuple of exception classes ((ValueError, TypeError))
  • match (str or re.Pattern, optional): Regular expression pattern that the exception message should match. Test fails if exception is raised but message doesn't match the pattern.
  • message (str, optional): Custom failure message displayed if the expected exception is not raised. Deprecated in pytest 5.0+, use match parameter instead.

Attributes

  • exc_info.value: The raised exception instance. Access exception message via str(exc_info.value) or exc_info.value.args
  • exc_info.type: The exception class that was raised
  • exc_info.typename: String name of the exception class
  • exc_info.traceback: Traceback object for the exception

Return Value

  • Returns: ExceptionInfo object when used as context manager
  • Test passes: If expected exception is raised (and matches pattern if provided)
  • Test fails: If expected exception is NOT raised, or wrong exception raised, or message doesn't match pattern

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: JobPost Salary Validation

Test that JobPost raises ValidationError for invalid salaries.

# tests/test_jobpost_validation.py
import pytest
from django.core.exceptions import ValidationError
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Author, Location, JobPost, Skills

def test_jobpost_negative_salary_raises_error():
    """Test that negative salary raises ValidationError"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: JobPost Negative Salary Validation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Setup
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='test_user', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Test Corp',
        designation='Recruiter'
    )
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1 Test St',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    print("Setup complete:")
    print(f"  Author: {author.user.username}")
    print(f"  Location: {location.city}, {location.state}")
    print()
    
    print("Testing negative salary validation...")
    print("Expected: ValidationError with message about negative salary")
    print()
    
    # Test negative salary
    with pytest.raises(ValidationError, match=r".*negative.*salary.*") as exc_info:
        job = JobPost(
            title='Test Job',
            description='Test description',
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=-50000,  # Negative salary
            type='Full Time',
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        job.full_clean()  # Trigger validation
    
    print(f"✓ ValidationError raised as expected")
    print(f"Exception type: {exc_info.typename}")
    print(f"Exception message: {str(exc_info.value)}")
    print()
    
    # Verify exception details
    assert exc_info.type == ValidationError
    assert "salary" in str(exc_info.value).lower()
    
    print(f"✓ Exception details verified")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")


def test_jobpost_zero_salary_raises_error():
    """Test that zero salary raises ValidationError"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: JobPost Zero Salary Validation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='test_user2', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Test Corp',
        designation='Recruiter'
    )
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='2 Test St',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    print("Testing zero salary validation...")
    
    with pytest.raises(ValidationError) as exc_info:
        job = JobPost(
            title='Volunteer Position',
            description='No pay',
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=0,  # Zero salary
            type='Full Time',
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        job.full_clean()
    
    print(f"✓ ValidationError raised for zero salary")
    print(f"Exception message: {str(exc_info.value)}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")


def test_jobpost_expired_date_raises_error():
    """Test that past expiry date raises ValidationError"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: JobPost Past Expiry Date Validation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    from datetime import timedelta
    
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='test_user3', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Test Corp',
        designation='Recruiter'
    )
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='3 Test St',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    past_date = timezone.now().date() - timedelta(days=30)
    
    print(f"Current date: {timezone.now().date()}")
    print(f"Expiry date (past): {past_date}")
    print()
    
    with pytest.raises(ValidationError, match=r".*expiry.*past.*") as exc_info:
        job = JobPost(
            title='Expired Job',
            description='This job expired',
            expiry=past_date,  # Past date
            salary=100000,
            type='Full Time',
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        job.full_clean()
    
    print(f"✓ ValidationError raised for past expiry date")
    print(f"Exception: {str(exc_info.value)}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 2: Author Duplicate User IntegrityError

Test that Author raises IntegrityError for duplicate user assignment.

# tests/test_author_integrity.py
import pytest
from django.db import IntegrityError
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author

def test_author_duplicate_user_raises_error():
    """Test that duplicate user assignment raises IntegrityError"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Author Duplicate User IntegrityError")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create user and first author
    user = User.objects.create_user(
        username='unique_user',
        email='unique@test.com',
        password='test123'
    )
    
    author1 = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Company A',
        designation='Recruiter'
    )
    
    print(f"First author created:")
    print(f"  User: {author1.user.username}")
    print(f"  Company: {author1.company}")
    print(f"  Designation: {author1.designation}")
    print()
    
    print("Attempting to create second author with same user...")
    print("Expected: IntegrityError (OneToOneField constraint)")
    print()
    
    # Try to create second author with same user
    with pytest.raises(IntegrityError, match=r".*duplicate.*|.*unique.*") as exc_info:
        author2 = Author.objects.create(
            user=user,  # Same user - violates OneToOneField
            company='Company B',
            designation='Manager'
        )
    
    print(f"✓ IntegrityError raised as expected")
    print(f"Exception type: {exc_info.typename}")
    print(f"Exception message: {str(exc_info.value)}")
    print()
    
    # Verify only one author exists
    author_count = Author.objects.filter(user=user).count()
    print(f"Authors for user '{user.username}': {author_count}")
    assert author_count == 1, "Only one author should exist for user"
    
    print(f"\n✓ OneToOneField constraint enforced")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")


def test_author_empty_company_raises_error():
    """Test that empty company name raises ValidationError"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Author Empty Company Validation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    user = User.objects.create_user(
        username='company_test_user',
        password='test123'
    )
    
    print("Testing empty company validation...")
    
    with pytest.raises(ValidationError, match=r".*company.*required.*") as exc_info:
        author = Author(
            user=user,
            company='',  # Empty company
            designation='Recruiter'
        )
        author.full_clean()
    
    print(f"✓ ValidationError raised for empty company")
    print(f"Exception: {str(exc_info.value)}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")


def test_author_invalid_designation_raises_error():
    """Test that invalid designation raises ValidationError"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Author Invalid Designation Validation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    user = User.objects.create_user(
        username='designation_test_user',
        password='test123'
    )
    
    print("Testing invalid designation...")
    
    with pytest.raises(ValidationError) as exc_info:
        author = Author(
            user=user,
            company='Test Corp',
            designation=''  # Empty designation
        )
        author.full_clean()
    
    print(f"✓ ValidationError raised for empty designation")
    print(f"Exception: {str(exc_info.value)}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 3: Location ZIP Code Validation

Test that Location raises ValidationError for invalid ZIP codes.

# tests/test_location_validation.py
import pytest
from django.core.exceptions import ValidationError
from jobpost.models import Location

def test_location_invalid_zip_format_raises_error():
    """Test that invalid ZIP code format raises ValidationError"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Location Invalid ZIP Format Validation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    invalid_zips = [
        ('ABC12', 'alphabetic characters'),
        ('123', 'too short'),
        ('1234567890', 'too long'),
        ('12-34', 'invalid format'),
        ('', 'empty string'),
    ]
    
    print(f"Testing {len(invalid_zips)} invalid ZIP formats:\n")
    
    for invalid_zip, description in invalid_zips:
        print(f"  Testing: '{invalid_zip}' ({description})")
        
        with pytest.raises(ValidationError, match=r".*zip.*") as exc_info:
            location = Location(
                street='123 Test St',
                city='Test City',
                state='CA',
                country='USA',
                zip=invalid_zip
            )
            location.full_clean()
        
        print(f"    ✓ ValidationError raised")
        print(f"    Message: {str(exc_info.value)}")
    
    print(f"\n✓ All invalid ZIP formats rejected")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")


def test_location_invalid_state_code_raises_error():
    """Test that invalid state code raises ValidationError"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Location Invalid State Code Validation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    invalid_states = [
        ('ABC', 'three letters'),
        ('C', 'one letter'),
        ('1A', 'contains number'),
        ('', 'empty'),
    ]
    
    print(f"Testing {len(invalid_states)} invalid state codes:\n")
    
    for invalid_state, description in invalid_states:
        print(f"  Testing: '{invalid_state}' ({description})")
        
        with pytest.raises(ValidationError) as exc_info:
            location = Location(
                street='123 Test St',
                city='Test City',
                state=invalid_state,
                country='USA',
                zip='12345'
            )
            location.full_clean()
        
        print(f"    ✓ ValidationError raised")
    
    print(f"\n✓ All invalid state codes rejected")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")


def test_location_empty_required_fields_raises_error():
    """Test that empty required fields raise ValidationError"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Location Empty Required Fields Validation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    test_cases = [
        {'field': 'city', 'values': {'street': '123 St', 'city': '', 'state': 'CA', 'country': 'USA', 'zip': '12345'}},
        {'field': 'state', 'values': {'street': '123 St', 'city': 'City', 'state': '', 'country': 'USA', 'zip': '12345'}},
        {'field': 'country', 'values': {'street': '123 St', 'city': 'City', 'state': 'CA', 'country': '', 'zip': '12345'}},
    ]
    
    for test_case in test_cases:
        field = test_case['field']
        values = test_case['values']
        
        print(f"Testing empty {field}...")
        
        with pytest.raises(ValidationError) as exc_info:
            location = Location(**values)
            location.full_clean()
        
        assert field in str(exc_info.value).lower()
        print(f"  ✓ ValidationError raised for empty {field}")
        print(f"  Message: {str(exc_info.value)}")
        print()
    
    print(f"✓ All required field validations enforced")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 4: Skills Uniqueness Constraint

Test that Skills raises IntegrityError for duplicate names.

# tests/test_skills_integrity.py
import pytest
from django.db import IntegrityError
from jobpost.models import Skills

def test_skills_duplicate_name_raises_error():
    """Test that duplicate skill names raise IntegrityError"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Skills Duplicate Name IntegrityError")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create first skill
    skill1 = Skills.objects.create(name='Python')
    
    print(f"First skill created:")
    print(f"  ID: {skill1.id}")
    print(f"  Name: {skill1.name}")
    print()
    
    print("Attempting to create duplicate skill...")
    print("Expected: IntegrityError (unique constraint)")
    print()
    
    # Try to create duplicate
    with pytest.raises(IntegrityError, match=r".*unique.*|.*duplicate.*") as exc_info:
        skill2 = Skills.objects.create(name='Python')  # Duplicate name
    
    print(f"✓ IntegrityError raised as expected")
    print(f"Exception type: {exc_info.typename}")
    print(f"Exception message: {str(exc_info.value)}")
    print()
    
    # Verify only one skill exists
    python_skills = Skills.objects.filter(name='Python').count()
    print(f"Skills named 'Python': {python_skills}")
    assert python_skills == 1, "Only one Python skill should exist"
    
    print(f"\n✓ Unique constraint enforced")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")


def test_skills_case_sensitive_duplicates():
    """Test that case-sensitive duplicates are handled"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Skills Case-Sensitive Duplicate Handling")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create skill with specific case
    skill1 = Skills.objects.create(name='JavaScript')
    print(f"Created: {skill1.name}")
    
    # Test different cases
    case_variations = ['javascript', 'JAVASCRIPT', 'Javascript']
    
    print(f"\nTesting {len(case_variations)} case variations:")
    
    for variation in case_variations:
        print(f"\n  Attempting to create: '{variation}'")
        
        try:
            # If unique constraint is case-insensitive, this will raise IntegrityError
            # If case-sensitive, this will succeed (which might be a bug)
            skill = Skills.objects.create(name=variation)
            print(f"    ✓ Created (case-sensitive allowed)")
        except IntegrityError as e:
            print(f"    ✗ IntegrityError (case-insensitive constraint)")
            print(f"    Message: {str(e)}")
    
    total_js_skills = Skills.objects.filter(name__iexact='javascript').count()
    print(f"\nTotal JavaScript-like skills: {total_js_skills}")
    
    if total_js_skills > 1:
        print(f"⚠ Warning: Case-sensitive duplicates allowed (potential bug)")
    
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")


def test_skills_empty_name_raises_error():
    """Test that empty skill name raises ValidationError"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Skills Empty Name Validation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print("Testing empty skill name...")
    
    with pytest.raises(ValidationError, match=r".*name.*") as exc_info:
        skill = Skills(name='')
        skill.full_clean()
    
    print(f"✓ ValidationError raised for empty name")
    print(f"Exception: {str(exc_info.value)}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 5: Complete Exception Testing Integration

Comprehensive exception testing across all models.

# tests/test_complete_exception_handling.py
import pytest
from django.core.exceptions import ValidationError
from django.db import IntegrityError
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

def test_complete_model_exception_handling():
    """Comprehensive exception testing for all models"""
    print(f"\n{'='*80}")
    print("COMPLETE MODEL EXCEPTION HANDLING TEST")
    print(f"{'='*80}\n")
    
    exception_tests = []
    
    # Test 1: Skills duplicate
    print("Test 1: Skills Duplicate Name")
    print("-" * 80)
    Skills.objects.create(name='TestSkill1')
    
    with pytest.raises(IntegrityError) as exc_info:
        Skills.objects.create(name='TestSkill1')
    
    exception_tests.append(('Skills Duplicate', 'IntegrityError', True))
    print(f"✓ IntegrityError raised: {str(exc_info.value)[:50]}...")
    print()
    
    # Test 2: Author duplicate user
    print("Test 2: Author Duplicate User")
    print("-" * 80)
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='test_user', password='test123')
    Author.objects.create(user=user, company='Company A', designation='Role A')
    
    with pytest.raises(IntegrityError) as exc_info:
        Author.objects.create(user=user, company='Company B', designation='Role B')
    
    exception_tests.append(('Author Duplicate User', 'IntegrityError', True))
    print(f"✓ IntegrityError raised: {str(exc_info.value)[:50]}...")
    print()
    
    # Test 3: Location invalid ZIP
    print("Test 3: Location Invalid ZIP")
    print("-" * 80)
    
    with pytest.raises(ValidationError) as exc_info:
        location = Location(
            street='123 St',
            city='City',
            state='CA',
            country='USA',
            zip='INVALID'
        )
        location.full_clean()
    
    exception_tests.append(('Location Invalid ZIP', 'ValidationError', True))
    print(f"✓ ValidationError raised: {str(exc_info.value)[:50]}...")
    print()
    
    # Test 4: JobPost negative salary
    print("Test 4: JobPost Negative Salary")
    print("-" * 80)
    
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='123 St',
        city='City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='12345'
    )
    
    with pytest.raises(ValidationError) as exc_info:
        job = JobPost(
            title='Test Job',
            description='Test',
            expiry=timezone.now().date(),
            salary=-50000,
            type='Full Time',
            location=location,
            author=Author.objects.first()
        )
        job.full_clean()
    
    exception_tests.append(('JobPost Negative Salary', 'ValidationError', True))
    print(f"✓ ValidationError raised: {str(exc_info.value)[:50]}...")
    print()
    
    # Test 5: Multiple exceptions in sequence
    print("Test 5: Multiple Related Exceptions")
    print("-" * 80)
    
    # Empty skill name
    with pytest.raises(ValidationError) as exc_info:
        skill = Skills(name='')
        skill.full_clean()
    print(f"  ✓ Skills ValidationError: {str(exc_info.value)[:40]}...")
    
    # Empty author company
    user2 = User.objects.create_user(username='user2', password='test123')
    with pytest.raises(ValidationError) as exc_info:
        author = Author(user=user2, company='', designation='Role')
        author.full_clean()
    print(f"  ✓ Author ValidationError: {str(exc_info.value)[:40]}...")
    
    # Empty location city
    with pytest.raises(ValidationError) as exc_info:
        location = Location(street='St', city='', state='CA', country='USA', zip='12345')
        location.full_clean()
    print(f"  ✓ Location ValidationError: {str(exc_info.value)[:40]}...")
    
    exception_tests.append(('Multiple Validations', 'ValidationError', True))
    print()
    
    # Summary
    print(f"{'='*80}")
    print("EXCEPTION TESTING SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*80}\n")
    
    print(f"Total exception tests: {len(exception_tests)}")
    passed = sum(1 for _, _, success in exception_tests if success)
    print(f"Passed: {passed}/{len(exception_tests)}")
    print()
    
    print("Test Results:")
    for test_name, exception_type, success in exception_tests:
        status = '✓' if success else '✗'
        print(f"  {status} {test_name}: {exception_type}")
    
    print()
    print(f"✓ All exception handling tests passed")
    print(f"{'='*80}\n")
    
    # Verify database state
    print("Database State After Exception Tests:")
    print(f"  Skills: {Skills.objects.count()}")
    print(f"  Users: {User.objects.count()}")
    print(f"  Authors: {Author.objects.count()}")
    print(f"  Locations: {Location.objects.count()}")
    print(f"  JobPosts: {JobPost.objects.count()}")
    print()
    
    # All assertions
    assert passed == len(exception_tests), "All exception tests should pass"
    print(f"✓ Complete exception handling test successful")
    print(f"{'='*80}\n")

pytest.deprecated_call()

Official Docs: pytest.deprecated_call() Reference

Assert that code triggers a DeprecationWarning or PendingDeprecationWarning.

Full Description

The pytest.deprecated_call() context manager ensures that code triggers deprecation warnings. It's used to test that deprecated features properly warn users before removal. Test passes if DeprecationWarning or PendingDeprecationWarning is raised, fails if no warning occurs. Essential for maintaining backward compatibility while signaling upcoming changes to API consumers.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.deprecated_call() helps test deprecation paths: ensuring old JobPost methods warn users before removal, validating that deprecated Author permission checks trigger warnings, testing that legacy Location geocoding functions warn about new alternatives, verifying Skills matching algorithms marked for deprecation emit proper warnings, and ensuring deprecated QuerySet methods guide users to modern alternatives.

Syntax

# Basic usage
with pytest.deprecated_call():
    deprecated_function()

# As function call
pytest.deprecated_call(deprecated_function, arg1, arg2)

# With lambda
pytest.deprecated_call(lambda: deprecated_function(args))

# Multiple deprecations
with pytest.deprecated_call():
    old_method_1()
    old_method_2()

# Test fails if NO deprecation warning
with pytest.deprecated_call():
    modern_function()  # Fails: no deprecation warning

Parameters Description

  • func (callable, optional): Function to call that should trigger deprecation warning. If provided, subsequent args and kwargs are passed to this function.
  • *args: Positional arguments to pass to func
  • **kwargs: Keyword arguments to pass to func

Return Value

  • Returns: WarningsRecorder when used as context manager
  • Test passes: If DeprecationWarning or PendingDeprecationWarning is triggered
  • Test fails: If no deprecation warning is raised

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: Deprecated JobPost Method

Test that deprecated JobPost method triggers deprecation warning.

# jobpost/models.py (add deprecated method)
import warnings
from django.utils import timezone

class JobPost(models.Model):
    # ... existing fields ...
    
    def get_salary_range(self):
        """
        DEPRECATED: Use get_salary_category() instead.
        This method will be removed in version 3.0.
        """
        warnings.warn(
            "get_salary_range() is deprecated, use get_salary_category() instead",
            DeprecationWarning,
            stacklevel=2
        )
        if self.salary < 50000:
            return "low"
        elif self.salary < 100000:
            return "medium"
        else:
            return "high"
    
    def get_salary_category(self):
        """New method replacing get_salary_range()"""
        if self.salary < 50000:
            return "entry"
        elif self.salary < 100000:
            return "mid"
        elif self.salary < 150000:
            return "senior"
        else:
            return "executive"


# tests/test_jobpost_deprecation.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Author, Location, JobPost, Skills

def test_get_salary_range_deprecated():
    """Test that get_salary_range() triggers deprecation warning"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: JobPost get_salary_range() Deprecation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Setup
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='deprecation_test', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(user=user, company='Test Corp', designation='Recruiter')
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1 Test St',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    skill = Skills.objects.create(name='Python')
    
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Software Engineer',
        description='Test position',
        expiry=timezone.now().date(),
        salary=75000,
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    job.skills.add(skill)
    
    print(f"JobPost created:")
    print(f"  Title: {job.title}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${job.salary:,}")
    print()
    
    print("Testing deprecated method: get_salary_range()")
    print("Expected: DeprecationWarning")
    print()
    
    # Test deprecated method
    with pytest.deprecated_call():
        result = job.get_salary_range()
    
    print(f"✓ DeprecationWarning raised as expected")
    print(f"  Method returned: '{result}'")
    print()
    
    # Test new method (should NOT warn)
    print("Testing new method: get_salary_category()")
    new_result = job.get_salary_category()
    print(f"  No warning (as expected)")
    print(f"  Method returned: '{new_result}'")
    print()
    
    print(f"Migration path:")
    print(f"  Old API: get_salary_range() -> '{result}'")
    print(f"  New API: get_salary_category() -> '{new_result}'")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Deprecation properly tested")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 2: Deprecated Author Permission Check

Test deprecated permission checking method.

# jobpost/models.py (add deprecated method)
class Author(models.Model):
    # ... existing fields ...
    
    def has_permission(self, permission_name):
        """
        DEPRECATED: Use Django's permission system instead.
        This custom permission method will be removed in version 3.0.
        """
        warnings.warn(
            "has_permission() is deprecated, use Django's permission framework instead",
            DeprecationWarning,
            stacklevel=2
        )
        # Legacy permission logic
        return self.user.is_staff


# tests/test_author_deprecation.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author

def test_author_has_permission_deprecated():
    """Test that has_permission() triggers deprecation warning"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Author has_permission() Deprecation")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create author
    user = User.objects.create_user(
        username='perm_test',
        password='test123',
        is_staff=True
    )
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='Test Corp',
        designation='Manager'
    )
    
    print(f"Author created:")
    print(f"  Username: {author.user.username}")
    print(f"  Company: {author.company}")
    print(f"  Is staff: {author.user.is_staff}")
    print()
    
    print("Testing deprecated method: has_permission()")
    print("Expected: DeprecationWarning")
    print()
    
    # Test deprecated permission check
    with pytest.deprecated_call():
        result = author.has_permission('can_post_jobs')
    
    print(f"✓ DeprecationWarning raised")
    print(f"  Permission check result: {result}")
    print()
    
    # Show migration path
    print(f"Migration path:")
    print(f"  Old API: author.has_permission('can_post_jobs')")
    print(f"  New API: author.user.has_perm('jobpost.can_post_jobs')")
    print()
    
    # Test new Django permission system (no warning)
    new_result = author.user.is_staff  # Using Django's built-in
    print(f"New permission system result: {new_result}")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Deprecation warning properly triggered")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

# jobpost/utils.py (add deprecated function)
import warnings

def geocode_location(location):
    """
    DEPRECATED: Use Location.geocode() method instead.
    This standalone function will be removed in version 3.0.
    """
    warnings.warn(
        "geocode_location() function is deprecated, use Location.geocode() method instead",
        DeprecationWarning,
        stacklevel=2
    )
    # Legacy geocoding logic
    return {
        'lat': 37.7749,
        'lon': -122.4194,
        'address': f"{location.city}, {location.state}"
    }


# jobpost/models.py (add new method)
class Location(models.Model):
    # ... existing fields ...
    
    def geocode(self):
        """New geocoding method"""
        return {
            'latitude': 37.7749,
            'longitude': -122.4194,
            'full_address': f"{self.street}, {self.city}, {self.state} {self.zip}, {self.country}"
        }

Example 4: Deprecated Skills Matching Algorithm

Test deprecated Skills matching function.

# jobpost/utils.py (add deprecated function)
def match_skills(skill1, skill2):
    """
    DEPRECATED: Use Skills.calculate_similarity() instead.
    This function will be removed in version 3.0.
    """
    warnings.warn(
        "match_skills() is deprecated, use Skills.calculate_similarity() instead",
        DeprecationWarning,
        stacklevel=2
    )
    # Simple name matching
    return skill1.name.lower() == skill2.name.lower()


# jobpost/models.py (add new method)
class Skills(models.Model):
    # ... existing fields ...
    
    def calculate_similarity(self, other_skill):
        """New similarity calculation method"""
        # More sophisticated matching
        name1 = self.name.lower()
        name2 = other_skill.name.lower()
        
        if name1 == name2:
            return 1.0
        
        # Simple character overlap similarity
        common = len(set(name1) & set(name2))
        total = len(set(name1) | set(name2))
        return common / total if total > 0 else 0.0


# tests/test_skills_deprecation.py

from jobpost.utils import match_skills

Example 5: Multiple Deprecation Warnings in Sequence

Test multiple deprecated methods triggering warnings.

# tests/test_multiple_deprecations.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost
from jobpost.utils import geocode_location, match_skills

def test_multiple_deprecations_in_workflow():
    """Test that multiple deprecated methods trigger warnings in sequence"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Multiple Deprecation Warnings")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Setup
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='multi_dep_test', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(user=user, company='Test Corp', designation='Recruiter')
    
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='100 Test St',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    skill1 = Skills.objects.create(name='Python')
    skill2 = Skills.objects.create(name='Django')
    
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Full Stack Developer',
        description='Test job',
        expiry=timezone.now().date(),
        salary=120000,
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    job.skills.set([skill1, skill2])
    
    print("Setup complete - all models created")
    print()
    
    # Test 1: JobPost deprecated method
    print("Test 1: JobPost.get_salary_range()")
    with pytest.deprecated_call():
        salary_range = job.get_salary_range()
    print(f"  ✓ DeprecationWarning raised")
    print(f"  Result: {salary_range}")
    print()
    
    # Test 2: Author deprecated method
    print("Test 2: Author.has_permission()")
    with pytest.deprecated_call():
        has_perm = author.has_permission('can_post')
    print(f"  ✓ DeprecationWarning raised")
    print(f"  Result: {has_perm}")
    print()
    
    # Test 3: Location deprecated function
    print("Test 3: geocode_location()")
    with pytest.deprecated_call():
        geocode_result = geocode_location(location)
    print(f"  ✓ DeprecationWarning raised")
    print(f"  Result: {geocode_result}")
    print()
    
    # Test 4: Skills deprecated function
    print("Test 4: match_skills()")
    with pytest.deprecated_call():
        match_result = match_skills(skill1, skill2)
    print(f"  ✓ DeprecationWarning raised")
    print(f"  Result: {match_result}")
    print()
    
    # Test all deprecations in single block
    print("Test 5: All deprecations in single context")
    with pytest.deprecated_call():
        job.get_salary_range()
        author.has_permission('can_post')
        geocode_location(location)
        match_skills(skill1, skill2)
    print(f"  ✓ All DeprecationWarnings raised")
    print()
    
    # Summary
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print("DEPRECATION TESTING SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    deprecated_apis = [
        'JobPost.get_salary_range()',
        'Author.has_permission()',
        'geocode_location()',
        'match_skills()',
    ]
    
    new_apis = [
        'JobPost.get_salary_category()',
        'Django permission framework',
        'Location.geocode()',
        'Skills.calculate_similarity()',
    ]
    
    print("Deprecated APIs tested:")
    for i, (old_api, new_api) in enumerate(zip(deprecated_apis, new_apis), 1):
        print(f"  {i}. {old_api}")
        print(f"     → {new_api}")
    
    print()
    print(f"✓ All {len(deprecated_apis)} deprecation warnings properly triggered")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

pytest.register_assert_rewrite()

Official Docs: pytest.register_assert_rewrite() Reference

Register modules to have assertion rewriting enabled before import.

Full Description

The pytest.register_assert_rewrite() function registers module names that should have assertion rewriting applied before they're imported. Pytest's assertion rewriting provides detailed failure messages by introspecting assert statements. When you import helper modules or test utilities that contain assertions, you must register them before importing to get detailed assertion messages.

This function must be called before the module is imported - typically in conftest.py. When you call pytest.register_assert_rewrite('mymodule'), pytest will rewrite all assert statements in mymodule to provide detailed information when they fail. Without registration, assertions in helper modules show minimal failure information.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.register_assert_rewrite() is useful when you have test helpers with assertions: JobPost validation helpers that check salary ranges, Author permission checking utilities with complex assertions, Location validation helpers that verify address formats, Skills matching utilities with assertion-based checks, and shared test utilities that perform multi-model validations.

Syntax

# In conftest.py - register before importing
import pytest
pytest.register_assert_rewrite('test_helpers')
pytest.register_assert_rewrite('jobpost.validators')

# Register multiple modules
pytest.register_assert_rewrite('helpers.jobpost_helpers')
pytest.register_assert_rewrite('helpers.author_helpers')
pytest.register_assert_rewrite('helpers.skills_helpers')

# Now import the registered modules
from test_helpers import validate_jobpost
from jobpost.validators import check_salary

# Assertions in these modules will have detailed output
assert validate_jobpost(job)  # Detailed failure info
assert check_salary(75000)    # Detailed failure info

Parameters Description

  • *names (str): One or more module names to register for assertion rewriting. Use dotted module paths like 'helpers.validators' or 'test_utils'

Return Value

  • Returns: None
  • Effect: Registered modules will have assertion rewriting enabled when imported later
  • Timing: Must be called before the module is imported

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: JobPost Validation Helper with Assertion Rewriting

Register JobPost validation helper for detailed assertion output.

# conftest.py (at project root)
import pytest

# Register test helper modules before they're imported
pytest.register_assert_rewrite('helpers.jobpost_validators')


# helpers/jobpost_validators.py
"""JobPost validation helpers with assertions"""
from django.utils import timezone

def validate_jobpost_salary(job):
    """Validate JobPost salary with assertions"""
    assert job.salary > 0, f"Salary must be positive, got {job.salary}"
    assert job.salary >= 30000, f"Salary below minimum, got {job.salary}"
    assert job.salary <= 500000, f"Salary exceeds maximum, got {job.salary}"
    return True

def validate_jobpost_expiry(job):
    """Validate JobPost expiry date"""
    today = timezone.now().date()
    assert job.expiry >= today, f"Expiry {job.expiry} is in the past (today: {today})"
    
    future_limit = today + timezone.timedelta(days=365)
    assert job.expiry <= future_limit, f"Expiry {job.expiry} exceeds 1 year limit"
    return True

def validate_jobpost_complete(job):
    """Complete JobPost validation"""
    assert job.title, "Title is required"
    assert len(job.title) >= 5, f"Title too short: '{job.title}' (min 5 chars)"
    assert job.description, "Description is required"
    assert job.location, "Location is required"
    assert job.author, "Author is required"
    assert job.skills.exists(), "At least one skill is required"
    
    validate_jobpost_salary(job)
    validate_jobpost_expiry(job)
    return True


# tests/test_jobpost_helpers.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost
from helpers.jobpost_validators import (
    validate_jobpost_salary,
    validate_jobpost_expiry,
    validate_jobpost_complete
)

def test_jobpost_validation_with_rewriting():
    """Test JobPost validation helpers with assertion rewriting"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: JobPost Validation with Assertion Rewriting")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Setup
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='validator_test', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(user=user, company='Test Corp', designation='Recruiter')
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='100 Test St',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    skill = Skills.objects.create(name='Python')
    
    # Valid job
    valid_job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Senior Python Developer',
        description='Great opportunity',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=30),
        salary=120000,
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    valid_job.skills.add(skill)
    
    print("Valid JobPost created:")
    print(f"  Title: {valid_job.title}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${valid_job.salary:,}")
    print(f"  Expiry: {valid_job.expiry}")
    print()
    
    # Test valid job
    print("Testing valid JobPost:")
    result = validate_jobpost_complete(valid_job)
    print(f"  ✓ All validations passed: {result}")
    print()
    
    # Create invalid job (low salary)
    invalid_job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Internship',
        description='Test',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=10),
        salary=15000,  # Below minimum
        type='Part Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    invalid_job.skills.add(skill)
    
    print("Invalid JobPost created (low salary):")
    print(f"  Title: {invalid_job.title}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${invalid_job.salary:,} (below $30,000 minimum)")
    print()
    
    # Test invalid job - assertion will provide detailed output
    print("Testing invalid JobPost:")
    print("Expected: Detailed assertion failure with salary information")
    print()
    
    try:
        validate_jobpost_salary(invalid_job)
    except AssertionError as e:
        print(f"✓ Detailed assertion error caught:")
        print(f"  Message: {e}")
        print(f"  (Thanks to assertion rewriting!)")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Assertion rewriting provides detailed failure information")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 2: Author Permission Helper with Assertion Rewriting

Register Author permission checking helper.

# conftest.py (add to existing)
pytest.register_assert_rewrite('helpers.author_validators')


# helpers/author_validators.py
"""Author validation helpers with assertions"""

def validate_author_can_post(author):
    """Validate author can create job posts"""
    assert author.user.is_active, f"User {author.user.username} is not active"
    assert author.company, f"Author {author.user.username} has no company"
    assert author.designation, f"Author {author.user.username} has no designation"
    
    # Check user status
    assert not author.user.is_superuser or author.user.is_staff, \
        "Superusers must also be staff"
    
    return True

def validate_author_company_info(author):
    """Validate author company information"""
    assert len(author.company) >= 2, \
        f"Company name too short: '{author.company}' (min 2 chars)"
    assert len(author.designation) >= 2, \
        f"Designation too short: '{author.designation}' (min 2 chars)"
    
    # Check valid designation
    valid_designations = ['Recruiter', 'HR Manager', 'CEO', 'CTO', 'Team Lead']
    assert author.designation in valid_designations, \
        f"Invalid designation: '{author.designation}'. Valid: {valid_designations}"
    
    return True


# tests/test_author_helpers.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author
from helpers.author_validators import validate_author_can_post, validate_author_company_info

def test_author_validation_with_rewriting():
    """Test Author validation helpers with assertion rewriting"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Author Validation with Assertion Rewriting")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Valid author
    user1 = User.objects.create_user(
        username='valid_author',
        password='test123',
        is_active=True
    )
    valid_author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user1,
        company='TechCorp Inc',
        designation='Recruiter'
    )
    
    print("Valid Author created:")
    print(f"  Username: {valid_author.user.username}")
    print(f"  Company: {valid_author.company}")
    print(f"  Designation: {valid_author.designation}")
    print()
    
    # Test valid author
    print("Testing valid author:")
    result1 = validate_author_can_post(valid_author)
    result2 = validate_author_company_info(valid_author)
    print(f"  ✓ Can post jobs: {result1}")
    print(f"  ✓ Company info valid: {result2}")
    print()
    
    # Invalid author (inactive user)
    user2 = User.objects.create_user(
        username='inactive_user',
        password='test123',
        is_active=False
    )
    inactive_author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user2,
        company='Test Corp',
        designation='Recruiter'
    )
    
    print("Inactive Author created:")
    print(f"  Username: {inactive_author.user.username}")
    print(f"  Is active: {inactive_author.user.is_active}")
    print()
    
    # Test inactive author
    print("Testing inactive author:")
    try:
        validate_author_can_post(inactive_author)
    except AssertionError as e:
        print(f"✓ Detailed assertion error:")
        print(f"  {e}")
    print()
    
    # Invalid designation
    user3 = User.objects.create_user(username='invalid_designation', password='test123')
    invalid_author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user3,
        company='Test Corp',
        designation='Manager'  # Not in valid list
    )
    
    print("Author with invalid designation:")
    print(f"  Designation: {invalid_author.designation}")
    print()
    
    print("Testing invalid designation:")
    try:
        validate_author_company_info(invalid_author)

        print(f"✓ Detailed assertion error with valid options:")
        print(f"  {e}")

Example 3: Location Validation Helper with Assertion Rewriting

Register Location validation utilities.

# helpers/location_validators.py
"""Location validation helpers with assertions"""
import re

def validate_location_address(location):
    """Validate location address fields"""
    assert location.street, "Street is required"
    assert location.city, "City is required"
    assert location.state, "State is required"
    assert location.country, "Country is required"
    assert location.zip, "ZIP code is required"
    
    assert len(location.street) >= 3, \
        f"Street too short: '{location.street}' (min 3 chars)"
    assert len(location.city) >= 2, \
        f"City too short: '{location.city}' (min 2 chars)"
    
    return True

def validate_location_zip_code(location):
    """Validate ZIP code format"""
    zip_code = location.zip
    
    # US ZIP: 12345 or 12345-6789
    us_pattern = r'^\d{5}(-\d{4})?$'
    assert re.match(us_pattern, zip_code), \
        f"Invalid US ZIP code format: '{zip_code}'. Expected: 12345 or 12345-6789"
    
    return True

def validate_location_state_code(location):
    """Validate US state code"""
    valid_states = ['CA', 'NY', 'TX', 'FL', 'WA', 'IL', 'MA', 'GA', 'OR', 'CO']
    
    assert location.state in valid_states, \
        f"Invalid state code: '{location.state}'. Valid: {', '.join(valid_states)}"
    
    return True

Example 4: Skills Validation Helper with Assertion Rewriting

Register Skills validation utilities.

# conftest.py (add to existing)
pytest.register_assert_rewrite('helpers.skills_validators')


# helpers/skills_validators.py
"""Skills validation helpers with assertions"""

def validate_skill_name(skill):
    """Validate skill name"""
    assert skill.name, "Skill name is required"
    assert len(skill.name) >= 2, \
        f"Skill name too short: '{skill.name}' (min 2 chars)"
    assert len(skill.name) <= 50, \
        f"Skill name too long: '{skill.name}' (max 50 chars)"
    
    # Check for valid characters
    import string
    valid_chars = string.ascii_letters + string.digits + ' +-#'
    invalid_chars = set(skill.name) - set(valid_chars)
    assert not invalid_chars, \
        f"Skill name contains invalid characters: {invalid_chars}"
    
    return True

def validate_skill_uniqueness(skill):
    """Validate skill name uniqueness (case-insensitive)"""
    from jobpost.models import Skills
    
    # Check for duplicates with different case
    similar_skills = Skills.objects.filter(
        name__iexact=skill.name
    ).exclude(pk=skill.pk)
    
    assert not similar_skills.exists(), \
        f"Skill '{skill.name}' already exists (case-insensitive). " \
        f"Found: {[s.name for s in similar_skills]}"
    
    return True

def validate_skills_category(skill_name):
    """Validate skill belongs to known category"""
    categories = {
        'Languages': ['Python', 'JavaScript', 'Java', 'C++', 'Ruby', 'Go'],
        'Frameworks': ['Django', 'React', 'Flask', 'Vue', 'Angular'],
        'Databases': ['PostgreSQL', 'MySQL', 'MongoDB', 'Redis'],
        'Tools': ['Git', 'Docker', 'Kubernetes', 'Jenkins', 'AWS'],
    }
    
    # Check if skill is in any category
    found_in = []
    for category, skills in categories.items():
        if skill_name in skills:
            found_in.append(category)
    
    assert found_in, \
        f"Skill '{skill_name}' not found in any category. " \
        f"Known skills: {[s for skills in categories.values() for s in skills]}"
    
    return found_in[0]

import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

# Import all registered helpers
from helpers.jobpost_validators import validate_jobpost_complete
from helpers.author_validators import validate_author_can_post, validate_author_company_info
from helpers.location_validators import validate_location_address, validate_location_state_code
from helpers.skills_validators import validate_skill_name, validate_skills_category

def test_complete_workflow_with_rewriting():
    """Test complete job posting workflow with assertion rewriting"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Complete Workflow with Assertion Rewriting")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print("Step 1: Create and validate Author")
    user = User.objects.create_user(
        username='workflow_test',
        password='test123',
        is_active=True
    )
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='TechCorp Solutions',
        designation='HR Manager'
    )
    
    try:
        validate_author_can_post(author)
        validate_author_company_info(author)
        print(f"  ✓ Author validated: {author.user.username}")
        print(f"    Company: {author.company}")
        print(f"    Designation: {author.designation}")
    except AssertionError as e:
        print(f"  ✗ Author validation failed: {e}")
        return
    print()
    
    print("Step 2: Create and validate Location")
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='1234 Technology Drive',
        city='San Francisco',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    try:
        validate_location_address(location)
        validate_location_state_code(location)
        print(f"  ✓ Location validated:")
        print(f"    Address: {location.street}, {location.city}")
        print(f"    State: {location.state}, ZIP: {location.zip}")
    except AssertionError as e:
        print(f"  ✗ Location validation failed: {e}")
        return
    print()
    
    print("Step 3: Create and validate Skills")
    skills_data = ['Python', 'Django', 'PostgreSQL']
    validated_skills = []
    
    for skill_name in skills_data:
        skill = Skills.objects.create(name=skill_name)
        try:
            validate_skill_name(skill)
            category = validate_skills_category(skill.name)
            validated_skills.append(skill)
            print(f"  ✓ Skill validated: {skill.name} ({category})")
        except AssertionError as e:
            print(f"  ✗ Skill validation failed for '{skill_name}': {e}")
    print()
    
    print("Step 4: Create and validate JobPost")
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Senior Django Developer',
        description='Exciting opportunity to work with cutting-edge technology',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=45),
        salary=135000,
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    job.skills.set(validated_skills)
    
    try:
        validate_jobpost_complete(job)
        print(f"  ✓ JobPost validated:")
        print(f"    Title: {job.title}")
        print(f"    Salary: ${job.salary:,}")
        print(f"    Expiry: {job.expiry}")
        print(f"    Skills: {', '.join([s.name for s in job.skills.all()])}")
    except AssertionError as e:
        print(f"  ✗ JobPost validation failed: {e}")
        return
    print()
    
    print(f"{'='*70}")
    print("VALIDATION SUMMARY")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    summary = {
        'Author': 'Valid',
        'Location': 'Valid',
        'Skills': f'{len(validated_skills)} skills validated',
        'JobPost': 'Valid',
    }
    
    for component, status in summary.items():
        print(f"  {component}: {status}")
    
    print()
    print("Registered validation helpers used:")
    print("  • helpers.author_validators (assertion rewriting enabled)")
    print("  • helpers.location_validators (assertion rewriting enabled)")
    print("  • helpers.skills_validators (assertion rewriting enabled)")
    print("  • helpers.jobpost_validators (assertion rewriting enabled)")
    print()
    
    print(f"✓ Complete workflow validated with detailed assertion messages")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

pytest.warns()

Official Docs: pytest.warns() Reference

Assert that code triggers a specific warning.

Full Description

The pytest.warns() context manager asserts that code triggers specific warnings (UserWarning, FutureWarning, etc.). It's used to test that code properly warns users about important conditions, deprecated features, or potential issues. Test passes if the expected warning is raised, fails if no warning or wrong warning type occurs. Essential for ensuring your application communicates important information to users through Python's warning system.

Unlike pytest.deprecated_call() which specifically checks for DeprecationWarning/PendingDeprecationWarning, pytest.warns() can check for any warning type and allows matching warning messages with regex patterns. You can also inspect the caught warnings for detailed assertions about warning content, category, and source location.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.warns() helps test warning scenarios: ensuring JobPost salary calculations warn about rounding, validating that Author permission changes trigger security warnings, testing that Location geocoding warns about approximation, verifying Skills matching algorithms warn about ambiguous results, and ensuring database query performance warnings are triggered appropriately.

Syntax

# Basic usage
with pytest.warns(UserWarning):
    warnings.warn("This is a warning", UserWarning)

# With message matching (regex)
with pytest.warns(UserWarning, match=r"salary.*rounded"):
    calculate_salary()

# Capture warning for inspection
with pytest.warns(UserWarning) as warning_info:
    trigger_warning()
    
# Check captured warning
assert len(warning_info) == 1
assert "expected text" in str(warning_info[0].message)

# Function form
pytest.warns(UserWarning, lambda: my_function())

# Multiple warnings
with pytest.warns(UserWarning) as warnings_list:
    warn_multiple_times()
assert len(warnings_list) == 3

Parameters Description

  • expected_warning (Warning class or tuple): The warning class(es) to check for (UserWarning, FutureWarning, RuntimeWarning, etc.). Can be a tuple of warning classes.
  • match (str or Pattern, optional): Regex pattern that the warning message must match. If provided, test fails if warning message doesn't match pattern.
  • func (callable, optional): Function to call that should trigger warning. If provided, subsequent args/kwargs are passed to this function.
  • *args: Positional arguments to pass to func
  • **kwargs: Keyword arguments to pass to func

Return Value

  • Returns: WarningsRecorder context manager that captures warnings as list
  • Each warning: Has attributes: message, category, filename, lineno
  • Test passes: If expected warning is triggered and matches pattern (if provided)
  • Test fails: If no warning, wrong warning type, or message doesn't match pattern

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: JobPost Salary Rounding Warning

Test that JobPost salary calculations warn about rounding.

# jobpost/models.py (add method with warning)
import warnings

class JobPost(models.Model):
    # ... existing fields ...
    
    def calculate_annual_bonus(self, percentage):
        """Calculate annual bonus with rounding warning"""
        bonus = self.salary * (percentage / 100)
        
        # Warn if rounding occurs
        if bonus != int(bonus):
            rounded_bonus = round(bonus, 2)
            warnings.warn(
                f"Bonus amount ${bonus:.4f} rounded to ${rounded_bonus:.2f}",
                UserWarning
            )
            return rounded_bonus
        
        return bonus
    
    def estimate_monthly_salary(self):
        """Estimate monthly salary with approximation warning"""
        monthly = self.salary / 12
        
        if monthly != int(monthly):
            warnings.warn(
                f"Monthly salary ${monthly:.2f} is approximate (annual: ${self.salary:,})",
                UserWarning
            )
        
        return round(monthly, 2)


# tests/test_jobpost_warnings.py
import pytest
import warnings
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

def test_jobpost_salary_rounding_warning():
    """Test that salary calculations trigger appropriate warnings"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: JobPost Salary Rounding Warnings")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Setup
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='salary_warn_test', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(user=user, company='Test Corp', designation='HR')
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='100 Test St',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    skill = Skills.objects.create(name='Python')
    
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Software Engineer',
        description='Test position',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=30),
        salary=75000,
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    job.skills.add(skill)
    
    print(f"JobPost created:")
    print(f"  Title: {job.title}")
    print(f"  Annual Salary: ${job.salary:,}")
    print()
    
    # Test 1: Bonus calculation with rounding
    print("Test 1: Calculate 7.5% bonus (will require rounding)")
    print(f"  7.5% of ${job.salary:,} = ${job.salary * 0.075:.4f}")
    print("  Expected: UserWarning about rounding")
    print()
    
    with pytest.warns(UserWarning, match=r"Bonus amount.*rounded"):
        bonus = job.calculate_annual_bonus(7.5)
    
    print(f"✓ UserWarning raised as expected")
    print(f"  Calculated bonus: ${bonus:.2f}")
    print()
    
    # Test 2: Monthly salary approximation
    print("Test 2: Calculate monthly salary")

Example 2: Author Permission Security Warnings

Test that Author permission changes trigger security warnings.

# jobpost/models.py (add method with security warnings)
class Author(models.Model):
    # ... existing fields ...
    
    def grant_elevated_access(self):
        """Grant elevated access with security warning"""
        if not self.user.is_staff:
            warnings.warn(
                f"Granting elevated access to non-staff user: {self.user.username}",
                UserWarning
            )
        
        self.user.is_staff = True
        self.user.save()
        return True
    
    def update_company(self, new_company):
        """Update company with change warning"""
        old_company = self.company
        
        if old_company != new_company:
            warnings.warn(
                f"Author company changing from '{old_company}' to '{new_company}'. "
                f"This may affect existing job posts.",
                FutureWarning
            )
        
        self.company = new_company
        self.save()
        return True


# tests/test_author_warnings.py
import pytest
import warnings
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author

def test_author_security_warnings():
    """Test that Author permission changes trigger security warnings"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Author Security Warnings")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Create regular user author
    user = User.objects.create_user(
        username='regular_user',
        password='test123',
        is_staff=False
    )
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company='StartupCo',
        designation='Recruiter'
    )
    
    print(f"Author created:")
    print(f"  Username: {author.user.username}")
    print(f"  Is staff: {author.user.is_staff}")
    print(f"  Company: {author.company}")
    print()
    
    # Test 1: Elevate non-staff user
    print("Test 1: Grant elevated access to non-staff user")
    print("  Expected: UserWarning about security risk")
    print()
    
    with pytest.warns(UserWarning, match=r"elevated access.*non-staff"):
        result = author.grant_elevated_access()
    
    author.user.refresh_from_db()
    print(f"✓ UserWarning raised")
    print(f"  User is now staff: {author.user.is_staff}")
    print(f"  Operation result: {result}")
    print()
    
    # Test 2: Change company name
    print("Test 2: Update author company")
    print(f"  Old company: '{author.company}'")
    print(f"  New company: 'MegaCorp Inc'")
    print("  Expected: FutureWarning about impact on job posts")
    print()
    
    with pytest.warns(FutureWarning, match=r"company changing.*may affect"):
        author.update_company('MegaCorp Inc')
    
    author.refresh_from_db()
    print(f"✓ FutureWarning raised")
    print(f"  Company updated to: '{author.company}'")
    print()
    
    # Test 3: Multiple authors with warnings
    print("Test 3: Multiple authors receiving elevated access")
    
    users_data = [
        ('user1', False),
        ('user2', False),
        ('user3', True),  # Already staff
    ]
    
    warned_count = 0
    for username, is_staff in users_data:
        u = User.objects.create_user(username=username, is_staff=is_staff)
        a = Author.objects.create(user=u, company='Test', designation='HR')
        
        print(f"  {username} (staff: {is_staff})", end='')
        
        if not is_staff:
            with pytest.warns(UserWarning):
                a.grant_elevated_access()
            warned_count += 1
            print(" → Warning raised ✓")
        else:
            # Should not warn for already-staff users
            with warnings.catch_warnings(record=True) as w:
                warnings.simplefilter("always")
                a.grant_elevated_access()
                if not w:
                    print(" → No warning (already staff) ✓")
    
    print()
    print(f"✓ {warned_count} warnings raised for non-staff users")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}\n")

Example 3: Location Geocoding Approximation Warnings

Test that Location geocoding warns about approximation.

# jobpost/models.py (add geocoding method)
class Location(models.Model):
    # ... existing fields ...
    
    def geocode_approximate(self):
        """Geocode with approximation warning"""
        # Simplified geocoding
        city_coords = {
            'San Francisco': (37.7749, -122.4194),
            'New York': (40.7128, -74.0060),
            'Chicago': (41.8781, -87.6298),
        }
        
        if self.city in city_coords:
            lat, lon = city_coords[self.city]
            
            warnings.warn(
                f"Geocoding for '{self.street}, {self.city}' is approximate. "
                f"Using city center coordinates: ({lat}, {lon})",
                UserWarning
            )
            
            return {'latitude': lat, 'longitude': lon, 'approximate': True}
        else:
            warnings.warn(
                f"City '{self.city}' not in geocoding database. Using default coordinates.",
                RuntimeWarning
            )
            return {'latitude': 0.0, 'longitude': 0.0, 'approximate': True}
    
    def validate_zip_format(self):
        """Validate ZIP with format warning"""
        import re
        
        if not re.match(r'^\d{5}(-\d{4})?$', self.zip):
            warnings.warn(
                f"ZIP code '{self.zip}' may not be in standard US format (12345 or 12345-6789)",
                UserWarning
            )
            return False
        return True

def test_location_geocoding_warnings():

        country='USA',
        zip='00000'
    )
    
    print(f"Location: {location2.street}, {location2.city}")
    print("Expected: RuntimeWarning about unknown city")
    print()
    
    with pytest.warns(RuntimeWarning, match=r"not in geocoding database"):
        coords = location2.geocode_approximate()
    
    print(f"✓ RuntimeWarning raised")
    print(f"  Default coordinates: ({coords['latitude']}, {coords['longitude']})")
    print()

    print("Test 3: Validate invalid ZIP format")
    location3 = Location.objects.create(
        street='200 Oak Ave',
        city='Chicago',
        state='IL',
        country='USA',
        zip='ABC123'  # Invalid
    )
    
    print(f"ZIP code: '{location3.zip}'")
    print("Expected: UserWarning about format")
    print()
    
    with pytest.warns(UserWarning, match=r"not be in standard US format"):
        is_valid = location3.validate_zip_format()
    
    print(f"✓ UserWarning raised")
    print(f"  ZIP format valid: {is_valid}")

        ('789 Elm St', 'Chicago', 'IL', '60601'),
        ('321 Oak Dr', 'San Francisco', 'CA', '94102'),
    ]

        loc = Location.objects.create(
            street=street,
            city=city,
            state=state,
            country='USA',
            zip=zip_code
        )
        
        with pytest.warns(UserWarning):
            coords = loc.geocode_approximate()
        
        geocoded_results.append({
            'city': city,
            'coords': (coords['latitude'], coords['longitude'])
        })
        print(f"  {city}: ({coords['latitude']}, {coords['longitude']}) ✓")
    
    print()
    print(f"✓ All {len(geocoded_results)} locations geocoded with warnings")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 4: Skills Matching Ambiguous Results Warnings

Test that Skills matching warns about ambiguous results.

# jobpost/utils.py (add skills matching with warnings)
import warnings

def find_similar_skills(skill_name, threshold=0.7):
    """Find similar skills with ambiguity warnings"""
    from jobpost.models import Skills
    
    all_skills = Skills.objects.all()
    similar = []
    
    for skill in all_skills:
        # Simple similarity: character overlap
        set1 = set(skill_name.lower())
        set2 = set(skill.name.lower())
        
        if set1 and set2:
            similarity = len(set1 & set2) / len(set1 | set2)
            
            if similarity >= threshold:
                similar.append((skill.name, similarity))
    
    if len(similar) > 3:
        warnings.warn(
            f"Found {len(similar)} similar skills for '{skill_name}'. "
            f"Results may be ambiguous. Consider refining search.",
            UserWarning
        )
    elif len(similar) == 0:
        warnings.warn(
            f"No similar skills found for '{skill_name}'. "
            f"Consider adding to database or checking spelling.",
            UserWarning
        )
    
    return similar


def match_job_skills(job, candidate_skills):
    """Match job skills with candidate skills, warn on partial matches"""
    required_skills = set(skill.name for skill in job.skills.all())
    candidate_set = set(candidate_skills)
    
    matched = required_skills & candidate_set
    missing = required_skills - candidate_set
    extra = candidate_set - required_skills
    
    match_percentage = (len(matched) / len(required_skills) * 100) if required_skills else 100
    
    if 50 <= match_percentage < 100:
        warnings.warn(
            f"Partial skill match: {match_percentage:.1f}%. "
            f"Matched: {matched}, Missing: {missing}",
            UserWarning
        )
    elif match_percentage < 50:
        warnings.warn(
            f"Low skill match: {match_percentage:.1f}%. "
            f"Candidate may not be suitable for position.",
            RuntimeWarning
        )
    
    return {
        'matched': matched,
        'missing': missing,
        'extra': extra,
        'percentage': match_percentage
    }

Example 5: Database Query Performance Warnings

Test warnings for potentially slow database queries.

# jobpost/utils.py (add performance monitoring)
def search_jobs_with_warning(filters=None):
    """Search jobs with performance warnings"""
    from jobpost.models import JobPost
    
    if filters is None:
        filters = {}
    
    queryset = JobPost.objects.all()
    
    # Warn about potentially slow queries
    if not filters:
        count = queryset.count()
        if count > 100:
            warnings.warn(
                f"Fetching all {count} JobPosts without filters. "
                f"Consider adding filters to improve performance.",
                UserWarning
            )
    
    # Apply filters
    if 'skills' in filters:
        queryset = queryset.filter(skills__name__in=filters['skills'])
        
        if len(filters['skills']) > 5:
            warnings.warn(
                f"Filtering by {len(filters['skills'])} skills may be slow. "
                f"Consider reducing filter criteria.",
                RuntimeWarning
            )
    
    # Warn about missing select_related
    if 'include_author' in filters and filters['include_author']:
        warnings.warn(
            "Including author details without select_related. "
            "Use select_related('author__user') to optimize queries.",
            UserWarning
        )
    
    return queryset


# tests/test_performance_warnings.py
import pytest
import warnings
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost
from jobpost.utils import search_jobs_with_warning

def test_database_performance_warnings():
    """Test warnings for potentially slow database operations"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Database Performance Warnings")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    # Setup: Create multiple jobs
    print("Setup: Creating test data")
    
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='perf_test', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(user=user, company='Test Corp', designation='HR')
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='100 Test St',
        city='Test City',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    # Create skills
    skills = []
    for skill_name in ['Python', 'JavaScript', 'Java', 'Ruby', 'Go', 'Rust', 'C++', 'PHP']:
        skill, _ = Skills.objects.get_or_create(name=skill_name)
        skills.append(skill)
    
    # Create 15 jobs (to trigger "too many" warning)
    jobs_created = []
    for i in range(15):
        job = JobPost.objects.create(
            title=f'Position {i+1}',
            description='Test description',
            expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=30),
            salary=80000 + (i * 5000),
            type='Full Time',
            location=location,
            author=author
        )
        # Assign random skills
        job.skills.set(skills[:((i % 3) + 1)])
        jobs_created.append(job)
    
    print(f"  Created {len(jobs_created)} jobs")
    print(f"  Created {len(skills)} skills")
    print()
    
    # Test 1: Query without filters
    print("Test 1: Query all jobs without filters")
    print(f"  Database has {JobPost.objects.count()} jobs")
    print("  Expected: UserWarning (if count > 100, or mocked)")
    print()
    
    # Note: In real scenario with >100 jobs, would trigger warning
    # For this test, we'll demonstrate the logic
    print("  (In production with >100 jobs, would trigger warning)")
    print()
    
    # Test 2: Query with too many skill filters
    print("Test 2: Query with many skill filters")
    
    many_skills = ['Python', 'JavaScript', 'Java', 'Ruby', 'Go', 'Rust', 'C++', 'PHP']
    print(f"  Filtering by {len(many_skills)} skills")
    print("  Expected: RuntimeWarning about performance")
    print()
    
    with pytest.warns(RuntimeWarning, match=r"may be slow"):
        results = search_jobs_with_warning({'skills': many_skills})
    
    print(f"✓ RuntimeWarning raised")
    print(f"  Query would search across {len(many_skills)} skills")
    print()
    
    # Test 3: Missing optimization warning
    print("Test 3: Query without select_related optimization")
    print("  Expected: UserWarning about missing select_related")
    print()
    
    with pytest.warns(UserWarning, match=r"select_related"):
        results = search_jobs_with_warning({'include_author': True})
    
    print(f"✓ UserWarning raised")
    print(f"  Recommendation: Use select_related('author__user')")
    print()
    
    # Test 4: Multiple warnings in single query
    print("Test 4: Query triggering multiple warnings")
    
    with warnings.catch_warnings(record=True) as w:
        warnings.simplefilter("always")
        
        results = search_jobs_with_warning({
            'skills': ['Python', 'Java', 'Ruby', 'Go', 'Rust', 'C++'],
            'include_author': True
        })
        
        warning_count = len(w)
    
    print(f"✓ {warning_count} warnings raised:")
    print(f"  1. RuntimeWarning: Too many skill filters")
    print(f"  2. UserWarning: Missing select_related")
    print()
    
    # Test 5: Optimized query (no warnings)
    print("Test 5: Well-optimized query")
    
    with warnings.catch_warnings(record=True) as w:
        warnings.simplefilter("always")
        
        # Only filter by 2 skills (under threshold)
        results = search_jobs_with_warning({'skills': ['Python', 'JavaScript']})
        
        warning_count = len(w)
    
    print(f"  Filtering by 2 skills (under threshold)")
    if warning_count == 0:
        print(f"✓ No warnings raised (query is optimized)")
    else:
        print(f"  {warning_count} warnings raised")
    
    print()
    print(f"Performance monitoring summary:")
    print(f"  Total jobs in database: {JobPost.objects.count()}")
    print(f"  Total skills available: {Skills.objects.count()}")
    print(f"  Warnings help identify slow queries before they become problems")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}\n")

pytest.freeze_includes()

Official Docs: pytest.freeze_includes() Reference

Return list of module names used by pytest for freezing into executables.

Full Description

The pytest.freeze_includes() function returns a list of module names that pytest requires to function properly. This is primarily used when creating frozen executables (standalone applications) with tools like PyInstaller, cx_Freeze, or py2exe. These tools need to know which modules to include in the executable bundle, and pytest.freeze_includes() provides that list.

When you freeze a Python application that includes pytest (for example, a testing tool or a development utility), you need to ensure all pytest's dependencies are included. Without this, the frozen executable will fail when trying to run tests. The function returns module paths that should be added to your freezing tool's configuration.

In your anihpj Django project, pytest.freeze_includes() is useful when: creating standalone testing utilities for JobPost validation, building executable test runners for CI/CD systems, packaging Django test suites for distribution to QA teams, creating portable testing tools for Author permission testing, or building custom test executables that need pytest functionality.

Syntax

# Get list of modules needed by pytest
includes = pytest.freeze_includes()

# Use with PyInstaller spec file
# myapp.spec
a = Analysis(
    ['myapp.py'],
    ...
    hiddenimports=pytest.freeze_includes(),
    ...
)

# Use with cx_Freeze setup.py
from cx_Freeze import setup, Executable
import pytest

setup(
    name='mytestapp',
    options={
        'build_exe': {
            'includes': pytest.freeze_includes()
        }
    },
    executables=[Executable('mytestapp.py')]
)

# Print modules for manual inspection
for module in pytest.freeze_includes():
    print(module)

Parameters Description

  • None: This function takes no parameters

Return Value

  • Returns: List of strings, where each string is a module name required by pytest
  • Typical modules: Includes core pytest modules, plugins, and dependencies
  • Usage: Pass this list to your freezing tool's includes/hiddenimports configuration
