Marks

Pytest marks allow you to add metadata to test functions. Marks can be used to selectively run tests, skip tests under certain conditions, parametrize tests with multiple inputs, and control test behavior.

@pytest.mark.filterwarnings

Official Docs: @pytest.mark.filterwarnings Reference

Add warning filter to specific test functions.

Full Description

The @pytest.mark.filterwarnings decorator allows you to add warning filters to individual test functions, similar to Python's warnings.filterwarnings(). This is useful when you want to handle warnings differently for specific tests - ignore certain warnings, convert warnings to errors, or display warnings that are normally hidden. The filter applies only to the decorated test function, not globally.

Warning filters use the format: "action:message:category:module:line". Common actions include 'error' (convert warning to exception), 'ignore' (suppress warning), 'always' (always show warning), 'default' (show first occurrence), 'module' (show first per module), and 'once' (show only once).

In your anihpj Django project, @pytest.mark.filterwarnings is useful for: ignoring deprecation warnings from third-party libraries while testing JobPost creation, converting specific warnings to errors for critical Author permission checks, allowing UserWarnings for Location geocoding approximations, ignoring ResourceWarnings during Skills database operations, and handling Django's RemovedInDjango50Warning for legacy code paths.

Syntax

# Ignore all warnings in test
@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("ignore")
def test_function():
    pass

# Convert specific warning to error
@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("error::UserWarning")
def test_function():
    pass

# Ignore specific deprecation warning
@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("ignore:.*deprecated.*:DeprecationWarning")
def test_function():
    pass

# Multiple filters
@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("ignore::DeprecationWarning")
@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("error::UserWarning")
def test_function():
    pass

# Filter with module specification
@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("ignore:.*:DeprecationWarning:django.*")

Parameters Description

  • filter_string (str): Warning filter specification in format "action:message:category:module:line"
  • action: What to do with matching warnings - error, ignore, always, default, module, once
  • message (optional): Regex pattern to match warning message
  • category (optional): Warning class to match (UserWarning, DeprecationWarning, etc.)
  • module (optional): Regex pattern to match module name
  • line (optional): Line number (rarely used)

Return Value

  • Returns: Mark decorator that applies warning filter to test function
  • Effect: Modifies warning behavior only for the decorated test
  • Scope: Test-function level (does not affect other tests)

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: Ignore Third-Party Deprecation Warnings in JobPost Tests

Test JobPost creation while ignoring external library deprecation warnings.

# tests/test_jobpost_filterwarnings.py
import pytest
import warnings
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("ignore::DeprecationWarning")
def test_jobpost_creation_ignore_deprecations():
    """Test JobPost creation, ignoring all deprecation warnings"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: JobPost Creation (Ignoring Deprecations)")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print("Filter applied: ignore::DeprecationWarning")
    print("Effect: All DeprecationWarnings will be suppressed\n")
    
    # Trigger a deprecation warning (simulated)
    warnings.warn("Old API is deprecated", DeprecationWarning)
    print("✓ DeprecationWarning triggered but ignored by filter")
    print()
    
    # Create test data
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='filtertest1', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(user=user, company='Tech Corp', designation='HR Manager')
    
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='100 Innovation Drive',
        city='San Francisco',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94105'
    )
    
    skill1 = Skills.objects.create(name='Python')
    skill2 = Skills.objects.create(name='Django')
    skill3 = Skills.objects.create(name='PostgreSQL')
    
    print("Test data created:")
    print(f"  User: {user.username}")
    print(f"  Author: {author.company} - {author.designation}")
    print(f"  Location: {location.city}, {location.state}")
    print(f"  Skills: {', '.join([s.name for s in [skill1, skill2, skill3]])}")
    print()
    
    # Create JobPost
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Senior Django Developer',
        description='We are seeking an experienced Django developer...',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=45),
        salary=145000,
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    job.skills.set([skill1, skill2, skill3])
    
    print("JobPost created:")
    print(f"  Title: {job.title}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${job.salary:,}")
    print(f"  Type: {job.type}")
    print(f"  Expiry: {job.expiry}")
    print(f"  Skills: {job.skills.count()}")
    print()
    
    # Validation
    assert job.title == 'Senior Django Developer'
    assert job.salary == 145000
    assert job.skills.count() == 3
    assert job.author.company == 'Tech Corp'
    assert job.location.city == 'San Francisco'
    
    print("Validations:")
    print(f"  ✓ Title correct: {job.title}")
    print(f"  ✓ Salary correct: ${job.salary:,}")
    print(f"  ✓ Skills assigned: {job.skills.count()}")
    print(f"  ✓ Author linked: {job.author.company}")
    print(f"  ✓ Location linked: {job.location.city}")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Test passed with deprecation warnings filtered")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 2: Convert UserWarning to Error for Critical Author Validation

Make UserWarnings fatal for Author permission tests.

# tests/test_author_warning_as_error.py
import pytest
import warnings
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author

def validate_author_strict(author):
    """Strict validation that triggers warnings"""
    if not author.user.is_staff:
        warnings.warn(
            f"Author {author.user.username} is not staff - security risk!",
            UserWarning
        )
    
    if not author.company:
        warnings.warn("Author has no company specified", UserWarning)
    
    return True

@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("error::UserWarning")
def test_author_validation_warnings_as_errors():
    """Test that UserWarnings are converted to errors"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Author Validation (UserWarning → Error)")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print("Filter applied: error::UserWarning")
    print("Effect: UserWarnings will raise exceptions\n")
    
    # Create valid author (staff user with company)
    user1 = User.objects.create_user(
        username='valid_author',
        password='test123',
        is_staff=True
    )
    author1 = Author.objects.create(
        user=user1,
        company='ValidCorp Inc',
        designation='Recruiter'
    )
    
    print("Valid Author created:")
    print(f"  Username: {author1.user.username}")
    print(f"  Is staff: {author1.user.is_staff}")
    print(f"  Company: {author1.company}")
    print()
    
    # Test valid author (should pass without warnings)
    print("Testing valid author...")
    result = validate_author_strict(author1)
    print(f"✓ Validation passed: {result}")
    print("  No warnings triggered\n")
    
    # Create invalid author (non-staff)
    user2 = User.objects.create_user(
        username='invalid_author',
        password='test123',
        is_staff=False  # Not staff!
    )
    author2 = Author.objects.create(
        user=user2,
        company='TestCorp',
        designation='HR'
    )
    
    print("Invalid Author created:")
    print(f"  Username: {author2.user.username}")
    print(f"  Is staff: {author2.user.is_staff} (INVALID!)")
    print(f"  Company: {author2.company}")
    print()
    
    # Test invalid author (should raise error due to warning filter)
    print("Testing invalid author...")
    print("Expected: UserWarning converted to error\n")
    
    try:
        validate_author_strict(author2)
        print("✗ Should have raised error!")
    except UserWarning as e:
        print(f"✓ UserWarning converted to error:")
        print(f"  Error message: {e}")
        print(f"  Filter working correctly!")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Warning filter successfully converts UserWarnings to errors")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 3: Multiple Warning Filters for Location Testing

Apply multiple filters to handle different warning types.

# tests/test_location_multiple_filters.py
import pytest
import warnings
from jobpost.models import Location

def process_location_with_warnings(location):
    """Process location with various warnings"""
    # Deprecation warning
    warnings.warn("Old geocoding API is deprecated", DeprecationWarning)
    
    # User warning for approximation
    if not location.street:
        warnings.warn(f"Location {location.city} has no street address", UserWarning)
    
    # Runtime warning for data quality
    if location.zip == '00000':
        warnings.warn(f"Invalid ZIP code for {location.city}", RuntimeWarning)
    
    return location

@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("ignore::DeprecationWarning")
@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("default::UserWarning")
@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("error::RuntimeWarning")
def test_location_multiple_warning_filters():
    """Test location processing with multiple warning filters"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Location with Multiple Warning Filters")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print("Filters applied:")
    print("  1. ignore::DeprecationWarning - Suppress deprecation warnings")
    print("  2. default::UserWarning - Show UserWarnings normally")
    print("  3. error::RuntimeWarning - Convert RuntimeWarnings to errors")
    print()
    
    # Test 1: Clean location (no warnings)
    print("Test 1: Clean location")
    loc1 = Location.objects.create(
        street='100 Main St',
        city='Portland',
        state='OR',
        country='USA',
        zip='97201'
    )
    
    print(f"  Location: {loc1.street}, {loc1.city}")
    result1 = process_location_with_warnings(loc1)
    print(f"  ✓ Processed successfully")
    print(f"    DeprecationWarning ignored by filter")
    print()
    
    # Test 2: Location with missing street (UserWarning shown)
    print("Test 2: Location with missing street")
    loc2 = Location.objects.create(
        street='',  # Missing
        city='Seattle',
        state='WA',
        country='USA',
        zip='98101'
    )
    
    print(f"  Location: {loc2.city} (no street)")
    print("  Expected: UserWarning displayed (default behavior)")
    with warnings.catch_warnings(record=True) as w:
        warnings.simplefilter("always")
        result2 = process_location_with_warnings(loc2)
        
        user_warnings = [warning for warning in w if issubclass(warning.category, UserWarning)]
        if user_warnings:
            print(f"  ✓ UserWarning shown: {user_warnings[0].message}")
    print()
    
    # Test 3: Location with invalid ZIP (RuntimeWarning → Error)
    print("Test 3: Location with invalid ZIP")
    loc3 = Location.objects.create(
        street='300 Pine Ave',
        city='Denver',
        state='CO',
        country='USA',
        zip='00000'  # Invalid
    )
    
    print(f"  Location: {loc3.street}, {loc3.city}")
    print(f"  ZIP: {loc3.zip} (invalid)")
    print("  Expected: RuntimeWarning converted to error")
    print()
    
    try:
        result3 = process_location_with_warnings(loc3)
        print("  ✗ Should have raised RuntimeWarning as error!")
    except RuntimeWarning as e:
        print(f"  ✓ RuntimeWarning converted to error:")
        print(f"    {e}")
    
    print()
    print("Summary:")
    print("  ✓ DeprecationWarnings ignored")
    print("  ✓ UserWarnings shown normally")
    print("  ✓ RuntimeWarnings converted to errors")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*70}\n")

Example 4: Filter Django-Specific Warnings in Skills Tests

Ignore Django framework warnings while testing Skills model.

# tests/test_skills_django_warnings.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("ignore::django.utils.deprecation.RemovedInDjango50Warning")
@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("ignore:.*django.*:DeprecationWarning")
def test_skills_assignment_ignore_django_warnings():
    """Test Skills assignment ignoring Django deprecation warnings"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Skills Assignment (Ignoring Django Warnings)")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print("Filters applied:")
    print("  • ignore::django.utils.deprecation.RemovedInDjango50Warning")
    print("  • ignore:.*django.*:DeprecationWarning")
    print("Effect: All Django-related warnings suppressed\n")
    
    # Create skills
    skills_data = [
        'Python', 'Django', 'REST APIs', 'PostgreSQL',
        'Redis', 'Docker', 'Kubernetes', 'AWS'
    ]
    
    print(f"Creating {len(skills_data)} skills...")
    skills = []
    for skill_name in skills_data:
        skill = Skills.objects.create(name=skill_name)
        skills.append(skill)
        print(f"  ✓ {skill.name}")
    
    print(f"\nTotal skills created: {len(skills)}")
    print()
    
    # Create job and assign skills
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='django_test', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(user=user, company='Django Shop', designation='CTO')
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='200 Python Lane',
        city='San Francisco',
        state='CA',
        country='USA',
        zip='94102'
    )
    
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Full Stack Django Engineer',
        description='Looking for expert Django developer',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=60),
        salary=165000,
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    
    # Assign all skills
    job.skills.set(skills)
    
    print("JobPost created and skills assigned:")
    print(f"  Title: {job.title}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${job.salary:,}")
    print(f"  Skills count: {job.skills.count()}")
    print()
    
    print("Assigned skills:")
    for i, skill in enumerate(job.skills.all(), 1):
        print(f"  {i}. {skill.name}")
    
    print()
    
    # Validations
    assert job.skills.count() == len(skills_data)
    assert job.skills.filter(name='Django').exists()
    assert job.skills.filter(name='PostgreSQL').exists()
    
    print("Validations:")
    print(f"  ✓ All {len(skills_data)} skills assigned")
    print(f"  ✓ Django skill present: {job.skills.filter(name='Django').exists()}")
    print(f"  ✓ PostgreSQL skill present: {job.skills.filter(name='PostgreSQL').exists()}")
    
    # Query skills by category (simulated)
    backend_skills = job.skills.filter(name__in=['Python', 'Django', 'PostgreSQL', 'Redis'])
    devops_skills = job.skills.filter(name__in=['Docker', 'Kubernetes', 'AWS'])
    
    print()
    print("Skills by category:")
    print(f"  Backend: {', '.join([s.name for s in backend_skills])}")
    print(f"  DevOps: {', '.join([s.name for s in devops_skills])}")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Test completed with Django warnings filtered")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 5: Pattern Matching for Specific Warning Messages

Use regex patterns to filter warnings by message content.

# tests/test_complete_warning_patterns.py
import pytest
import warnings
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

def comprehensive_job_validation(job):
    """Comprehensive validation triggering various warnings"""
    # Salary warnings
    if job.salary < 50000:
        warnings.warn(f"Low salary: ${job.salary:,} may not attract candidates", UserWarning)
    
    if job.salary > 300000:
        warnings.warn(f"High salary: ${job.salary:,} - ensure budget approved", UserWarning)
    
    # Skills warnings
    if job.skills.count() < 2:
        warnings.warn("Too few skills listed - add more requirements", UserWarning)
    
    if job.skills.count() > 10:
        warnings.warn("Too many skills - may discourage applicants", UserWarning)
    
    # Location warnings
    if not job.location.street:
        warnings.warn("Location missing street address", UserWarning)
    
    return True

@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("ignore:.*Low salary.*:UserWarning")
@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("ignore:.*Too few skills.*:UserWarning")
@pytest.mark.filterwarnings("error:.*High salary.*:UserWarning")
def test_job_validation_with_pattern_filters():
    """Test job validation with pattern-based warning filters"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print("TEST: Job Validation with Pattern-Based Filters")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print("Pattern filters applied:")
    print("  1. Ignore: 'Low salary' messages")
    print("  2. Ignore: 'Too few skills' messages")
    print("  3. Error: 'High salary' messages")
    print()
    
    # Setup
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='pattern_test', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(user=user, company='Pattern Corp', designation='HR')
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='400 Filter St',
        city='Austin',
        state='TX',
        country='USA',
        zip='78701'
    )
    
    skill = Skills.objects.create(name='Testing')
    
    # Test 1: Low salary job (warning ignored)
    print("Test 1: Low salary job")
    job1 = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Junior Developer',
        description='Entry level position',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=30),
        salary=45000,  # Low salary
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    job1.skills.set([skill])
    
    print(f"  Salary: ${job1.salary:,} (low)")
    print("  Expected: Low salary warning ignored by pattern filter")
    
    result1 = comprehensive_job_validation(job1)
    print(f"  ✓ Validation passed: {result1}")
    print("    Low salary warning successfully filtered")
    print()
    
    # Test 2: Normal job (no warnings)
    print("Test 2: Normal job")
    skill2 = Skills.objects.create(name='Development')
    skill3 = Skills.objects.create(name='Communication')
    
    job2 = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Mid-Level Developer',
        description='Standard position',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=30),
        salary=95000,  # Normal salary
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    job2.skills.set([skill, skill2, skill3])
    
    print(f"  Salary: ${job2.salary:,} (normal)")
    print(f"  Skills: {job2.skills.count()}")
    
    result2 = comprehensive_job_validation(job2)
    print(f"  ✓ Validation passed: {result2}")
    print("    No warnings triggered")
    print()
    
    # Test 3: High salary job (warning becomes error)
    print("Test 3: High salary job")
    job3 = JobPost.objects.create(
        title='Executive Position',
        description='C-level role',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=60),
        salary=350000,  # High salary
        type='Full Time',
        location=location,
        author=author
    )
    job3.skills.set([skill, skill2, skill3])
    
    print(f"  Salary: ${job3.salary:,} (high)")
    print("  Expected: High salary warning converted to error")
    print()
    
    try:
        result3 = comprehensive_job_validation(job3)
        print("  ✗ Should have raised error for high salary!")
    except UserWarning as e:
        print(f"  ✓ UserWarning converted to error by pattern filter:")
        print(f"    {e}")
    
    print()
    print("Summary:")
    print(f"  Total jobs tested: 3")
    print(f"  Low salary warnings: Ignored by pattern")
    print(f"  Normal salary: No warnings")
    print(f"  High salary warnings: Converted to errors")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Pattern-based filtering working correctly")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Ignore: 'Low salary' messages 2. Ignore: 'Too few skills' messages 3. Error: 'High salary' messages Test 1: Low salary job Salary: $45,000 (low) Expected: Low salary warning ignored by pattern filter ✓ Validation passed: True Low salary warning successfully filtered Test 2: Normal job Salary: $95,000 (normal) Skills: 3 ✓ Validation passed: True No warnings triggered Test 3: High salary job Salary: $350,000 (high) Expected: High salary warning converted to error ✓ UserWarning converted to error by pattern filter: High salary: $350,000 - ensure budget approved Summary: Total jobs tested: 3 Low salary warnings: Ignored by pattern Normal salary: No warnings High salary warnings: Converted to errors ✓ Pattern-based filtering working correctly ====================================================================== PASSED [100%] ========================= 1 passed in 0.61s ==========================
QuerySet Output: JobPost.objects.all() , , ]> JobPost.objects.values('title', 'salary').order_by('salary') # Low salary job (warning filtered) JobPost.objects.filter(salary__lt=50000) ]> # High salary job (warning becomes error) JobPost.objects.filter(salary__gt=300000) ]>

@pytest.mark.parametrize

Official Docs: @pytest.mark.parametrize Reference

Run a test function multiple times with different parameters.

Full Description

The @pytest.mark.parametrize decorator enables you to run the same test function multiple times with different argument values. This is one of pytest's most powerful features, allowing you to test many scenarios without duplicating test code. You specify parameter names and a list of value tuples, and pytest creates separate test cases for each tuple.

Parametrization helps reduce code duplication, makes tests more maintainable, and provides better test coverage. When a parametrized test fails, pytest clearly shows which specific parameter combination caused the failure, making debugging easier. You can parametrize multiple arguments, nest parametrizations, and even mark specific parameter sets with special behaviors (skip, xfail, etc.).

In your anihpj Django project, @pytest.mark.parametrize is invaluable for: testing JobPost creation with various salary ranges, validating Author permissions across different user roles, testing Location with multiple address formats and ZIP codes, validating Skills with different character limits and special characters, and testing JobPost filters across multiple type combinations (Full Time, Part Time, Contract, Remote).

Syntax

# Single parameter
@pytest.mark.parametrize("input", [1, 2, 3])
def test_function(input):
    pass

# Multiple parameters
@pytest.mark.parametrize("input,expected", [
    (1, 2),
    (3, 4),
    (5, 6)
])
def test_function(input, expected):
    pass

# Named parameters for clarity
@pytest.mark.parametrize("salary,expected_level", [
    (50000, "Junior"),
    (100000, "Mid"),
    (150000, "Senior")
])
def test_salary_levels(salary, expected_level):
    pass

# Using pytest.param for special cases
@pytest.mark.parametrize("value", [
    1,
    pytest.param(2, marks=pytest.mark.xfail),
    3
])
def test_with_special_params(value):
    pass

# Nested parametrization
@pytest.mark.parametrize("x", [1, 2])
@pytest.mark.parametrize("y", [3, 4])
def test_nested(x, y):
    # Creates 4 tests: (1,3), (1,4), (2,3), (2,4)
    pass

Parameters Description

  • argnames (str or list): Parameter names as string ("x,y") or list ["x", "y"]
  • argvalues (list): List of parameter values or tuples of values for each test case
  • indirect (bool or list, optional): Use fixtures instead of direct values
  • ids (list or callable, optional): Custom test IDs for better readability
  • scope (str, optional): Scope for parametrization (function, class, module, session)

Return Value

  • Returns: Mark decorator that creates multiple test variants
  • Effect: Pytest generates separate test cases for each parameter combination
  • Test Count: Number of tests = number of parameter value sets
  • Failure Reporting: Each parameter set reported individually if it fails

5 Detailed Django Examples

Example 1: Test JobPost Creation with Multiple Salary Ranges

Parametrize salary values to test different job levels.

# tests/test_jobpost_parametrize_salary.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

@pytest.fixture
def setup_job_data():
    """Setup common test data"""
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='paramtest', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(user=user, company='ParamCorp', designation='HR Manager')
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='500 Test Ave',
        city='Boston',
        state='MA',
        country='USA',
        zip='02101'
    )
    skill = Skills.objects.create(name='Python')
    return {'author': author, 'location': location, 'skill': skill}

@pytest.mark.parametrize("salary,job_level,expected_type", [
    (45000, "Entry", "Full Time"),
    (75000, "Junior", "Full Time"),
    (105000, "Mid-Level", "Full Time"),
    (155000, "Senior", "Full Time"),
    (220000, "Lead/Principal", "Full Time"),
])
def test_jobpost_salary_levels(setup_job_data, salary, job_level, expected_type):
    """Test JobPost creation across different salary ranges"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print(f"TEST: JobPost Salary Level - {job_level}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print(f"Parameters:")
    print(f"  Salary: ${salary:,}")
    print(f"  Job Level: {job_level}")
    print(f"  Expected Type: {expected_type}")
    print()
    
    # Create JobPost with parametrized salary
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title=f'{job_level} Python Developer',
        description=f'Position for {job_level} developer',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=30),
        salary=salary,
        type=expected_type,
        location=setup_job_data['location'],
        author=setup_job_data['author']
    )
    job.skills.add(setup_job_data['skill'])
    
    print("JobPost created:")
    print(f"  Title: {job.title}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${job.salary:,}")
    print(f"  Level: {job_level}")
    print(f"  Type: {job.type}")
    print()
    
    # Validate salary ranges
    if job_level == "Entry":
        assert 30000 <= job.salary < 60000
        print(f"  ✓ Salary in Entry range (30K-60K)")
    elif job_level == "Junior":
        assert 60000 <= job.salary < 90000
        print(f"  ✓ Salary in Junior range (60K-90K)")
    elif job_level == "Mid-Level":
        assert 90000 <= job.salary < 130000
        print(f"  ✓ Salary in Mid-Level range (90K-130K)")
    elif job_level == "Senior":
        assert 130000 <= job.salary < 180000
        print(f"  ✓ Salary in Senior range (130K-180K)")
    elif job_level == "Lead/Principal":
        assert job.salary >= 180000
        print(f"  ✓ Salary in Lead/Principal range (180K+)")
    
    # Standard validations
    assert job.salary == salary
    assert job.type == expected_type
    assert job.skills.count() == 1
    
    print(f"  ✓ Salary matches parameter: ${salary:,}")
    print(f"  ✓ Type matches: {expected_type}")
    print(f"  ✓ Skills assigned: {job.skills.count()}")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Test passed for {job_level} level")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 2: Parametrize Author User Roles and Permissions

Test Author with different user permission levels.

# tests/test_author_parametrize_permissions.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author

@pytest.mark.parametrize("username,is_staff,is_superuser,expected_can_post", [
    ("regular_user", False, False, True),  # Regular users can post
    ("staff_user", True, False, True),     # Staff can post
    ("superuser", True, True, True),       # Superusers can post
    ("inactive_staff", True, False, True), # Inactive staff (still can post structurally)
    ("basic_author", False, False, True),  # Basic author permission
])
def test_author_permissions(username, is_staff, is_superuser, expected_can_post):
    """Test Author creation with various user permission levels"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print(f"TEST: Author Permissions - {username}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print(f"Parameters:")
    print(f"  Username: {username}")
    print(f"  Is Staff: {is_staff}")
    print(f"  Is Superuser: {is_superuser}")
    print(f"  Expected Can Post: {expected_can_post}")
    print()
    
    # Create user with specified permissions
    user = User.objects.create_user(
        username=username,
        password='test123',
        is_staff=is_staff,
        is_superuser=is_superuser
    )
    
    print(f"User created:")
    print(f"  Username: {user.username}")
    print(f"  Is staff: {user.is_staff}")
    print(f"  Is superuser: {user.is_superuser}")
    print(f"  Is active: {user.is_active}")
    print()
    
    # Create Author
    author = Author.objects.create(
        user=user,
        company=f'{username.title()} Company',
        designation='Recruiter'
    )
    
    print(f"Author created:")
    print(f"  Company: {author.company}")
    print(f"  Designation: {author.designation}")
    print()
    
    # Validate permissions
    can_post = expected_can_post  # In real app, this would check actual permissions
    
    print(f"Permission checks:")
    print(f"  Can post jobs: {can_post}")
    
    if user.is_superuser:
        print(f"  ✓ Superuser - Full permissions")
    elif user.is_staff:
        print(f"  ✓ Staff member - Can manage posts")
    else:
        print(f"  ✓ Regular user - Basic posting")
    
    # Validations
    assert author.user.username == username
    assert author.user.is_staff == is_staff
    assert author.user.is_superuser == is_superuser
    assert can_post == expected_can_post
    
    print()
    print(f"Validations:")
    print(f"  ✓ Username correct: {username}")
    print(f"  ✓ Staff status: {is_staff}")
    print(f"  ✓ Superuser status: {is_superuser}")
    print(f"  ✓ Posting permission: {expected_can_post}")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Test passed for {username}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 3: Parametrize Location Address Formats and Validations

Test Location with various address formats and ZIP codes.

# tests/test_location_parametrize_formats.py
import pytest
from jobpost.models import Location

@pytest.mark.parametrize("city,state,zip_code,country,is_valid", [
    ("New York", "NY", "10001", "USA", True),
    ("Los Angeles", "CA", "90001", "USA", True),
    ("Chicago", "IL", "60601", "USA", True),
    ("Houston", "TX", "77001", "USA", True),
    ("Phoenix", "AZ", "85001", "USA", True),
    ("Miami", "FL", "33101", "USA", True),
    ("Seattle", "WA", "98101", "USA", True),
    ("Denver", "CO", "80201", "USA", True),
])
def test_location_address_formats(city, state, zip_code, country, is_valid):
    """Test Location creation with various US city formats"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print(f"TEST: Location - {city}, {state}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print(f"Parameters:")
    print(f"  City: {city}")
    print(f"  State: {state}")
    print(f"  ZIP: {zip_code}")
    print(f"  Country: {country}")
    print(f"  Expected Valid: {is_valid}")
    print()
    
    # Create Location
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street=f'{zip_code[0:2]}00 Main Street',
        city=city,
        state=state,
        country=country,
        zip=zip_code
    )
    
    print(f"Location created:")
    print(f"  Street: {location.street}")
    print(f"  City: {location.city}")
    print(f"  State: {location.state}")
    print(f"  ZIP: {location.zip}")
    print(f"  Country: {location.country}")
    print()
    
    # Validate ZIP code format (5 digits)
    zip_valid = len(zip_code) == 5 and zip_code.isdigit()
    
    print(f"Validations:")
    print(f"  ZIP format: {zip_valid} (5 digits: {zip_code})")
    
    if state in ['CA', 'NY', 'TX', 'FL', 'IL', 'WA', 'AZ', 'CO']:
        print(f"  ✓ State code valid: {state}")
    
    # Assertions
    assert location.city == city
    assert location.state == state
    assert location.zip == zip_code
    assert location.country == country
    assert zip_valid == is_valid
    
    print(f"  ✓ City matches: {city}")
    print(f"  ✓ State matches: {state}")
    print(f"  ✓ ZIP matches: {zip_code}")
    print(f"  ✓ Country matches: {country}")
    print(f"  ✓ Validation status: {is_valid}")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Test passed for {city}, {state}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 4: Parametrize Skills Name Validations

Test Skills model with various name formats and lengths.

# tests/test_skills_parametrize_names.py
import pytest
from jobpost.models import Skills

@pytest.mark.parametrize("skill_name,category,expected_valid", [
    ("Python", "Programming", True),
    ("JavaScript", "Programming", True),
    ("React", "Frontend", True),
    ("Django", "Backend", True),
    ("PostgreSQL", "Database", True),
    ("Docker", "DevOps", True),
    ("AWS", "Cloud", True),
    ("Git", "Version Control", True),
    ("Machine Learning", "AI/ML", True),
    ("RESTful APIs", "Backend", True),
], ids=lambda skill_name: f"skill_{skill_name.replace(' ', '_')}")
def test_skills_name_formats(skill_name, category, expected_valid):
    """Test Skills creation with various name formats"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print(f"TEST: Skill - {skill_name}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print(f"Parameters:")
    print(f"  Skill Name: {skill_name}")
    print(f"  Category: {category}")
    print(f"  Expected Valid: {expected_valid}")
    print()
    
    # Create Skill
    skill = Skills.objects.create(name=skill_name)
    
    print(f"Skill created:")
    print(f"  Name: {skill.name}")
    print(f"  Length: {len(skill.name)} characters")
    print()
    
    # Validate name properties
    name_length_valid = 2 <= len(skill_name) <= 100
    no_special_chars = skill_name.replace(' ', '').replace('/', '').replace('.', '').isalnum()
    
    print(f"Name validations:")
    print(f"  Length (2-100 chars): {name_length_valid}")
    print(f"  Category: {category}")
    
    if '/' in skill_name:
        print(f"  Contains '/' - Acceptable for compound skills")
    if ' ' in skill_name:
        print(f"  Contains space - Multi-word skill name")
    
    # Assertions
    assert skill.name == skill_name
    assert name_length_valid == expected_valid
    assert Skills.objects.filter(name=skill_name).exists()
    
    print()
    print(f"Assertions:")
    print(f"  ✓ Name matches: {skill_name}")
    print(f"  ✓ Length valid: {name_length_valid}")
    print(f"  ✓ Skill exists in database")
    print(f"  ✓ Category: {category}")
    
    # Test uniqueness constraint
    skill_count = Skills.objects.filter(name=skill_name).count()
    print(f"  ✓ Skill count (should be 1): {skill_count}")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Test passed for {skill_name}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")

Example 5: Nested Parametrization for JobPost Type and Salary Combinations

Test all combinations of job types and salary ranges using nested parametrization.

# tests/test_jobpost_nested_parametrize.py
import pytest
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from django.utils import timezone
from jobpost.models import Skills, Author, Location, JobPost

@pytest.fixture(scope="module")
def shared_setup():
    """Shared setup for all parametrized tests"""
    user = User.objects.create_user(username='nested_test', password='test123')
    author = Author.objects.create(user=user, company='NestedCorp', designation='HR')
    location = Location.objects.create(
        street='600 Nested Ave',
        city='Atlanta',
        state='GA',
        country='USA',
        zip='30301'
    )
    skill = Skills.objects.create(name='Testing')
    return {'author': author, 'location': location, 'skill': skill}

@pytest.mark.parametrize("job_type", ["Full Time", "Part Time", "Contract"])
@pytest.mark.parametrize("salary_range", [60000, 90000, 120000])
def test_jobpost_type_salary_combinations(shared_setup, job_type, salary_range):
    """Test all combinations of job types and salaries (3 × 3 = 9 tests)"""
    print(f"\n{'='*70}")
    print(f"TEST: JobPost - {job_type} @ ${salary_range:,}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
    
    print(f"Parameters:")
    print(f"  Job Type: {job_type}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${salary_range:,}")
    print()
    
    # Create JobPost with parametrized type and salary
    job = JobPost.objects.create(
        title=f'{job_type} Developer',
        description=f'{job_type} position with ${salary_range:,} salary',
        expiry=timezone.now().date() + timezone.timedelta(days=30),
        salary=salary_range,
        type=job_type,
        location=shared_setup['location'],
        author=shared_setup['author']
    )
    job.skills.add(shared_setup['skill'])
    
    print(f"JobPost created:")
    print(f"  Title: {job.title}")
    print(f"  Type: {job.type}")
    print(f"  Salary: ${job.salary:,}")
    print()
    
    # Type-specific validations
    print(f"Type-specific checks:")
    if job_type == "Full Time":
        print(f"  ✓ Full Time - Standard benefits expected")
        expected_benefits = True
    elif job_type == "Part Time":
        print(f"  ✓ Part Time - Hourly or reduced benefits")
        expected_benefits = False
    elif job_type == "Contract":
        print(f"  ✓ Contract - Project-based, no benefits")
        expected_benefits = False
    
    # Salary range checks
    print()
    print(f"Salary analysis:")
    if salary_range <= 70000:
        print(f"  • Entry to Junior level")
    elif 70000 < salary_range <= 110000:
        print(f"  • Mid-level position")
    else:
        print(f"  • Senior level position")
    
    # Assertions
    assert job.type == job_type
    assert job.salary == salary_range
    assert job.skills.count() == 1
    
    print()
    print(f"Assertions:")
    print(f"  ✓ Type matches: {job_type}")
    print(f"  ✓ Salary matches: ${salary_range:,}")
    print(f"  ✓ Skills assigned: {job.skills.count()}")
    
    # Combination validation
    print()
    print(f"Combination Analysis:")
    print(f"  {job_type} + ${salary_range:,} = Valid combination")
    
    if job_type == "Part Time" and salary_range > 100000:
        print(f"  Note: High salary for Part Time (unusual but valid)")
    
    print(f"\n✓ Test passed for {job_type} @ ${salary_range:,}")
    print(f"{'='*70}\n")
